EXECUTIVE SUMMARY  
SCALIBUR creates a holistic consortium to cut urban biowaste and replace it with a new production chain of 
biomaterials, forming a partnership of end users to recover and transform biowaste from three municipalities, 
namely Madrid (ES), Albano (IT) and Kozani (EL), into value added products.  
During SCALIBUR a complete study of the quality, logistics and management schemes for municipal solid waste 
(MSW) and urban sewage sludge (USS) will be performed, to integrate innovative sys tems and technologies and 
obtain high-value biobased products.  
In SCALIBUR, HORECA waste will be transformed to proteins, lipids and chitin from insect rearing, while the organic 
fraction of MSW will generate biopesticides and bioplastics by high -solid en zymatic hydrolysis followed by 
fermentation.  The resulting biogas from MSW and USS will be upgraded by bioelectrochemical treatment to 
produce commodity chemicals and bioplastics, such as PHBV.   
By cutting traditional linear waste management, new busines s models are created for the resulting circular value 
chains, applying a sustainable approach to generate new activities and benefits. These new profit sources will be 
created from a baseline analysis of existing waste management data and business models f or each municipality, 
generating social innovation and favouring the adaptation and uptake of new opportunities along the entire urban 
value cycle.  
Continuous tests and development along 
SCALIBUR will create and fine tune new 
business models based on innovative processes, 
and feedback will be obtained from all 
stakeholders, in order to improve the definition, 
performance and integration of value, to 
minimize waste and maximize its benefit.  
With social engagement strategies, key 
communities will participate in all aspects of the 
new value creation, calibrating the returns of 
the project both for the generation of jobs and 
improved urban welfare, such as reducing the 
dependence from outside materials and the 
environmental impacts.

SECTION 1. EXCELLENCE
1.1 OBJECTIVES 
OPPORTUNITIES AND CHALLENGES 
Current European biowaste management is not yet aligned with the circular economy roadmap proposed by the 
European Commission.1 Across the EU, over 100 M tonnes of biowaste are produced every year, with management 
of this waste representing a cost as large as 143 billion euros. Households and HORECA  are the main producers 
(35% and 7.4 % respectively), while a significant amount consists of food waste ( an average of 173 kg per person 
per year). 2 Despite continued efforts to introduce policies to reduce biowaste, these numbers are expected to 
increase in the coming years.3  
Unfortunately, in stark contrast to the successes obtained for other resources (e.g. paper, cardboard, glass, 
plastics), EU recycling policies have proven largely ineffective for biowaste. 4 Currently, more than 75% of biowaste 
is sent for incineration or landfilling, which causes significant environmental damage. Therefore, a great part of this 
biowaste is not being valorised, which irreversibly extracts valuable resources from the economic cycle. 
Considering these numbers, an effective waste management chain and innovative recycling strategies are required.  
With the clear objective of reducing the environmental damage, the  proposal COM (2015) 594 for a Directive 
amending the existing EU Landfill Directive requires member states to progressively reduce landfilling of municipal 
biodegradable waste to 10% by 2030.5 In fact, as much as 40% of biowaste in the EU is still landfilled (up to 100% in 
some member states), 6 resulting in major environmental hazards through the associated emission of greenhouse 
gases (GHG) and pollution of soil and groundwater.  
Besides reducing waste generation and increasing recycling of existing waste, changes in the whole biowaste chain 
are required to reach EU goals. Whilst a reintroduction of biowaste in the production value chain allows a return of 
resource value of waste into the economy (closing the loop), new business opportunities and economic growth are 
foreseen.7,8 Adopting policies where waste from industrialised counties is used as a resource across the EU could 
save €1.4bn a year and generate €1.6bn in sales. 9 Thus, with the right policies, the circular economy may help 
reduce waste, increase recycling, and give new use to biowaste through its transformation into profitable products.  
Finding feasible and economically viable procedures to convert  urban biowaste into valuable biobased products is 
in fact a challenge. Currently, market policies for bioproducts derived from waste are limited, which in turn leads to 
low valorisation rates of bio -waste.2 In order to optimize and reach the full potential of the biobased products 
derived from waste, action across the whole value chain is required.  
GLOBAL OBJECTIVES OF SCALIBUR 
SCALIBUR aims at closing the gap between technological feasibility and industrial applications in the field of urban 
biowaste valorisation by enhancing strategic cooperation between sectors. SCALIBUR contributes to two European 
challenges - to reduce landfil ling and the creation of a bio based Economy in 2030 -  through the creation of a 
holistic consortium that handles the recovery of urban biowaste from citizens through several municipalities, the 
production chain of biobased products by innovative technologies, and equally important, direct collaboration with 
the future end-users.  
SCALIBUR’s main objectives are:  
 To engage all relevant stakeholders in the urban biowaste value chain in line with RRI principles.10 SCALIBUR will 
start at the household level directly involving citizens and public authorities in the recovery of biowaste at their 
city ( pilot municipalities : Madrid (ES), Albano ( LAZIO, IT) and Kozani ( CLUBE, EL)). Together with innovative

SCALIBUR aims at: increasing the understanding of citizens, changing behaviour regarding collection and biowaste 
usage, increasing acceptance of urban- biowaste products, and reducing the amount of mixed and non- valorised 
biowaste. As a long-term goal, SCALIBUR aims at improving current policies and logistics in the waste management 
chain, and supporting new profitable business models and social innovation initiatives (WPs 2&10).  
 To demonstrate innovative value chains converting  three urban-biowaste streams, namely organic fraction of 
municipal solid waste (OFMSW), HORECA and retail organic waste (ROW), and urban sewage sludge (USS) from 
wastewater treatment plants (UWWTP)  into high-value industrial bio based products  with enhance d 
sustainability profiles and new functionalities by a vast number of innovative technological processes (WPs 4 -
6). Among these valorisation  processes, biobased plastics (WPs 4& 6), biopesticides (WPs 4& 6), commodity 
chemicals (WP4 &6), and a sustainable and resilient sour ce of proteins, lipids, and chitin (WP5) will be 
produced.  
 To assess the sustainability of all technological processes included in SCALIBUR, by analyzing their performance 
at the techno-economical, environmental, and social level. Environmental impacts will be analyzed through Life 
Cycle Assessment (LCA) . Environmental management tools su ch as Environmental and Social Impact 
Assessment (ESIA) and Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, and T hreats (SWOT) analysis will be also 
included (WP8). The potential social benefits ( e.g. creation of jobs, policy changes and recommendations) will 
be assessed with a  social life cycle assessment (S LCA). In addition, all the technological developments will be 
analysed under and engineering -oriented approach for the techno -economic assessment of the developed 
processes.   
 To ensure the safety of the new biobased products and provide recommendations for the regulatory framework 
to biowaste which will be assessed by in-depth safety and risk analysis and a regulatory assessment during the 
progress of the project (WP8). 
 To influence current and new policies and logistics in the waste management chain that allow the introduction of 
new supply changes for food and feed,  by involving all relevant stakeholders  (citizens (represented by the 
Urban B iowasteclubs), academia, industry and government (represented by the pilot municipalities and 
regions)) in the waste value chain and by accumulating evidence-based know-how (WPs 2, 3 & 7). 
 To identify effective business and social innovations considering the information obtained from the stakeholders 
(WP2) and implemented in a practical way to support the integration of the new value chains for the bio based 
products generated in ea ch municipality where the pilots are taking  place. Further replication of SCALIBUR 
results in numerous municipalities shall be encouraged (see letters of support, Annex).

1.2 RELATION TO WORK PROGRAMME 
The SCALIBUR project addresses the topic CE-SFS-25-2018: Integrated system innovation in valorising urban 
biowaste, part of the focus area “ Connecting economic and environmental gains - the Circular Economy (CE)”. This 
section shows how SCALIBUR addresses each of the issues indicated in the specific challenge and scope indicated in 
the call text. 
SPECIFIC CHALLENGE 
Most of the biowaste produced in cities (such as garden and park waste, food and kitchen waste fr om households, 
restaurants, caterers and retail premises), as well as sewage sludge from urban wastewater treatment plants are 
processed without fully exploiting , in a smart and innovative cascading fashion , its potential as feedstock for 
valuable and precious compounds. 
The SCALIBUR consortium is built to fit the challenges, aiming at using innovative social and industrial technologies 
to produce high -value bio based products ( proteins, lipids, chemical commodities,  bioplastics and  biopesticides) 
from biowaste (OFMSW, HORECA, ROW, and USS from WWTP ). This pr oject will have a direct impact by reducing  
health threats and burden on the environment. Significant economic benefits are also envisioned from SCALIBUR, 
e.g. creation of new profitable businesses, biowaste valorisation and production of high-value products. 
Besides the technological challenges, there will be a need for public authorities to adopt new policies; changing 
citizens' behaviour will require social innovation initiatives, and new, profitable bu siness models along the entire 
urban biowaste value chain will have to be developed.  
A consortium of R&D organizations, academia, waste management companies and municipalities are taking the 
initiative to develop new strategies to contribute to wards attai ning a circular biobased economy scheme with 
urban waste. With SCALIBUR ’s strategies, public authorities will have the facts and the support to implement 
changes in the current policies. Outcomes from the project will be also used to modify citizen attitud es towards 
biowaste as a raw material source for new products, ensuring a good quality supply of biowaste. Such changes will 
be promoted by the participating municipalities. At the same time , waste management companies will seek the 
optimum conditions and supply of biowaste to run the above -mentioned processes for the management of 
biowaste both at OFMSW  and USS from UWWTP . Pilot studies will be performed in 3 municipalities in three 
different countries from southern Europe (Spain, Italy, and Greece), while a Swedish municipality will act as a best-
performing territory (BPT) as example of a high-performance on biowaste collection from households. 
SCOPE 
Proposals shall focus on an integrated system i nnovation approach in urban biowaste recycling and valorisation for 
the production of high-value biobased products, including proteins for food and feed. 
MSW, HORECA, ROW  and USS from WWTP  will be used as starting mater ials to produce high -value bio based 
products. New technologies from several partners are combined  together to p roduce a portfolio of bio based 
products (proteins, lipids, chemical commodities, bioplastics and biopesticides) from these waste streams. 
Proposals shall ensure the full integr ation of the upgraded urban bio waste value chain into the existing  local 
waste/wastewater management schemes. 
The SCALIBUR project will involve the recovery and treatment of 3 different waste sources with 3  different 
municipalities for OFMSW,  HORECA, ROW  (Madrid (ES), Albano  (IT), Lazio, (IT) and Kozani ( CLUBE, EL)), in 
cooperation with UWWTP treating the USS  from Ostrava (SMVAK, CZ) and Braban province (WBD, NL). Collection, 
transport, logistics, sorting and pre -treatment (through stabilization and homogenization) of biowaste  will be

Life Cycle Assessment (LCA) of the entire urban biowaste valu e chain; improving logistic models taking into account 
behaviour change and participation of citizens and local communities in relation to the collection and use of this 
particular feedstock; increasing consumer awareness and acceptance of urban biowaste -derived products; 
adapting/developing business models for successful market uptake; food and feed safety aspects; regulatory 
aspects; and facilitating the exchange of good practices and experiences between all stakeholders. 
Under the supervision of ITENE (c oordinator of SCALIBUR), a LCA will be performed (WP8) aiming at recovering 
biowaste and producing new products (closing the loop) through five different technologies (WPs 3-6). This LCA will 
yield science -based support for more efficient and environmental ly sustainable waste management through 
biowaste valorisation  and will identify the preferable processing options of the biowaste . LCA and SLCA will be 
applied to also tailor SCALIBUR end -products to the needs of society ( environmental and social aspects) and 
promote SCALIBUR strategies. In addition, cost-benefit analysis, social LCA, and input and output analysis are useful 
tools to obtain relevant information to ensure the success of the project. Social acceptance of high -value biobased 
products produced  in this project will be performed by the engagement activities described in WP2, namely, 
interactive workshops, “see-touch-taste” events, walking tours, etc.  
Optimized logistic models with metaheuristic algorithms for  the transport of both OFMSW,  HORECA and ROW will 
be generated during SCALIBUR development, which will be completed with consumer research, socio -economic 
research, business model development and the circular economy. 
Food and feed safety and regu latory aspects of the final bio based products intended for human and animal 
consumption will be performed by Nutrition Science, experts on safety assessment. In addition, regulatory aspects 
will be assessed by the legal unit in UNIMORE (WP8). 
Consumer awareness of good practices will be tackle d from the start of SCALIBUR through engagement activities 
and continuous monitoring of citizen’s waste management (WP2).  Moreover, SCALIBUR’s pilot municipalities, BPT 
and following municipalities will exchange best practices on waste management during this project.  
New business and organisational models on cities ensuring the full integr ation of the upgraded urban bio waste 
value chain into the existing local waste/wastewater management schemes; 
SCALIBUR strategy consists of building a business model for each mun icipality involved in the pilots. Such models 
will be co-created with previously engaged citizens, waste generators, the municipalities, the waste managers and 
other relevant stakeholders. A stakeholder platform will be generated (WP7) to integrate the new  business models 
based on cooperation and transparency. Indeed, through this platform the results of SCALIBUR will be available for 
waste generators, which are the main providers of waste fractions, capable of taking action to improve waste 
fractions. The next step consists of innovative treatment processes (WP s4-6), which will greatly benefit from 
optimization of waste recovery. The result of these strategies will be implemented to improve waste management 
policies in each municipality. SCALIBUR can encour age new waste management through the economic value of 
waste-derived products potentiating biowaste collection or enhancing financial sustainability of the overall waste 
system. These new business and organizational models will be validated following munic ipality group  to ensure 
replication in EU countries with emphasis on eastern EU countries (see letters of support). 
Improved perception of citizens on urban biowaste as a local resource and their enhanced active participation in its 
separate collection thr ough social innovation initiatives; and improved c onsumer acceptance of urban bio waste-
derived products, including food and feed ingredients;

SCALIBUR will engage citizens from the beginning of the project with the creation of Urban Biowaste Clubs and  a 
stakeholder platform (WPs2& 7). Following this strategy, citizens will be able to check the results of their actions, 
contributing directly to the production of high -value products from urban biowaste.  These clubs will also increase 
consumer acceptance and participation, together with dissemination activities done by G!E (WP9). 
A more sustainable and resilient protein supply chain; 
There is an urgent need to increase protein supply from sustainable sources for feed and food. At the moment they 
represent an imp ortant share of imports. 11 To face this urgen t issue , the European Parliament has adopted a 
resolution to foster actions to replace imported protein crops with alternative European sources. 12 SCALIBUR’s 
approach using insects rear ed on bio-waste are a possib le contribution to these efforts . With an innovative and 
sustainable approach described in WP5, using insects fed with HORECA  and ROW, proteins will be obtained to be 
further used in the production chain of food and feed applications and potentially also i n the production of 
bioplastics. This approach has been identified as an economic, efficient, competitive and low -impact system to 
exploit these organic masses making their disposal profitable and with a lesser impact on the environment, fitting 
within The Protein Challenge 2040 to shift the production of protein onto a more sustainable path. 
Safety assessment of biobased processes and products from urban bio-waste; 
Safety assessment of the end products is essential to ensure their use by humans and animals. Safety of bio based 
products generated by in WP s4-6 will be performed by Nutrition Science, who are experts in in-vitro analysis with 
tailored Standard-operating Protocols (SOP). 
Reduced amount of urban bio -waste that would otherwise be incinerated or landfilled, and hence reduced 
environmental impact (including emissions of GHG and of air pollutants and their precursors) of municipal and foo d 
waste; 
The outcome of SCALIBUR should highlight the best use of urban biowaste in moving towards a zero-waste circular 
economy at local level, by reducing resources depletion, and in promoting economic growth.  Based on the waste 
hierarchy, it will promote valorisation actions and shift current landfilling and incineration practises.  The biowaste 
value chain has great social, environmental and economic opportunities and SCALIBUR aims to turn biowaste into a 
profitable renewable material for valuable bio based products from which society can greatly benefit.  Preliminary 
numbers show that a great increase of biowaste collection and an improved organic fraction in the collected 
biowaste will be achieved with SCALIBUR actions (see Table 1.1a). 
Detailed assessments of specific technical, regulatory, financial, market and logistical barriers hampering the full 
exploitation of the urban biowaste value chain; 
Both feasibility assessment and an analysis of the barriers that can potentially hamper this project will be 
performed at the start of the project  (WP10). During this project, the stakeholder platform (WP7) will serve as a 
feedback loop to all WPs, ensuring best exploitation of the value chain. 
Evidence-based support for EU policies/targets in the biobased and ci rcular economy, climate mitigation, 
sustainable growth and re-industrialisation. 
SCALIBUR is aligned with  EU policies on the waste management hierarchy focusing o n the efficient recovery of 
biowaste and its reus e. The goals of this project  deal with b iowaste in the most resource- efficient and 
environmentally way, which is also in line with the EU Waste Framework Directive (2008/98/EC) . Using disruptive 
and feasible technological solutions SCAL IBUR will valorise 3 different biowaste sources  (OFMSW, HORECA, ROW 
and USS) into profitable products, promoting biowaste usage. Safety assessment of the products will be done to 
ensure that they meet end-market requirements in line with EU legislation.
1.3 CONCEPT AND METHODOLOGY 
1.3.1 CONCEPT 
The SCALIBUR consortium has been designed to effectively implement all RRI tools and co -creation with 
stakeholders and society, combining  all inputs from the participants  and creating a platform that brings together 
citizens, municipalities, waste management companies, industries, policy makers, and other relevant stakeholders. 
Through close feedback between individual WPs, SCALIBUR aims to create a synergistic series of innovative 
strategies that will enable improvements across the urban biowaste value chain.

Figure 2. SCALIBUR concept 
SCALIBUR presents an innovative concept to valorise  3 important biowaste streams: OFMSW, and retail biowaste, 
and USS from WWTP. In this project, high-value products such as proteins, lipids , chemical commodities,  
bioplastics, and biopesticides  with boosted  sustainability profiles and new functionalities will be produced using 
three innovative technological lines (WPs 4-6).  
SCALIBUR’s goal of producing high-value biobased products will be tested and validated in 3  municipalities (Madrid 
(ES), Albano (LAZIO, IT) and Kozani (CLUBE, EL)) and 2 UWWTP (CZ and NL) . These operational environments are 
highly relevant, allowing for the channelling of feedback into the production chain to reach optimal results. Indeed, 
all work packages in this project are feeding each other: e.g. from stakeholder and citizen engagement designed in 
WP2 to improve waste management, recycling and social engagement, SCALIBUR will obta in OFMSW fractions 
that, in turn, will improve the results of the valorisation  of this waste stream (WP4). Moreover, WP3 will include 
innovative selection strategies to optimize biowaste  in plant, engaging citizens and supplying best quality starting 
materials to the indus tries where valorisation  is performed. In addition, an online stakeholder platform (WP7) is 
expected to engage all actors involved (quadruple helix stakeholders) in the value chain and provide them with the 
knowledge to contribute using best practices in w aste management. Moreover, local authorities will also be 
involved in this platform to improve current policies on biowaste disposal, collection and treatment, and to test the 
full integration of the valorized urban-biowaste value chains.  
Life cycle and safety assessment (WP8) will give information about the sustainability approaches followed in WPs4-
6 for the selected waste streams, which allows optimization of these technological procedures along the duration 
of SCALIBUR project. Safety and regulatory aspects are also considered (WP8). 
In addition, following a circular economy approach, business and social innovation models will be identifie d to 
support the integration of  the resulting value chains  on a city level . To create these models, a benchmark analysis 
will be performed regarding the current situation on existing urban-waste management data, social innovation and 
business models for each municipality participating in the pilots (WP2). Updating and adapting these models along 
the entire urban biowaste value chain during SCALIBUR progress is also planned. Indeed, continuous tests of these 
approaches will be performed along all valorisation approaches, obtaining beneficial feedback to define them 
better and to improve their performance and integration in urban-biowaste value chains.  
With the results of SCALIBUR, implementation across Europe is intended. A large network of municipalities has 
already shown interest on the implementation of the work done in this project (see letters of support). 
TRL and project positioning  
SCALIBUR aims to integrate , at a European leve l, available technologies for the valorisation  of biowaste into 
biobased products. The process configuration can be considered to have a TRL between 5 and 6. According to the 
timeline projected for SCALIBUR, progress up to 7 is estimated within the project (see Table 1.3a for initial TRL).

SCALIBUR versus other R&I activities  
The SCALIBUR Project  has been designed to complement  the activities developed by other on -going projects 
funded under H2020 and BBI JU initiatives (Table 1.3.c). In some of them, partners are involved (such as URBIOFIN, 
with Exergy and VISUM), while some other partners are already working in collaboration  with other projects (such 
as EMBRACED, where VISUM is also creating synergies with the BBI POLYBIOSKIN project coordinated by IRIS).

1.3.2 METHODOLOGY 
SCALIBUR is aiming to improve the reuse of urban biowaste and fully exploit its value  producing a vast number of 
biobased products. In the following section a brief description of the overall methodology together with the 
activities and approaches during SCALIBUR project is described. All WPs are described in detail in section 3.1. In the 
following paragraphs SCALIBUR approaches are briefly introduced: 
Social innovation, Stakeholder Engagement, Co-Creation and Sustainable Business Models (WP 2,3,7,9) 
Social innovations take manifold approaches and present a wide array of success stories. In the environmental 
sector, social innovation is expected to have an even stronger role in enabling positive changes in behaviour in the 
future. Often social innovations have an explicitly local role.
13 The projects H2020 FUSIONS and REFRESH 
investigated how social innovations can help (as one activity among others) to prevent food waste. 14 SCALIBUR will 
build on these and other findi ngs and inventories 15 of promising practices to identify initiatives that -  uptaken, 
adapted, modified or scaled up -  help to achieve the full integration of the valorised urban biowaste technologies 
on a city level.  
In relation to stakeholder involvement in waste management, emphasis will be on the contribution of citizen s in 
the chosen municipalities. Already in 1996, in a study about landfill procedures ( Swiss case stud y) it was argued 
that “the public is in  principle capable and wise in making prudent decisions…[their] input is essential to make the 
right decision, and not only strategically necessary to gain acceptance.” The strong dependence on consumer 
choice entails increased awareness of (un)sustainable behaviour and puts emphasis on citizens’ involvement more 
generally. 
The SCALIBUR project aims to involve citizens  whenever possible. Citizen contribution to SCALIBUR strategy 
requires direct action with citizens, not only in correct organic waste separation and recycling,  but also in decision-
making. Frequent interaction of citizens should be stressed as a key factor  when dealing with bio waste. 
Interestingly, separate collection of bio waste has also shown to lead to  higher capture rates and higher quality of 
fractions of waste.16 Indeed, a case study in the city of Milan highlights that separate collection is possible in cities 
through intensive communication and education campaigns. 10 It is possible to convince house holds to separate

their waste as long as they are provided with the right knowledge and tools. SCALIBUR aims at giving the citizens 
these tools and autonomy to act, helping households with their waste management to, in turn, improve t he 
recovery of high quality biowaste. The specific tools provided by SCALIBUR are described in WP7.  
Citizens shall be empowered so that they can take full ownership of their own tasks in waste management. To 
ensure wide participation, engaging activities such as Biowasteclubs, interactive citizen workshops and “feel-touch, 
taste experiences” are key components of the project  (WP2). Biowasteclubs are based on trust, respect, and 
transparency and will give a voice to key stakeholders, including citizens.  
Improving urban waste collection, characterization and homogenization (WP3) 
Implementation of best practices from BPT (Lund (SE)) in both social and technical aspects will be performed in the 
participating pilot territories, while following territories will implement the processe s for future replicability . The 
aim is to improve the quality and quantity of urban biowaste  selectively collected to fully exploit its potential in 
valorisation processes. Characterization of all waste streams in SCALIBUR will be done, together with pre -
treatment, before their conversion into high-value products (WP3). 
Valorisation of different biowaste streams (WPs 4-5-6) 
The production of bio based products from biowaste from 3 different municipalities based on the valorisation  of 
MSW, HORECA, ROW and USS will be performed  in 7 demo dites (DS) s by 2 research organisations (CENER, and 
WETSUS), 3 large industrial partners (FCC, SMVAK and NOVAMONT), 3 SMEs (Aeris Technologies, KOUR and ASA), 1 
water authority (WBD) and 1 university (UNIMORE), working in close  collaboration among them, to m aximize the 
production of high-value products by three different technological lines. Validation of the technological processes 
and the characterization of the products will also be performed by several partners (NS and Zetadec), to ensure the 
quality and the safety of the final products. Assessment of the potential environmental impacts will be done  by 
ITENE and CENER (WP8). 
All 3 lines of valorisation  are described in detail in section 1.4 and section 3.1 . In the following p aragraphs all 3 
technological approaches are briefly introduced: 
 Valorisation of (OFMSW) into commodity chemicals, bioplastics and biopesticides (WP4) 
Previous to being valorised, the OFMSW needs to be stabilized and homogenized (WP3). This pre- treatment of the 
OFMSW will be perform ed in demo site DS  1 (Las Dehesas, ES). OFMSW will then be  valorised using innovative 
enzymatic hydrolysis and submerged and solid-state fermentation (SSF) processes in demo site DS  2 (CENER, ES) 
and 3 (AERIS, ES), respectively . Through careful characterization of the OFMSW composition and optimal enzyme 
selection, this work package aims at producing first a hydrolysate leading to two different fractions:  
1. A liquid fraction subsequently treated by submerged fermentation to produce diols for the synthesis of bio - 
based polyesters for packaging uses (DS 4, NOVAMONT, IT) and biopesticides (DS 2, CENER, ES).  
2. A solid fraction used in  solid-state fermentation to produce biopesticides by SSF (DS 3, AERIS, ES), as well as 
for the mixing with sewage sludge to be subsequently used in WP6.  
Currently more than half of the biogas produced in the MSW management and biomethanation plant “Las 
Dehesas” (DS 1) is misused and flared in a torch. An innovative solution will be validated to convert  CO
2 contained 
in this off -gas (35% in DS  1) in to different high -value products  (chemical commodities). About 830 kg of these 
compounds can be potentially produced per hour in this type of MSW management facilities, leading to 12,264 Ton 
of CO
2 per year that can be captured by implementing the SCALIBUR process at full-scale in DS 1. 
 Valorisation of HORECA and ROW biowaste into proteins, lipids and chitin (WP5) 
HORECA and ROW is full of raw materials to feed insects like Black Soldier Fly  (BSF) Hermetia illucens (Diptera, 
Stratiomyidae), who  can efficiently convert kitchen , restaurant and caterer scraps  or organic materials in to a 
biomass rich in proteins, lipids and chitin. SCALIBUR is following a sustainable and resilient approach to shifting the 
production of protein onto a more sustainable path. In addition, this project  exploits all products formed during 
insect rearing, isolating all proteins, lipids and chitin.  This valorisation process will be done in  demo site  DS 5 
(Unimore and KOUR, IT). Chitin is an imp ortant natural polymer used in a vast number of applications including 
medicine and cosmetics. 17 The main sources of chitin are marine crustaceans (e.g. shrimp and crabs). SCALIBUR ’s 
approach to obtain chitin from BSF rearing is sustainable and environmentally friendly.  
 Valorisation of USS into bioplastics and biopesticides (WP6) 
Actions will be carried out at DS 1, where USS will be partitioned to improve its valorisation. USS will be used as co-
substrate in the advanced anaerobic  digestion (AD)  step. Subsequently, the resulting material is used for

bioelectrosynthesis technologies ( BES). In this WP two prototypes will be designed and built to perform AD and 
BES, DS 1 (Madrid, ES) and DS 6 (SMVAK, CZ). Special attention will be given to the key parameters a nd system 
design for the production of valuable organics such as acids and alcohols (from the gas stream), which are in 
demand by different industrial segments (pharmaceutical, chemical and food industries). SCALIBUR will use these 
products for the production of bioplastics in a downstream process. 
In addition, and to fully exploit the BES prototype, the biogas produced in wastewater treatment plants operated 
by SMVAK (16%) will be valorised instead of flared. An innovative solution will be validated, which converts the CO
2 
contained in this off-gas (45% in DS #6) into different high-value products using BES.  
 Valorisation of surplus sewage sludge and organic waste into high quality PHBV bioplastic (WP6) 
The surplus activated sludge produced in the WWTP (WBD , NL) can be optimized to produce 
polyhydroxyalkalnoates (PHA) bioplastic harvested as a functional biomass. PHA will be produced when the 
biomass is subjected to aerobic or anoxic feast conditions within the WWTP using the microbial community 
growing directly in the biomass, with no additional requirement of energy. Using an extraction method with green 
solvents the PHA will be obtained . PHA has several applications, both as a biodegradable plastic and as an additive 
to improve other materials. This process will be done in DS 7 (WETSUS & WBD, NL). 
Life cycle and safety assessments (WP8) 
To verify and optimize the relative environmental sustainabil ity of the final bio based products obtained in this 
project, comparative LCA and SLCA studies are planned with the information collected from WPs 4-6. Together with 
the societal value of SCALIBUR results  a green profile and a cost profile are essential elements to be considered in 
the preparation of business models. Moreover, to verify and optimize efficacy and safe ty for humans and animals, 
quality driven analysis as well as in vitro safety and efficacity studies will be performed.  
Innovation-related activities (WPs 9-10) 
To reach key biowaste players, SCALIBUR project  will carry out a series of activities to disseminate key results to 
municipalities, waste managers, investors, current and future entrepreneurs as well as citizens  (WP9). These 
activities will increase awareness of collection solutions and will foster good practices in cities.  
A durable e xploitation strategy for the project’s results and the development of replicable business plans  will be 
performed during this project. The goal is to ensure successful market uptake of the valorisation technologies and 
products generated within the project (WP10). With the findings of the functional analysis and market assessment, 
the consortium will develop business models and business plans for each exploitable result.  
Sex and gender analysis 
The results of the innovation action are widely interdisciplinary and impact strongly upon women and men. A socio-
demographic analysis on the Attitude of Europeans towards waste management and resource efficiency reported in 
201418 shows a big gap among the answers of women and men, which is important to consider to ensure the 
excellence and high quality of the outcomes of SCALIBUR. At the start, the project team will create Urban Biowaste-
clubs to actively engage all relevant stakeholders in the waste value chain and to support the integration of the 
urban-biowaste valorisation a pproaches on a city level within each of the pilot regions. Citizen beh aviour and 
attitude towards bio waste and its valorisation will be assessed, considering also g ender and sex aspects. As 
previous EU reports show, d ifferent attitudes among women and men are expected.19 For example, women are 
more prone than men to reduce their household waste, whilst men are slightly more likely than women to think 
that better enforcement of existing antilitter laws would be effective (37% vs. 32%). In addition, women are  more 
likely to argue that reducing waste and sorting recyclable waste at home would make the biggest difference (54% 
vs. 49%). Moreover, it has been reported that gender may play a relevant role on the social acceptance of waste 
management costs.
20 It is therefore essential to perform this analysis to ensure that the social innovation initiatives 
are in line with the citizens  and to ensure that all actions implemented in SCALIBUR are gender inclusive . Special 
attention will be given to language and also to the design of the SCALIBUR stakeholder platform, which will also be 
gender inclusive.   Gender issues will  be addressed as well by promoting gender equality in recruitment and 
employment, following EC guideline s.21 This consortium consists of both highly qua lified female and male 
participants and partners will ensure that no gender will be unjustifiably preferred when recruiting new staff.

1.4 AMBITION 
1.4.1 STATE-OF-THE-ART AND BEYOND 
Proteins, lipids, chemical commodities, bioplastics, and biopesticides will be obtained using innovative technologies 
in the valorisation of urban biowaste. Three different waste sources will be used for valorisation processes (MSW, 
HORECA, ROW  and USS) in 7 different DSs. A design of three different lines of valorisation  processes has been 
created, namely biochemical conversion of the OFMSW (WP4), protein, lipid and chitin production from insects 
reared on ROW (WP5), and  generation of products from USS by anaerobic digestion and subsequent  
bioelectrochemical treatment of the resulting biogas; or fermentation of USS into PHA (WP6). Each line has been 
designed to optimally exploit each waste, considering their composition and physicochemical characteristics. 
Moreover, to fully optimize the bio based conversion of all waste fractions, where  applicable, side fractions not 
exploitable in the dedicated line can be shared among different WP s. These technological approaches are 
described below and detailed methodologies are summarized in section 3.1 (WPs description). 
Stabilisation of biowaste (WP3).  
Stabilisation of OFMSW, HORECA waste and USS will be performed before its valorisation into high-value products. 
Separation and optimisation of MSW from Madrid municipality (FCC, DS 1) will be done as follows: Detection of 
impurities directly in the conveyor belt and manual separation, trituration, separation of high density materials and 
removal of metals. Homogenisation, to balance different fractions of the organic waste will be done. Further, 
stabilization, hygenisation and sterilization to inhibit decomposition will be carried out. 
Sorting and pre-treatment of HORECA waste (Albano (IT), UNIMORE DS 5): Most suitable blends of HORECA waste 
(LAZIO, IT) for insect rearing will be identify, searching for the right balance of nutrient-enriched waste.  
Sorting and pre-treatment of USS (SMVAK, DS 6 and WBD, DS 7) consist of homogenisation of the sludges collected 
from primary settlement and the biological treatment. Optimised mixtures of fractions from the primary and 
secondary treatments will be done to r each the right balance before its valorisation. The activated sewage sludge 
from WBD ( DS 7, NL) will be collected from secondary treatment. Optimization to keep feedstock cultures with 
constant activity for PHBV production will be done. Additionaly, the ch ance to mix the secondary activated sludge 
from UWWTP with regionally sourced residual organic waste materials will be explored.  
Biochemical conversion of the organic fraction of MSW (WP4).  
Organic Fraction of Municipal Solid Waste (OFMSW) will be collec ted in Madrid ( DS 1) and will be pre -treated to 
ensure its stability. This stabilized OFMSW will be used for valorisation into bioplastics and biopesticides in DSs 2-4. 
To yield these bio-based products, several technological steps are required.  
  Enzymatic hydrolysis (EH) (DS 2, CENER): 
State-of-the-art: Biowaste displays high variability  in its compositio n (see table below) . D epending on the waste 
source and the effective decomposition of some of these components (cellulose, hemicellulose, starch and 
proteins) to simple molecules (i.e. sugars and amino acids) is often considered a rate -limiting factor of the 
biochemical process. Boosting this decomposition improvement of the solubilisation of the organic components in 
the OFMSW is required. Generally, different pretreatment processes - thermo-chemical, hydrothermal, enzymatic 
hydrolysis and combinations of chemical, thermal, and enzymatic treatments - are carried out. 
Component % in dry weight 
Cellulose 35-37% 
Hemicellulose 1.5-4.5% 
Lignin 7-9% 
Protein 5-6% 
Others (starch, sugars and lipids) ≤1.5% 
Table 1.4.1a Major components in OFMSW22 
EH uses enzymes as biocatalysts for the breakdown of cellulose into monomeric sugars . In combination with ß -
glucosidases, cellulases have the capacity to hydrolyse cellulose into glucose. In particular, t he filamentous fungus 
Trichoderma reesei produces a cocktail of enzymes (exo -cellulase, endo-cellulase, ß-glucosidase) that catalyses the 
reaction of water with cellulose to glucose. Due to the complex nature of cellulose, enzymatic hydrolysis is 
influenced by both the structural features of cellulose and related factors such as enzyme source, thermal 
                                                                                                               
22 Springham, D.; Moses, V.; Cape, R.E. Biotechnology - The Science and the Business. 1999. ISBN 9789057024078 - CAT# TF3180 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
14 
   
inactivation, activity balance for synergism, specific activity, nonspecific binding, and enzyme processability/ 
compatibility.  
The composition of enzymatic mixtures 
that will be used for EH depends on 
the nature of the raw material, the 
targeted compound and the ability of 
the used microorganisms to hydrolyze 
these compounds. Particularly, 
enzymatic hydrolysis has long been 
studied as a method to depolymerize 
the biogenic feedstocks into 
fermentable sugars, with a more 
recent focus on operating at high -
solids loadings.  This approach with 
high-solid loadings has been proposed 
to render the lignocellulosic 
conversion process more economically 
feasible.  Figure 3. Demo sites 1, 2 ,3, 4  
Currently there are several commercial technologies for biochemical conversion of MSW around the world. Only 
Fiberight23 (US), operates a demo plant based on EH and fermentation into ethanol. Nevertheless, Fiberight is 
doing solid loads of about 12% w/w; therefore, not yet into high solid loads. 
Beyond state-of-the-art: Unlike other commercial approaches, SCALIBUR’s efforts on EH processes will be focus ed 
on high solids loading (between 20% -25% w/w). 2425 This proc ess will be performed in specially adapted 3,000 L  
reactors, allowing higher sugar concentrations in the media and lower capital and operating costs.  A process is 
considered “high solids” if the ratio solid/liquid is such that almost no free water is present in the slurry or roughly 
a solids loadings ≥15% (w/w) 26,27. EH performed at high- solids loadings offers the following advantages over low - 
and moderate -solids loadings:  i) Higher final sugar concentrations  resulting in higher bio -based products 
concentrations ii) reducing energy use and costs associated with downstream processes because smaller equipment 
and/or fewer reactors to produce an equivalent output  are needed . iii) Reduction in water requirements:  this 
reduces the cost of disposal and/or treatment of processed water. 
The SCALIBUR project will use  a tailored enzyme cocktail based on careful analysis of biomass components, to 
optimize the full bioconversion of OFMSW by EH.  
Main challenges on Enzymatic hydrolysis at high-solids loadings:  
 Lack of available water in the reactor affects  mass transfer and lubricity.  When solid load reaches  20% (w/w) 
the apparent viscosity increases , complicating the mixing and handling of the material ,28 and contributing to 
increase final product inhibition of the enzymes . In SCALIBUR the enzymatic hydrolysis at high solids load (20 -
25% w/w) will be done in specially designed bioreactors with tailor-made impellers.  
 Long hydrolysis times. The reaction time needed for most enzymes to achieve sufficient glucose concentrations 
is usually 3 days27, which can only be reduced by increasing enzyme loading. However, enzymes can overcrowd 
accessible cellulose sites, affecting the full hydrolytic potential of the enzymes. In this project ASA will  provide 
cellulases with higher specific enzyme activity, the reaction temperature will be optimized for specific cellulase 
activity and mechanical-chemical will be also investigated. 
 Finding cost-effective approaches to develop highly active enzymes. Enzymes are typically added per weight of 
substrate, therefore at high loading the number  of enzymes must increase . SCALIBUR’s approach consists of 
using specific enzymes to depolymerize fractions other than carbohydrates (i.e. proteins, lipids), to achieve 
nutrient enriched hydrolysates for the next fermentation processes.

 The hydrolysate must comply with some quality requirements (solids, particulates, improper, etc.) for 
downstream processes commonly used at industrial scale. Throughout several intermediate processes e.g. 
coagulation and decanting the quality will be ensured. A concentration step will be applied to obtain high sugar 
syrup suitable for microbial conversion before fermentation if needed.  
  Fermentation to biopolyesters (DS 4, NOVAMONT): 
Conversion of OFMSW described above (using  EH and fermentation) yield several diols. Final valorisation  of these 
diols into bioplastics will be performed by NOVAMONT  (DS 4). Biobutanediol (1,4 BDO) will be obtained directly 
from sugars, thereby introducing production of other chemical intermediates from renewable sources.  
State-of-the-art: 1,4 Butanediol (BDO), which is normally obtained from fossil resources, is a chemical intermediate 
used in a wide range of applications (textiles, electronics, automotive, etc.), as well as a building block for the 
production of bioplastics. Besides the chemical processes that produce fossil -based BDO, there is an indirect 
biological route that produces 1,4 -BDO through the dehydration of succinic acid into succinic anhydride and the 
following hydrogenation to γ-butyrolactone (GBL).  
Beyond-state-of-the-art: Within the SCALIBUR project and based on the innovative enzymatic process developed by 
CENER (DS 2), the production of biobased 1,4 BDO from fermentable sugars produced through pre -treatment and 
hydrolysis of O FMSW will be demonstrated . Both upstream and downstream processes will be optimized for 
obtaining high purity (99%) 1,4 bio-BDO with optimal characteristics for polyesters formulation. 
Obtaining 1,4 Bio -BDO direct fermentation of sugars into succinyl -CoA b y an engineered E. coli  strain and 
subsequent production of 1,4 -BDO will be the strategy followed in SCALIBUR  (NOVAMONT DS 4). A downstream 
process mainly consisting of biomass removal, micro and nanofiltration, and ion exchange high purity Bio -BDO for 
polymerization application will be undertaken . This key building will then be  combined with other biobased 
dicarboxylic acids (among which azelaic acid obtained from low impact vegetable oils from dry corps ) to generate 
high performance biobased and biodegradable polyesters, which will be validated into sustainable packaging films 
application (by ITENE), following a full circular economy approach. 
Main challenges on the fermentation of liquid hydrolysed coming from OFMSW: 
 Low fermentability of OFMSW derived su gars into 1,4 bio-BDO: Work on sugar mix (including purer sources of 
sugars in combination with OFMSW derived sugars to achieve sustainable yields). Enhance sugars purification 
towards the obtaining of the desired purity. 
 Higher impurities in bio -BDO ferme ntation broth coming from OFMSW derived sugars : Downstream 
enhancement (separation and purification) towards the obtaining of high purity bio -BDO suitable for 
polymerization. 
  Production of microbial biopesticides (DS 3, AERIS): 
State-of-the-art: Currently, the standard method of productio n of substances with high- value by means of 
microorganisms is the process of fermentation. There are many types of fermentation; the two mo st common are 
"submerged" and "semi-solid", also known as “solid state fermentation” (SSF).  
The growth of microorganisms in a fully liquid system (so-called submerged or deep-tank fermentation) has several 
advantages: constant temperature and pH, the abil ity to pump air into the system and disperse it with stirring 
impellers, and the capacity to generate reasonably homogeneous conditions to maximize the growth of the 
microorganisms. Despite the se advantages, some fungi microorganisms will not yield a satis factory product 
through this type of fermentation. Semi -solid fermentation offers an alternative where the fungi microorganisms 
grow mainly on the wet surface of a solid material. This setting allows fungi to grow in conditions more similar to 
those found in nature, with the spores produced in the air being consequently more durable, and relatively easy to 
develop on a small scale. Nevertheless, scaling up this process to the sizes necessary for a commercial product 
presents numerous problems: aeration becomes difficult as the volume of a semi -solid mass and trays are difficult 
to keep sterile. In addition, the development of large vessels to scale- up semi-solid media fermentation requires 
the invention of a number of techniques or pieces of equipment.29 
Beyond state-of-the-art: The European biopesticides market is growing annually at a rate of 20%. Use of agro -
industrial wastes and SSF technology offers an alternative to biopesticide production with advantages vs  
conventional submerged fermentations:  reduced cost and energy consumption, low production of residual water 
and high stability products.  The reliability of SSF for the bioconversion of solid organic wastes into high -value 
                                                                                                               
29 Crit Rev Biotechnol.; 35,326-33 (2015) 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
16 
   
products is proven by a number of recent research studies 30,31,32. SSF consists of a low-cost technology that allows 
production of biosurfactants, enzymes (as peroxydases, cellulases, lipases or proteases), bioplastics and others.  
Nowadays, research efforts are focusing o n finding the most adequate culturing conditions (in terms of mixi ng, 
oxygen and nutrients requirements, temperature, pH, etc.) in order to optimize the production of these high- value 
compounds. During SCALIBUR, different strategies for the extraction and the conservation of the products will be 
optimized. The sugar hydr olysate produced from the EH  of the OFMSW  (CENER, DS 2) will be used for its 
bioconversion in biopesticides using Bacillus thuringensis sp (AERIS, DS 3) in a 1,000 L bioreactor to be considered a 
new valorisation route in a biorefinery. Moreover, the unhyd rolysed solid fraction wil l be also exploited using SSF  
to produce biopesticides (biofungicides and bioinsecticides). The optimal ranges of the main operational 
parameters will be established in order to maximize biopesticides production at an affordable cost.  
So far, most results have been obtained at lab -scale conditions, producing minimal amounts of valuable products 
and working under ideal, sterile conditions. Hence, one of the interests is in the upscaling of the process. A deep 
knowledge of the varia bles influencing the process and a wide experience in this or similar research fields is 
required in order to achieve an efficient scale-up. Both CENER and AERIS have this expertise.  
Main challenges in the production of biopesticides: 
 Maintenance of stabi lity of the production culture , both in its initial form (preservation) and as subcultures 
infrequently propagated via sporulation or vegetative generations. Laboratory tests to  establish the influence 
of the use of cultures previously adapted to the condi tions will be done . Emphasis will be on maximizing  the 
production of biopesticides and reducing the processing time. 
 Establishing the  conditions ensuring reproducible yields  and demonstration of microbial biopesticides 
production from substrates derived fr om OFMSW. SCALIBUR w ill tackle this by use of ra w ma terials of 
appropriate quality and the development of analytical methods for controlling culture processes.  
Protein, lipid and chitin production from insects reared on HORECA waste (WP5).  
Valorisation of ROW and HORECA waste by insect rearing will be done in Italy ( DS 5), where the current legislation 
considers that ROW is a by -product, while HORECA is considered a waste and feed for animals (including insects). 
To demonstrate that HORECA waste is a vali d feedstock for insect rearing, this stream will be used in parallel to 
ROW during WP5. HORECA waste and ROW will be collected in Lazio (IT)  and this by-product will be characterized 
and analysed. To produce bio-based products the Black Soldier Fly (BSF) will be used in a pilot plant (UNIMORE, DS 
5). SCALIBUR will focus its efforts on producing proteins, lipids and chitin through this innovative approach.  
 Insect rearing (DS 5, UNIMORE (IT)  
State-of-the-art: Insects like Black soldier Fly (BSF) Hermetia illucens (Diptera, Stratiomyidae) can convert in a very 
efficient way kitchen and restaurant scraps, or simply organic materials , into a biomass rich in proteins, lipids  and 
chitin33,34,35. In some European countries such as Germany ( www.hermetia.de) and the Netherlands 
(https://protix.eu) studies have been carried out  to use the BSF pre- pupae for food and feed  (aquaculture) 
purposes, rearing BSF on by-products of the vegetable food chain. 
As a demonstration of the growing interest in the subject, the EU has recently financed a €2.1M project (InDirect 
Project) aimed at developing biorefinery processes for the direct or indirect conversion of wa ste and by -products 
of the European agro -food chain through insects . Previously, another project of about 4 million euros 
(PROteINSECT) has been completed on the rearing of insects for the production of food and feed. 
Despite the great interest in BSF industrial rearing, there is  still no company able to propose industrial plants for 
massive insect rearing with several tons of insects per month production. At the moment in Italy there are only a 
few companies able to produce insects and BSF in particular that is mainly used for pet feeding/fishing.

Figure 4. Demo site 5 
Beyond state-of-the-art: This project takes advantage of the potential o f the organic materials using them  as a 
growth substrate to mass rear  the BSF , a non -infesting fly, whose larvae are able to rear on a wide variety of 
organic substrates with a high moisture content. Thanks to their action, the phosphorus and nitrogen content of 
the organic substrate is reduced, bacterial growth is suppressed, even that of harmful strains, 36 unpleasant odours 
and the population of invasive domestic flies are reduced. 37 The resulting residue after insect rearing is a good 
quality compost, valuable for agricultural crops. 38 In relation to th e type of growth substrate, mature larvae and 
pre-pupae (pre-adult stage) can be used for various purposes, depending on the laws of different countries.  
A project coordinated by UNIMORE  (leader of WP5), ValoriBio - Valorisation of organic waste by insects to obtain 
biomaterials for agricultural uses (€1.2 M POR -ERDF 2014-2020) - has developed a pilot plant for the breeding of 
insects on animal manure. A  new concept of BSF industrial rearing was adopted and new tech nologies were 
developed in order to decrease the manual labour and increase the industrial scalability. This  pilot plant is ready to 
be scaled-up and to be affordable for European applications. This production plant can be divided into  two main 
parts: a) the eggs production part where adults mate and lay their eggs  and b) the bioconverter where larvae grow 
on organic waste and carry out its conversion. A new technology for eggs collection was designed, tested in the lab, 
fabricated and covered by a patent ( submitted). In the larvae production part, a fully automated system for larvae 
feeding and growth was developed. This technology was designed to be industrially scalable and cost-effective. 
 Protein, lipid and chitin extraction from insect fractionation (DS 5, UNIMORE & Kour, IT) 
State-of-the-art: Protein may be extracted with different reported protocols, primarily used to separate only one 
constituent from the insect biomass 39,40,41, using pH adjustments to cause protein precipitation. Nevertheless, 
insects are rich with other interesting and valuable substances worth being  exploited: lipids and chitin. The 
extraction of lipids is the first step of insect fractionation. On dry, grinded insects  a solvent extraction is carried out 
to yield a defatted fraction for further protein extraction. The second step gives raw proteins and raw chitin by 
selective precipitations at different pH. Yield of protein extraction ranges between 70% and 90% depending on the 
procedure42. Unfortunately, current methods are too complex to be easily scaled up to an industrial level.  Other 
authors used less aggressive but time-consuming approaches, such as fermentation and EH43,44. 
Beyond state-of-the-art: SCALIBUR’s approach will benefit fro m the expertise of UNIMORE, whose protocol to 
extract all protein, lipid, and chitin,  has been recently developed 45. Different systematic approaches were applied 
on SF pre -pupae to fractionate lipid, protein and chitin to yield three fractions, following a cascade protocol. The 
protein yield reached on wet prepupae is about 6% and twice as much on dry matter. 
Characterisation of the protein will be performed by Zetadec. Zetadec’s methods will be optimised to validate and 
accurately estimate the potential use of the resulting products for feed, food, biomass and fertilizer industries.

Bioconversion of sewage sludge into high value chemicals, pesticides and polymers (WP6). 
  Conversion of biogas and solid fraction of USS (DS 1&6, Madrid & SMVAK): 
The main destinations for the biogas produced in WWTP  are cogeneration engines, where electricity and heat are 
concomitantly obtained, and flaring torch where excess of biogas is burned.  Instead of flaring the biogas, 
SCALIBUR’s approach raises its utilization to obtain enriched biomethane and organic compounds using 
bioelectrosynthesis (BES).  Specifically, CO 2 contained in biogas from MSW treatment ( DS 1 (ES) ) and from USS 
treatment (DS 6 (CZ)) will be used to produce organic compounds. T hese biological CO 2 streams have less toxic 
metal or chemical impurities compar ed to industrial CO 2 off-gases. The integration of this  process with the waste 
treatment would enable to re-utilize the emitted CO2 and increase the sustainability of these facilities. 
USS will be submitted to physical, chemical and biological processes in dividually or combined with the resulting 
solid fraction from EH of OFMSW (WP4, DS 2) to produce high-value products using BES. 
State-of-the-art: Nowadays, management of USS  includes composting for farmland utilization, incineration and 
landfilling46. The most widely used treatment is anaerobic digestion (AD) to convert it into biogas. This treatment is 
very inefficient (30-50% efficiency), and the produced biogas shows a low energy content (5,000 –  6,000 kCal/m3) 
as well as impurities like H2S and NH3. 
The rate limiting step in AD is the hydrolysis step, leading to high retention times, low organic solids degradation 
and unsatisfactory CH4 output47. Conventional mesophilic anaerobic digestion presents low overall volatile solids 
(VS) removal efficiency (30-50%) of raw sludge even at very long retention times of 20-30 days48. To accelerate this 
process and improve the efficiency of AD, various pre- treatment technologies have been developed, 
including49,50,51: i) mechanical (e.g. ultrasonic, microwave, electrokineti c, and high -pressure homogenization), ii) 
thermal, iii) chemical (e.g. acidic, alkali, ozonation, fenton chemistry) and iv) biological treatment (temperature -
phased AD, enzyme and microbial electrolysis cell).  
Although different pre-treatment methods have been proposed, full-scale application is not widely implemented. 
Figure 5. Demo sites 1, 3, 6 and 7 
There are a few patented technologies that 
have been applied in practical sludge 
treatment: CambiTHP™, Biothelys® (TH), 
Biosonator (ultrasonication), Aspal SLUDGE™, 
Praxair® Lyso™ (microwave), BioCrack 
(electrokinetic disintegration), MicroSludge™, 
and Cellruptor (HPH). The main disadvantages 
of full-scale implementation are: i) high 
energy demand and capital cost, ii) complex 
equipment, iii) complex operation and 
maintenance, and iv) risk of recalcitrant 
compounds formation in the case of thermal 
process. 
Beyond state-of-the-art: SCALIBUR proposes the implementation of reliable physical and mechanical pre -treatment 
for sewage sludg e conditioning to be subsequently treated by biological systems. This enhances sludge reduction 
and methane recovery, with associated energy, environmental and economic benefits. Therefore, energy required 
for pre -treatment, final sludge dewatering, transp ortation and ultimate disposal as well as corresponding GHG 
emission would be fully considered in SCALIBUR.  
Scalibur’s prototype for the anaerobic bioconversion of sewage sludge will include an innovative process for the 
collection (single and mixture was tes), conditioning and feed of the pre -treated materials. Pre-treatment by 
mechanical m illing and subsequent  anaerobic bioconversion will result in three value fractions: i) liquid for 
fertirrigation, ii) solid for biofertilizes production, and ii) biogas to obtain high-value compounds.

Bioelectrosynthesis technologies (BES) are an alternative to conventional physical and chemical biogas upgrading 
techniques for the production of biomethane from sewage sludge and MSW management. This process is driven by 
microorganisms grow n autotrophically using CO 2 as electron acceptor. Different compounds can be produced  
depending on the type of microorganisms present in the system . BES is highly versatile, with adaptable operation 
conditions allowing the preparation of target compounds, by influencing the metabolism of the microorganisms.  
The biogas from the AD of sewage sludge can be treated bioelectrochemically to produce high -value alcohols and 
carboxylic acids. For this purpose, biogas collection and conditioning wil l be carried out to be fed into the BES 
prototype. Optimization of the BES process will be done  using a ready-to-use inoculum. T his guarantees a quick 
start-up and stabilization of the SCALIBUR BES prototype.  Direct CO2 transformation in situ  BES and micro bial 
utilization of H 2 is achieved . This approach provides very high local H 2 concentration available for the microbial 
reaction, and lowering the overpotential of electrolytic H 2, which avoids process inhibition . This approach will 
greatly advance BES tec hnology readiness level to produce multi -carbon compounds from CO 2.52,53. To date, 
acetate is the most common final product of synthesis in the majority of BES studies that attempted this 
production methodology. However, University of Girona proved that buty rate and small amounts of ethanol and 
butanol can be produced by BES using CO2 as a sole carbon substrate70. 
Main challenges of USS pre-treatment, anaerobic bioconversion and bioelectrosynthesis technologies 
 Given the fluctuating composition of the raw was te materials (and mixtures) cost- effective homogenization 
and pre -treatment processes are desired to keep the system running close to steady state conditions. 
SCALIBUR addresses this issue including additional steps (separation, homogenization, pre-treatment methods) 
to be easily implemented in the prototypes and also at industrial scale.  
 The presence of complex molecules in the biowastes can make their hydrolysis difficult, limiting the anaerobic 
fermentation rate. Efficient physical and mechanical proces ses will be combined with chemical methods  to 
break-down complex molecules, improving the efficiency of the following anaerobic step. 
 Raw waste materials can contain inhibitory compounds and/or impurities  that can negatively impact on 
microorganisms. The B ES technology proposed in SCALIBUR uses the gas stream result ing from wastes 
processing, avoiding these effects and mitigating the impact of fluctuations in feed characteristics. 
  Valorisation of surplus sewage sludge into high quality PHBV (DS 7, WETSUS & WBD, NL): 
Most of the surplus activated sludge that is nowadays produced in the municipal WWTP  can be optimized to 
produce polyhydroxyalkalnoates (PHA) bioplastic 54,55. Fermented organic municipal waste or primary sewage 
sludge can be used to produce a PH A rich biomass  after dewatering and drying . The PHA can be extracted with 
green solvents to produce a pure and high quality PHA bioplastic with a very low environmental footprint. PHA has 
several applications both as a biodegradable plastic and as an additive to improve other materials56,57.  
State-of-the-art: Currently, it is estimated that the global PHA production (mainly by Kaneka, Danimer, Tianan) is 
between 2,000 – 4,000 tons/year. As market demand has started rising from 2015 onward, it is expected that these 
numbers will increase significantly due to scale up activities by various producer s.58 Furthermore, the current 
production methods are based on fe edstocks, like sugar or palm oil  that are in competition with food and feed 
production. With USS  one specific microbial culture is  grown that can produce the PHA with accumulation  in the 
microbes. Extraction from the biomass via oxidative wet- chemical methods is done. There are various European 
initiatives to produce PHA material using organic waste and USS . These approaches hold the promise of th e use of 
lower grades feedstock; however, none of the initiatives have progressed further than pilot scale.59,60 
Beyond state -of-the-art: Compared to other initiatives that intend to produce PHA from organic waste , the 
approach describe d here has some distinctive differences. First, PHA can be produced when this biomass is 
subjected to aerobic or anoxic feast conditions within the WWTP using the microbial community growing directly in 
the biomass  (without additional co sts from WWTP or additional energy and feedstock ). Secondly, a patented 
extraction method using green solvents to extract the PHA will be used, whereas most other competing processes

use a n oxidative wet approach. This extraction procedure yields  high qual ity PHA material with high molecular 
weights and controlled  PHA composition. It also leads to  an increase in purity of the resulting PHA, removing 
impurities and micro -pollutants. Using this strategy,  a PHA that consists of a copolymer of butyrate and vale rate 
(PHBV) with unique properties (more rubbery, amorphous, lower melting point) is obtained.  
In 2015 – 2016 fifteen municipal WWTP in The Netherlands were tested for PHA accumulation-potential by analysis 
of their surplus secondary sludge. The maximum P HA content reached ranged from 15 to 52% of the organic 
content. Economic evaluations show that a PHA content of 40 -50% is sufficient; therefore, some municipal WWTP 
can serve as process units producing functional biomass with PHA storing capacities. More importantly, 
modifications to treatment plants are not required 61. Fine tuning of the process can be implemented in practice to 
bring a wide range of WWTPs to produce biomass with PHA accumulation potential of 50 to 69 % organic wt. A 10 -
month pilot includi ng PHA accumulation and extraction showed that a very high quality PHA product could 
consistently be made (PHARIO project).  
Main Challenges for valorisation of surplus sewage sludge and organic waste to produce high quality PHA: 
Currently, there are three challenges that will be overcome in SCALIBUR by establishing a production line making 
up to 100 Kg of material per year: 
 End-users require enoug h material to be able to evaluate their interest  in involvement. SCALIBUR will work  
with prototype materials to plan a developing business around the material supply chain. 
 Costs for the solvent extraction process in the scale -up are currently only estimates, showing that this process 
is economical. However, cost must be understood with greater certainty.  SCALIBUR findings in the kilogram 
facility will help secure investments in scale-up design.  
 Food packaging is a relevant and promising field of application of PHA materials . However, renewable 
resources produced from “wastes” are stigmatized, given their origin from waste. The available evidence shows 
that solvent extraction methods, as used in SCALIBUR, will yield a pure PHBV material that could be used in 
food applications. Notwithstanding, these aspects can only be understood from the data and experience 
gained from within a true production environment as proposed herein. SCALIBUR aims also at the production 
and characterisation of the resulting products to ensure high quality.  
1.4.2 Innovation Potential 
The SCALIBUR project has been designed considering the interdisciplinary interactions among all different 
strategies provided by 21 partners, each of them bringing expertise that contribute s to ensuring excellence in the 
project. The main goal is  to create and develop innovative urban biowaste valorisation systems to produce high -
value biobased products through adaptation and upgrading of the current value chain and by applying co -creation 
methodologies involving relevant stakeholders such as citizens and municipalities. 
SCALIBUR is an innovation action with a large innovation potential.  New products, services and business models will 
arise from the project, included, but not limited to: 
 The SCALIBUR concept integrated by biowaste management companies. 
 Commercialisation of the SCALIBUR processes for production of biobased products. 
 Commercialisation of improved biobased products with great interest in industrial applications (food industry 
packaging materials, agriculture, chemical industry, etc.) 
 New collection schemes of biowaste at the city level.  
 Integrated stakeholder platform for prevention of waste and improved biowaste quality and the establishment 
of best practices among European countries for urban biowaste selective collection. 
 Commercialisation of tailored monitoring systems for biowaste treatment plants. 
 Commercialisation of CH4 and H2S sensors in waste management companies. 
 Knowledge about user acceptance, user behaviour and willingness for adaptation. 
 Engineering services for further biorefinery projects and similar projects. 
 A set of practical recommendations for urban biowaste management at all levels.

SECTION 2. IMPACT
2.1 EXPECTED IMPACTS 
2.1.1 CONTRIBUTION TO EXPECTED IMPACTS UNDER THE CALL TOPIC CE-SFS-25-2018 
The SCALIBUR project aims to create and develop innovative urban biowaste valorisation systems by upgrading 
existing value chains, obtaining high value biobased products, and by applying co -creation methodologies involving 
citizens, municipalities and other related stakeholders. This project is expected to develop its full potential and 
achieve its objectives by 2022. SCALIBUR will involve the participation of three municipalities (Madrid (ES), Albano 
(LAZIO, IT) and Kozani (CLUBE
, LE)) to establish a pilot for every system developed. These systems will be replicable 
in different contexts internationally and are thus expected to encourage new policies regarding urban biowaste 
treatment. A figure of Best 
Performing Territories  is crea ted, 
which represents municipalities with 
the current Municipal Waste lowest 
landfilling rate (in SCALIBUR, 
represented by LUND, Sweden ). The 
current landfilling rate per country is 
shown in 
Figure 6. In addition, a 
Following Territories figure will also 
be created during the project, 
represented by municipalities in 
countries with the highest municipal 
waste landfilling rates. The Best 
Territories will have the role of 
exchanging best practices with the 
three pilot  municipalities, being a 
reference for the implementation of 
the new biowaste management scheme. Following Territories will be the receptors of the created good practices, 
business models and other project results for replicating SCALIBUR innovative biowas te management scheme and 
achieving an international impact. Furthermore, new sustainable business models will be created during the course 
of this project, to ensure economic revenue in the locations where these systems are implemented, and to create 
momentum for other stakeholders to engage in SCALIBUR technologies in an early stage. 
Validated technical and economic viability of the proposed approaches at target TRL 7  
SCALIBUR will develop three innovative processes to obtain added -value products. The fir st one (WP4) will make 
use of the sugar fraction coming from OFMSW to obtain biobased plastics (polyesters) and biopesticides, with an 
initial TRL of 5 -6 to a final TRL7. The second one (WP5) will use HORECA and ROW waste to produce added -value 
products (including proteins for food and feed, lipid biobased plastics and chitin/chitosan), with an initial TRL of 4-6 
to a final TRL 7. The last one valorises sewage sludge and MSW to obtain bioplastics (PHAs) for packaging purposes 
and biopesticides with a starting TRL 5-6 to a final TRL 7. The technical and economic viability of each new process 
will be continuously assessed and re-validated through a techno-economic assessment and LCA analysis (WP8). 
New business and organisational models on cities ensuring the full integration of the upgraded urban biowaste 
value into the existing local waste/wastewater management schemes 
From its start, SCALIBUR will cooperate with municipalities, citizens, waste collectors and managers and other 
quadruple helix stakeholders in the locations of its pilot plants, not only to implement the mentioned biowaste 
valorisation procedures, but also to develop new business and social innovation approaches enabling the full 
integration of the valorisation technologies tested in WP4 -6. This will ensure economic revenue from these novel 
waste re-valorisation methods in a circular-economy fashion. 
Improved citizen perception of urban biowaste as a local resource and their enhanced active participation in its 
separate collection through social innovation initiatives; improved consumer acceptance of urban biowaste -derived 
products, including food and feed
