Co-creation activities and citizen engagement are a key issue for the development of SCALIBUR project, as reflected 
in WP2. This will be achieved in each municipality through engagement activities involving all relevant stakeholders 
and encouraging social innovation. Engagement activities include the creation of a tailored stakeholder 
engagement plan, a forum representing all related stakeholder’ s interests (Urban Biowasteclubs, representing 
citizens, waste managers, waste collectors, policy representatives, etc.), co -creation workshops and “see, touch, 
taste” experiences, engaging presentations back-to-back at existing citizen events. The generated outcomes will be 
validated through monitoring tools including our stakeholder platform at a neighbourhood level, in order to 
corroborate and validate behaviour changes related to urban biowaste management. In addition, participatory and 
co-creation acti vities throughout the project will present urban biowaste -derived products as a local resource, 
hence aiming to improve consumer acceptance. DIY guidelines for further uptake of Urban Biowasteclubs and 
project replicability will be provided based on the pr oject results in the three municipalities to increase the impact 
of this project. A policy brief “Recommendations for urban biowaste management” will be created and 
disseminated in order to encourage national policy to foster this uptake in other regions, cities, and EU countries.  
A more sustainable and resilient protein supply chain 
One of the three innovative urban biowaste valorisation systems proposed in SCALIBUR will make use of ROW 
HORECA to obtain high -value biobased products, such as proteins for f eed amongst others (as described in WP5). 
In alignment with “The Future of Protein: The Protein Challenge 2040” 62 document, SCALIBUR will provide an 
innovative, sustainable and resilient pattern to obtain food and feed. A huge environmental impact reduction  and 
improved land use will be achieved this way, since fields currently used for the production of animal feed can then 
be used for other agricultural purposes. 
Safety assessment of biobased processes and products from urban biowaste 
The safety assessment  of each new processes, especially in relation to urban biowaste, will be continuously 
followed-up and validated through safety assessments performed by the partner NS, as they are experts in in -vitro 
analysis with tailored Standard-operating Protocols (SOP). Safety assessments will be performed in WP8. 
Reduced amount of urban biowaste that would otherwise be incinerated or landfilled, and hence reduced 
environmental impact (including emissions of GHG and of air pollutants and their precursors) of municipal  and food 
waste 
SCALIBUR’s main impact will consist of a wide reduction of urban biowaste incineration and/or landfilling. Only 
during the project, a significant increase in organic fraction selective waste collection will be achieved in each pilot 
municipality. The current rates for organic fraction selective waste collection and the expected final rate per 
municipality are: Albano (LAZIO) – from 75% to 90%; Madrid – from 71% to 85%; and Kozani (CLUBE): from 19% to 
50%. A total incrementation of collected and valorised OFMSW of 21,945,600 t/year will be achieved, a reduction of 
21,79 Mt CO2 eq/year. In relation to the waste management plants, 30 t of urban biowaste will be valorised through 
different chemical and biological processes applied in the Spanish pilot plant. A valorisation of up to 30,000 t/year 
could be achieved at the end of the project, only considering the Spanish pre -treatment plant from Madrid ( DS 1, 
FCC, Las Dehesas). Furthermore, more than half of the biogas produced in this pre -treatment plant is misused and 
flared in a torch. The same occurs in wastewater treatment plants operated by SVMAK (16% of biogas produced is 
flared). A conversion of CO
2 contained in this off -gas (40%) into high -value products will be also achieved as an 
indirect c onsequence of the project (by implementing the fermentation solution developed in WP4 in those 
plants), thus capturing more than 12,264 Tonnes of CO2 per day per every similar facility implementing SCALIBUR’s 
developed solutions (biomethanation & wastewater treatment plants).  
Moreover, it is projected that the installed biogas production capacity in Europe will be of 30 billion m 3/year by 
2030 (European Biogas Association, EBA), of which about 30 -40% are a potential CO 2 source. SCALIBUR’s results 
will potentially save 300 – 400 Mm3 emissions of CO2/year by 2030.

the project. All of these activities will be continuously redefined through the feedback obtained during project 
development. The KERs (Key Exploitable Results) obtained during and after the project will be exploited by every 
involved partner, as defined in Table 3.2.1g, Table 3.2.1.h and Table 3.2.1.i. In addition, a preliminary exploitation

2.1.3 OTHER SIGNIFICANT IMPACTS NOT MENTIONED IN THE WORK PROGRAMME 
Policy impacts 
SCALIBUR will produce results that will influence the modification  of existing policies and their adaptation to the 
new processes, products and biowaste value chains in the area of bioplastics, waste management and animal 
feeding, including D2.2. National manuals for local uptake, D2.3. Policy brief “Recommendations for urban 
biowaste management”, D.5.6. Regulatory draft amending provisions on animal feeding in order to include insects 
and D.8.6. Regulatory Assessment. These deliverables will bring scientific evidence and validated results influencing 
EU and national rela ted regulations, as the new waste collection methodologies implemented in pilot 
municipalities and the biobased products obtained will constitute an improved biowaste management scheme. 
Thus, upgrades on related policies will be a key issue in order to imp lement and replicate the SCALIBUR results in 
other countries or regions. 
The following KPIs will be used as policy success indicators : (1) local implementation of national manuals; (2) 
recommendations by EU institutions after the submission of amending pro posals on EU acts; (3) changes made to 
EU and national acts after the submission of amending proposals; and (4) removal of legislative barriers to the 
fulfilment of the project’s objectives.

Alignment with the FOOD 2030 Staff Working Document64:  
This document establishes 4 main challenges regarding the following topics: Nutrition & Health, Climate & 
Sustainability, Circularity & Resource Efficiency and Innovation & Communities, with research and innovation 
priorities assigned to the aforementioned challenges, in order to mitigate and/or solve them. SCALIBUR contributes 
to the accomplishment of R&I priorities assigned to the 4 challenges: 
 Nutrition & Health: SCALIBUR provides new sustainable and resilient protein sources by valorising HORECA and 
retail organic waste through the process described in WP5. In addition, increased social awareness regarding 
the accep tance of urban biowaste -derived products (including food and feed) will be achieved through 
stakeholder and citizen engagement activities. All of them will be implemented from the beginning, and 
continuously revised and improved during the course of the pr oject (as described in WP2). An enhanced 
perception of urban biowaste as a local resource will be achieved this way. 
 Climate & sustainability : SCALIBUR contributes to GHG mitigation, biodiversity conservation, soil, water and 
land remediation, and the growth and preservation of healthy plants and animals, by strongly diminishing 
urban waste landfilling and thus avoiding landfill effects. These effects include production of leachate, the 
emission of GHGs produced during waste degradation (landfill sites cont ribute 20% of the world’s 
anthropogenic methane emissions
65), ecological effects leading to landscape changes, loss of habitats and 
displacement of fauna. Moreover, the implementation of SCALIBUR results in biomethanation and wastewater 
treatment plants for obtaining high-value biobased products will capture around 12,264 Tonnes of CO2 per day 
per plant. The replicability of results, together with the project’s international approach will definitely lead to a 
huge GHG emission reduction.  
 Circularity & Resource Efficiency: SCALIBUR allows the use of food losses and waste through the valorisation of 
HORECA and retail organic waste and organic MSW (since these raw materials are used to obtain high -value 
biobased products), while increasing resource efficiency and circularity across the food system. 
 Innovation & Communities: SCALIBUR contributes in almost all R&I priorities established in this area: (1) boost 
innovation, (2) empowering communities and consumers in FNS (Food National Security), (3) boosting 
investment in public and private sector R&I FNS, (4) encouraging RRI in food systems, (5) Open Science and 
acces to data and information in FNS, (6) quadruple helix innovation, multi -actor and public engagement in 
food systems, (7) education, skills development and capacity building in FNS and food science, and (8) new 
business models and inclusive/open/eco-/sustainable innovation. 
Activities defined in WP2 aim to engage and empower citizens and stakeholders through co -creation activities and 
workshops and the participation of all relevant quadruple helix stakeholders (citizens and society –  represented by 
the Urban Biowasteclubs, universities and academia, industry –  and government – represented by the 
municipalities). SCALIBUR aims to influence policies at a National and European level through the creation of 
guidelines and new business and social innovation approaches related to the upgraded urban biowaste value chain. 
All project results will be accessible through the online Stakeholder Platform as developed in  WP7. All the resulting

Alignment with EU Bioeconomy Strategy 201266:  
SCALIBUR is completely aligned with the Bioeconomy Action Plan proposed in the EU Bioeconomy Strategy 2012. 
SCALIBUR’s consortium includes multi -disciplinary and cross -sectorial members. Stakeholders related to urban 
biowaste value chains will provide data obtained during the validation and follow- up of novel waste management 
techniques in the 3 pilot plants in 3 different EU countries to provide scie ntific evidence that will influence urban 
biowaste-related regulations. In other words, SCALIBUR will provide new knowledge on urban biowaste valorisation 
technologies that can be further used in training schemes. Universities are part of the project conso rtium and the 
data generated will be accessible to all stakeholders through the Stakeholder Platform (detailed in WP7), which 
guarantees data dissemination. The online Stakeholder Platform will be also used as a tool for the establishment of 
a Bioeconomy O bservatory, and the policy interaction of SCALIBUR will be reinforced by stakeholder engagement 
activities performed throughout the project (WP2). Moreover, SCALIBUR will address global challenges regarding 
food security and climate change by supplying pro teins through sustainable and reliable patterns.  SCALIBUR is 
aligned with action 2.3 of the Bioeconomy Action Plan “Enhancement of markets and competitiveness in 
bioeconomy” as well, since it establishes scale-up activities (the three main processes that will be developed in the 
pilot plants) and the above -mentioned stakeholder engagement activities (including the training and deep 
involvement of citizens/stakeholders in a sustainable production of new high-value biobased products). 
Alignment with EU’s Circular Economy Package 2015:  
This document includes four proposals amending the Waste Framework Directive, Landfilling Directive and 
Packaging Waste Directive for achieving circular economy in the EU. SCALIBUR is strongly aligned with the 
objectives included in the proposal amending the Landfilling Directive, which establishes a limit of 10% in the share 
of municipal waste landfilled and a target increase of 65% in the preparation for re -use and recycling of municipal 
waste by 2030. SCALIBUR directly contrib utes to the Landfilling Directive by substantially 
increasing the reuse of 
OFMSW through its valorisation (increase of 15 -41% depending on the municipality)  into high -value biobased 
products such as proteins, lipids, bioplastics and biopesticides. The proj ect will also provide huge economic and 
environmental benefits, as expected in the Circular Economy Package 2015, amongst others: 
 Direct creation of more than 130 jobs by 2022  (see Table 3.2.1j), and the indirect creation of 664,464 job 
positions (only in pilot municipalities) due to the incrementation of the  economic value of OFMSW by 300%, 
and considering a rate of job creation of 1 job per increase of 150,000 € of additional turnover in the upgraded 
biowaste value chain. 
 A decrease in GHG emissions of 21,79 Mt CO2 eq/year (only in pilot municipalities) due to the incrementation of 
OFMSW valorised, and by more than 12,264 Tonnes of CO 2 per day per every similar facility implementing 
SCALIBUR’s developed solutions (biomethanation & wastewater treatment plants). Thus, a potential saving of 
300 – 400 Mm3 emissions of CO2/year can be achieved by 2030. 
 An increase in the competitiveness of EU waste management, by integrating innovative valorisation systems 
into the existing urban municipal waste value chains, reducing dependency of the EU on raw material imports. 
 Moreover, SCALIBUR will reduce the huge existing differences in landfill and reuse of waste between EU 
Member States because of its international approach, since it develops replicable systems in municipalities of 3 
different Member States that can be applied and scaled-up in other EU locations.  
Alignment with the priorities of H2020 Challenge 2 
Additionally, SCALIBUR is also aligned with 4 out of the 5 main priorities established in the Food security, 
sustainable agriculture and forestry, marine, maritime and inland water research and the bioeconomy67:  
1. Addressing climate change and resilience on land and sea : achieved by significantly reducing GHG emissions 
(21,79 Mt CO 2 eq/year (only in pilot municipalities), plus around 12,264 Tonnes of CO 2 per day per fa cility 
implementing SCALIBUR’s results) through waste landfilling minimization, by creating new patterns to obtain 
food, feed and biobased products applying a circular economy approach. Furthermore, a new pattern to obtain 
chitin from biowaste will be defined against current methods for chitin extraction affecting crustaceans; 
2. Making the transition towards a circular bioeconomy : achieved by upgrading current urban waste and sewage 
sludge value chains (which valorise urban biowaste in the form of high -value biobased products), and

Environmental and sustainability impacts 
 COP21 Agreement Paris68:  The Paris Agreement, adopted through Decision 1/CP.21, addresses  crucial areas 
necessary to combat climate change, setting up key aspects. SCALIBUR contributes to the following key 
aspects: Long-term temperature goal (Art.2) and Global peaking (Art. 4)  – by significantly diminishing GHG 
emissions through a minimization  of waste landfilling ( 21,79 Mt CO2 eq/year (only in pilot municipalities)) and 
also by the implementation of SCALIBUR’s processes in waste management and wastewater plants (more than 
20,000 nm 3 CO2 per day per plant); Sinks and reservoirs (Art. 5)  – by bo osting MSW and sewage sludge 
valorisation, thus applying a circular economy approach and diminishing the need for raw materials; Climate 
change education, training, public awareness, public participation and public access to information (Art. 12)  – 
by perf orming citizen engagement activities to enhance waste collection and raise awareness for the 
acceptance of new biobased products obtained through valorisation processes, and by providing open access 
to all SCALIBUR relevant information shared through the Stakeholder Platform. 
 7th Environmental Action Plan 69: SCALIBUR promotes the accomplishment of the 7 th EAP’s objectives by 
diminishing environmental pollution and fighting climate change through the implementation of improved 
biowaste value chains. This inno vative biowaste management scheme valorises OFMSW and sewage sludge 
that is currently landfilled or burnt, thus achieving a significant reduction in GHG emissions, improving the 
quality of ecosystems affected by waste disposal and reducing dependence on ra w materials. The project 
results are oriented to achieve a circular economy related to biowaste management, thus making EU cities 
more sustainable and resource-efficient.   
 Alignment with Principle 10 of Rio Declaration70: As in Principle 10, SCALIBUR aims to promote awareness in the 
EU democracies and has a social dimension by: 
- Building trust in the adopted decisions that have been co-created together with the citizens themselves, 
- encouraging public awareness and knowledge related to the new valorisation ap proaches of urban 
biowaste management, 
- and involving citizens during the decision -making processes, including the development of policy 
recommendations. SCALIBUR will as well provide access to information and justice through the creation of 
a Stakeholder P latform, a user -friendly Cloud Platform tailored to the needs of different stakeholders, 
therefore promoting public engagement at all levels. This platform will be actively maintained and 
proactively updated after this project execution.  
Societal impacts 
EU 2020 strategy for the creation of growth and jobs 71: the strategy sets out its objectives in 5 target areas, 3 of 
which are contributed to by SCALIBUR, namely:  
 Employment: creation of more than 130 direct job positions as a consequence of the growth of the companies 
participating in SCALIBUR, and the indirect creation of 664,464 job positions in pilot municipalities 
 Research and Development: increased EU investment in R&D  
 Climate change and energy: diminished GHG emissions from landfilled waste degradation

2.1.4 BARRIERS, OBSTACLES AND ANY FRAMEWORK CONDITIONS 
There are some identified barriers that may affect SCALIBUR’s impact and market success. The key barriers to focus 
on are related to market acceptance of the obtained high -value biobased products, as they are produced from 
non-typical sources like waste/sewage sludge, technological innovations and yields, related to the introduction of 
innovative processes and technologies (BES, use of insects, etc.), and regulatory, related to the consumption of 
obtained products as food and feed.

A. PATH TO MARKET: ACTIVITIES DURING AND AFTER THE PROJECT 
Several steps will be planned to ensure that the foregrounds will receive the deserved attention and make a 
substantial impact on the EU  economy, society and environment. Exploitation of foregrounds will not happen only 
at the end of the project, but the actions will accompany the project during its life from ‘setting the foundations’ to 
the ‘dissemination of results’ and beyond. During the project, the knowledge developed will be communicated and 
disseminated by G!E (Dissemination Manager) through the defined activities and the use of the Stakeholder 
Platform as a key resource for maximizing the impact of the project’s results. Disseminati on is a key part of the 
exploitation strategy (leaded by G!E), following a strategy targeted for each type of stakeholder.  
SCALIBUR outcomes (see Table 3.2.1.g, Table 3.2.1.h and Table 3.2.1.i) will be propagated through dissemination 
and communication to ols such as exhibition fairs, press releases, social media, articles, scientific papers, visits to 
demonstration sites, training sessions, etc. They will be constantly updated through a feedback loop as a result of 
interaction with stakeholders and they will be available on the project’s website and Stakeholder Platform, updated 
until 5 years after project completion. The exploitation of results after the end of the project will happen through 
business plans developed under the market strategy of each product. The SCALIBUR project will make sure that the 
benefits of the demonstrated products will be recognized by the community and as consequence the products shall 
enter the market by following a business strategy dedicated to them. At that stage, participati on in events, 
especially exhibition fairs for the products will have an important role for increasing market visibility. 
Context characterization and interactions 
 Strong in -depth market and stakeholder analysis  to ascertain market potential, stakeholder wi shes and the 
desired features that no one has delivered yet. Our strong multi-disciplinary consortium has the ambition to be 
able to highlight the perspectives of the many different stakeholders (e.g., citizens, municipalities, system 
developers, policy makers and society in general) involved to provide benefits and alleviate issues for each of 
them. Their points of view will be ascertained through literature/report review, discussion with relevant 
umbrella organizations and expert interviews. By having a c lear vision of the desired features from the 
beginning we will direct the development and demonstration onto the right track early on. 
 Engagement of the stakeholder community.  Early in the development trajectory we will establish continuous 
feedback loops with the main stakeholder organizations (WP2). Details regarding the stakeholder community 
targeted are presented in Figure 2. This community will be informed, engaged and invited to major events, 
basically representing our Advisory Board. They will suppor t us in making sure that the developments are in 
line with their needs and can be considered as our first critical early adopters that could for instance assess 
limitations on a certain advancement, try samples, etc.  
 The market will be thoroughly analysed  to elucidate the potential and synergies to be exploited among other 
technologies, non -EU countries and regulatory contexts. This will then be the basis for developing business 
models and exploitation plans for each of the technologies and contexts. 
 Regulation. The implications of regulations both as limitations but also as opportunities for the biowaste origin 
biobased products market will be characterized and will serve as the basis for directing developments. 
SCALIBUR solutions and final products should be ready for global markets, and therefore, should overcome 
certain market constraints related to complying with environmental and safety standards. If during the project 
we identify aspects in the regulation that should be modified and addressed differently, we will discuss them 
with lobbying and cluster organizations and the EC representative.

Table 2.2.1a. Preliminary dissemination and communication plan 
 
Draft Plan for the dissemination and exploitation of the results (PEDR) 
We have established a draft plan for the exploitation and disse mination activities (PEDR). This plan includes 
management of these activities, policy and rules, strategy and objectives, and target groups. 
Impact, Engagement, Exploitation and Dissemination Policy and Rules:  
SCALIBUR impact will be continuously monitore d along the project. All innovation activities (including project 
impact itself, intellectual property, and exploitation and dissemination activities) will be managed by appointed 
individuals with high level of expertise. For further information, the struc ture of the consortium support 
exploitation is addressed in Section 3.2. We will organise Impact, Engagement, Communication and Dissemination 
reviews throughout the project on a 6 -month basis, in the shape of a session of the General Assembly meeting 
where all partners will present the progress of their work and the results obtained. Previous communication and 
dissemination, impact monitoring, stakeholders’ engagement, exploitation and IPR issues, etc., will be discussed 
(status, next actions, etc.) during this review, as well as the best strategy for dissemination, and monitored KPIs.  
The policy and rules for protection, exploitation and dissemination activities are based on the principles set out in 
the Annotated Model Grant Agreement (GA) and will be in compliance with the Consortium Agreement (CA), based 
on DESCA model, to be signed by all consortium partners before the signature of the GA. Main issues tackled in the 
CA will be: confidentiality, ownership of results, join ownership, background, access ri ghts, dissemination and use 
of results, in addition to the internal governance of the consortium (see section 3.2). 
Dissemination activities: expected results, target groups and exploitation routes 
Dissemination of project results will be ensured through the Stakeholder Platform (WP7), together with co-creation 
workshops, presentations in events and conferences, scientific presentations and a final multi -stakeholder event 
(WP2 and WP9). 
Engagement activities organised at neighbourhood district-level will be performed throughout the project (WP2) to 
raise awareness and involve stakeholders at multiple levels with a quadruple helix approach 72 (local, national and 
European engagement). Promising practices generated in Urban Biowasteclubs as a result will be coll ected and 
step-by-step manuals provided for further uptake in other cities and regions at national and EU level, thus 
guaranteeing project replicability.  
Specific objectives, target groups and means for the exploitation and/or dissemination of each project result will be 
defined in the PEDR (to be established in the project’s M6) and updated throughout the project in order to include 
new outcomes and updates.

Dissemination, co-creation and science educational activities 
SCALIBUR dissemination activities aim to communicate the project results and raise consumer’s awareness and 
acceptance of urban biowaste -derived products by using the quadruple helix approach. To achieve the project 
results, traditional communication and dissemination activities are not en ough. Deep engagement processes, co -
creation and participatory strategies with a social innovation approach are considered key for project success, and 
as such are part of the core activities of SCALIBUR (included in WP2, WP3 and WP9). These activities inc lude co-
creation workshops with representative stakeholders of all the levels involved in this project, “see, touch, taste” 
experiences, direct citizen participatory activities about their current behaviour regarding biowaste classification, 
neighbour recycling levels, methodologies for biowaste collection etc. Science education activities are inherent to 
the co-creation process and will be further promoted within the involved municipalities by collaborators from the 
academia, industry and research partners . In addition, a policy brief (“Recommendations for urban biowaste 
treatment”) will be presented at the European Parliament explaining the outcome of this project in order to

resource and encourage general society to implement a new scheme for ur ban biowaste management, in order to 
achieve a wide diminution of the amount which is incinerated or landfilled, while disseminating project results. The 
Dissemination and Communication Plan will ensure that all communication and dissemination activities a re 
performed to maximize SCALIBUR outreach in Europe and beyond, to all quadruple helix stakeholders with 
personalised key messages and objectives (see section 2.2.B.). More details on SCALIBUR dissemination activities 
are shown in the table below:

Platform 
The Stakeholder Platform will consist of a Cloud Platform and will be setup to allow consortium members to 
exchange information, generate discussion boards, interpretate the results, man age the consortium, the project and 
the project risks, maintain the project budget and communicate with coordinators and the European Commission. 
The Stakeholder Platform will give an overview of the project activities and progress, as well as practical ac cess to 
deliverables (marked PU) and links to the publications in open access. The Stakeholder Platform will have interactive 
user-oriented modules in order to achieve an easy access to the information for every internal or external 
stakeholder, including citizens/consumers, waste generators and managers, users of bioproducts and policy makers. 
The Stakeholder Platform will be feed with WP2 results: analysis and studies related to current urban waste 
management data, promising practices in social innovation  and existing business models, National action manuals 
for local uptake (for the integration of urban biowaste value chains into the existing local waste/wastewater 
management schemes), policy briefs and summary reports of multi -level stakeholder engagemen t (including 
gender). The Stakeholder Platform will be used as a tool for the transmission of project results and valuable 
information during and after the project, thus will allow to achieve a maximum impact at European level, aiming to 
an international r eplication of the generated innovative urban biowaste value chains and a deep engagement of all 
quadruple helix stakeholders.

publications

Principle 10 implementation. The co -creation workshops will be addressed to Biowasteclubs and stakeholders 
(including other waste generators –  HORECA/retail organic waste generators - , waste managers and policy makers) 
and will allow them to co -create the most suitable methodologies for a local (and further national and international) 
uptake of new biowaste value chains.

Project Website 
A regular project website will be created together with the Stakeholder Platform. Project website will contain 
general project information, description of the project progress and results. This website will enable a wide visibility 
and accessibility to the project information and promote and raise awareness of biobased products obtained 
through SCALIBUR valorisation processes and their benefits. 
Product portfolio 
A product portfolio including all obtained biobased products (bioplastics, biopesticides, proteins and chitin) will be 
created, once the products are characterized, in order to describe the high quality of the products and raise 
awareness and acceptance in potential end-users/consumers and waste/wastewater management industries, as well 
as in other interesting stakeholders.  
Training courses 
Academia and research organisation partners (UNIMORE, CENER) will be able to design and create training c ourses 
related to the new knowledge obtained and oriented to PhD, postdocs and industry -related professionals. Training 
courses will widely contribute to spread project knowledge and results, and to train new professionals focused on 
the innovative processes developed in SCALIBUR, thus increasing the implementation of them. 
Leaflets and 
newsletter 
A leaflet will be created at the project start and updated every year. Newsletters also will be generated throughout 
the development of SCALIBUR. Non -confidential information of SCALIBUR project, concept and results as well as 
socio-economic impact will be shared. The associated strategic dissemination objective is to increase the awareness 
of stakeholders, including general public about the project and to promote  the use of Stakeholder Platform and 
project website, as well as achieve an involvement of the different target audiences in the Stakeholder Platform.

Preparing exploitation during development 
Many R&D project foregrounds enter the death- valley because it is not clear who i s the responsible/can benefit 
from its exploitation and there are not solid business models or plans for exploitation and commercialization. This 
will not happen in SCALIBUR. Indeed, there is a strong focus on the needed steps for reaching the market: 
 Competence assessment and matching of developments with customer/market needs . One of the most 
complex aspects when carrying out innovation is to find a great match between what are the desired and the 
delivered features/benefits. Therefore, as soon as the for egrounds are identified we will perform a SWOT 
analysis capable of highlighting extraordinary features and limitations. This will then support the Fit 
Assessment, basically the matching between the needs and the delivered features. 
 Protection of IPR and management of foregrounds. As soon as a foreground is identified, the involved partners 
with the support of G!E will start discussing agreements. Additionally, before dissemination starts, we will 
perform patent search, IPR protection and multilateral agreem ents among partners involved. Only after an 
innovation is fully protected and agreements (among consortium partners but also with external ones) are 
reached dissemination and commercialization will occur. The manager assigned for each foreground will 
receive great support by the exploitation expert (G!E) along all the steps. 
 Risk assessment and mitigation plan will be detailed to avoid undermining the full exploitation potential of the 
developments. Our project will take all the required steps to identify the risks (technical, economic, 
environmental, and social), define preventive and mitigation measures with different ambitions and scopes 
depending on the severity of the expected damage. The risk analysis will be periodically revised to adapt to the 
fast-changing nature of the topics involved.

models’ implementation and environmental impact,

Entering the market 
During SCALIBUR, the following actions to ensure the full exploitation of project results will be undertaken:  
 Solid exploitation plan and business models based on past experiences, stakeholder analysis and discussion 
among interes ted partners and relevant organizations will define appropriate business cases for each 
development and context. Draft exploitation plans and preliminary business models are already identified and 
will be optimized as soon as the features of the foregrounds are clearly assessed.  
 All the steps performed before, especially regarding market potential, the results from the demonstration and 
the 
feedback from the stakeholder community should ensure that our foregrounds will be well positioned to 
strongly enter the market. Commercialization and market uptake will be defined with ad -hoc discussion 
between technical, financial and marketing staff among the consortium supported by the expertise of the 
exploitation partner (G!E). Industrial partners will be our first , very critical and demanding clients that will help 
us in optimizing the products and clearly identifying excellence and limitations. The solidity of the results will 
allow the IP owners to strengthen their market position, which for the key technology pr oviders involved has a 
strong focus on internationalization. 
 Dissemination for market uptake will take part initially via the products portfolio and their application through 
the demonstration sites. Technology performance, results and outcomes will be fol lowed-up throughout the 
project targeting specific audiences with contribution from the consortium partners in order to incorporate 
feedback from stakeholders. This will be done mainly through the participation in conferences, webinars, 
training courses, workshops and roundtables in events, e.g. International Society of Electrochemistry (ISE) 
Annual Meeting, the Circular Economy European Summit, among others. Events will take part in collaboration 
with major associations, involving also regulatory bodies at EU and national levels. Once the business models 
are mature enough, we will pursue participation in sectorial fairs related to the bioproducts obtained, such as 
ECOFIRA (ES), IFAT or World Biogas Expo, where the SCALIBUR processes and biobased products ca n be 
introduced to the market. In addition, many of the involved organizations are leaders in their fields and have 
strong and established network with universities, regulatory bodies and the other stakeholders. 
A preliminary 
dissemination and communication plan is shown in Table 2.2.1.a, Table 3.2.1.d and in the next pages. 
 Training. It is necessary to provide confidence to the final users in the reliability and benefits of the biobased 
solutions provided. The successful implementation of SCALIBUR processes and bio -products in the DSs will 
allow the creation of use cases dedicated to training and knowledge exchange to promote the use of scalable 
technologies for urban biowaste recovery and valorisation. Interaction with municipalities, waste managers, 
academia, students, construction and engineering sector professionals (installers, chemical and industrial 
engineers, and end user companies) and also the general public, is foreseen in the shape of papers, trainings 
courses, webinars and visits to the DSs.  
 From TRL 6 to TRL 9. The project results are pre-competitive, so at least a further 3-year period will be required 
to turn them into commercial products (TRL 9). For this purpose, the PPIF will achieve the following  objectives: 
(1) to keep the momentum with exploitation, communication and dissemination over a sufficient period of 
time after the project’s completion in order to fully achieve the desired project impact, and (2) to investigate 
opportunities for follow-up activities. Continuous interactions with end users, Europe research community, and 
other relevant stakeholders such as EC will be targeted 
To reach the potential market, several partners will invest in technology, further adaptation of manufacturing 
processes, sales channels, marketing, etc. after the end of SCALIBUR. The source of financing might be own 
company funds or by requesting additional funding from regional/national/European programmes, such as 
H2020, 
SPIRE, BBI calls, Structural funds and National and regional calls.

B. PRELIMINARY EXPLOITATION AND BUSINESS PLANS 
Market estimations for the new high-value biobased products 
A potential target to achieve 8% of the total market by 5 years after project conclusion and increasing the share in 
the following years, gives the industrial partners of SCALIBUR a possible starting market of around 32,270 M€. 
Thanks to its high performance, the need to use biowaste using a cascading approach, and the valorisation of a 
waste into a feedstock, SCALIBUR solutions are likely to be deployed by biowaste managers and by final producers. 
To allow the deployment biobased products from biowaste and the increase of European competitiveness in this 
field, the correct collection and logistics, followed by replacement of current landfilling and biometanization of 
biowaste is an unavoidable necessity. Biobased processes using biowastes are already being studied, but 
development is often still in the R&D stage and the performance has not yet been demonstrated on pilot or pre -
industrial scale involving citizen and municipal ities role from the very beginning. To successfully approach the 
demonstration of new process technologies on an industrial pilot plant scale broad knowledge is needed from all 
steps of the value chain, including technical but also social concerns such as citizen behaviours in the collection or 
consumer acceptance of final biobased products.  
SCALIBUR creates the opportunity of sharing both knowledge and costs between the consortium companies from 
different value chains and sectors following an open innovation approach within a wide range of partners and 
noteworthy advisors. The project partners will gain important additional insights in the field with a large potential 
for market application. This will permit the SCALIBUR consortium to develop processes tha t the partners alone 
would not be able to achieve on their own. The demonstration and application of novel integrated technologies 
among the consortium partners will not only facilitate and accelerate their adaption, transfer and take up, but also 
deepen the understanding of the new biowaste valorisation processes and allow an overall integration of needed 
knowledge within the consortium.  
Final products Market potential 
Bioplastics & biopolymers market potential 2,660 million USD73 (globally, 2015) 
Biobased pesticides market potential 718 million USD74 (globally, 2016) 
Biobased feed market potential 400,000 million USD75 (globally, 2016) 
Table 3.2.1f. Market potential of SCALIBUR’s final biobased products 
Proposed measures to achieve the expected impact of the project: Exploitation plan 
 Exploitation team.  The full exploitation value chain is available in the project to properly ensure an efficient 
exploitation of the results. SCALIBUR will appoint an Exploitation Manager (G!E), to properly manage the 
exploitation of project results (see Section 3.2.2). Exploitation rights and specific agreements between partners 
will be taken into account in the consortium agreement).  
 Exploitation strategy of all the partners. The competitiveness of organizations is increasingly depending on their 
ability to collaborate in networks, and for such collaborations (knowledge -based ones), strong IPR management 
is a prerequisite for efficient trade and transfer of IPR and technology. Detailed IPR rules and protection will be 
described in the Consortium Agreement. The adequate treatment of IPR should help the consortium to 
maximize the returns from research and investments, by selecting the best way to prevent the innovation being 
attacked by competitors. It should also be regarded in the context of appropriation of the innovation benefits. 
 Exploitation of the project results  will take place by the industrial partners as well as by transferring knowledge 
on valorization routes of biowastes to companies specialized in the field, or to  municipalities and biowaste 
managers, on the basis of non- exclusive licenses on the IPR generated during the project. A summary of the 
main outcomes that will be generated along the project as well as the way they will be protected is presented 
hereafter. However, it has to be noted that in terms of direct exploitation of SCALIBUR outcomes, it is expected 
that at the end of the project, all the different patents generated will be fully owned by consortium members 
and licensed or sold to end -users. The IPR & Exploitation manager of the project will carefully take care for the 
IP generated and the way it might be transferred at the end of the project. It must be noted that the knowledge 
and experience generated in SCALIBUR will benefit all partners and also the preliminary exploitation strategy for 
each partner.  
Detailed business plans for each final biobased product and new technology/process will be developed in WP10, 
and annexed to the PEDR, in order to provide details on how the project’s results will be used in commercial

business models drafted at this stage are based on two different strategies:

On the other hand, Research Centres and Academic partners will benefit mainly in terms of: 
 Advancement of knowledge on  the technological aspects linked to the SCALIBUR technological innovations, 
particularly on: biowaste characteristics and management, application of innovative integration concepts in 
hydrolysis and fermentation, insects feeding and extraction, bioelectro chemical solutions, novel bioproducts 
using biowaste, modelling and simulation of complex industrial processes, measurement procedures, etc.  
 Technology transfer of novel solutions, from lab-based prototypes and tests to pilot devices; 
 Exposure to relevant industrial counterparts, giving them the possibility to measure the point of view of final 
users of new strategies and technological solutions;  
 Development and provision of new services and consultancies to industry and end-users of SCALIBUR.  
 Beneficial effects on scientific productivity in terms of world ranking and scientific publications.  
 The knowledge developed with other partners will be used for teaching activities both for undergraduate and 
graduate students as well as doctoral, in Process Technology, Chemistry, Bio Science…

C. KNOWLEDGE MANAGEMENT AND PROTECTION 
Knowledge and innovation management: RRI methodologies that have been designed by consortium members and 
specifically adapted for the project SCALIBUR will be tested and validated to co -create and co-design strategies for 
urban biowaste valorisation value chains and business models that can be further replicated, standardised and 
eventually influence related waste and food regulations. Therefore, new knowledge is expected to be generated 
and is thus susceptible to being protected. Our consortium will identify all project outco mes (new knowledge, new 
technological solutions, any data or business information) from the beginning until the end of the project (see 
Table 3.2.1.g, Table 3.2.1.h and Table 3.2.1.i), and establish, together with the partner(s) who generated the result, 
the most appropriate strategy to protect (IP, non -disclosure…), exploit (further research project as background, 
commercial agreements…; see Table 3.2.1.j) and disseminate (open access publications, international conferences, 
website, etc.) a result. The IP R & Exploitation Manager will be the responsible for coordinating actions related to 
the IPR management. The Consortium Agreement already sets the basic rules to manage ownership and access to 
key knowledge (IPR, research data, etc.) by referring to the terms and conditions of the GA, Annex II about 
ownership of background information and results and mutual granting of Access Rights. 
Open Access policy and measures: In a wider context of knowledge management, dissemination and exploitation 
activities, we will ensure compliance with Horizon 2020 rules regarding Open Access (OA) to scientific literature, by 
making freely accessible online any scientific publication for free under the scope of the project. Each beneficiary 
will choose the most suitable approach  (either “green” OA or “gold” OA) to peer -reviewed scientific publications 
that might result from the project. The publisher will be chosen amongst those who respect both the authors’ 
interests and accept the terms of open access publication (with an embargo period). Partners will use an open access 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
39 
   
repository, connected to the tools proposed by the EC (e.g. open AIRE), in order to grant access to the publications 
and a bibliographic metadata in standard format, including the information requested by the EC. 
Data collection and management: SCALIBUR project will provide access to project data through the Stakeholder 
Platform, a Cloud Platform accessible from the web and mobile devices, and tailored to different levels of internal 
and external stakeholders with a user -friendly interface. SCALIBUR tools (participatory, interactive, online, co -
creation and citizen science tools) will empower citizens/waste generators at all levels not only to access the data, 
but also to become data generators. Project data will be generated through the Urban Biowasteclubs, which will 
enable actors to actively and efficiently work together, by organizing workshops where all consortium members will 
be present. During these workshops, the following topics will be addressed and discu ssed about: 
(1) citizen 
behaviour changes regarding acceptance of urba -biowaste products; (2) new trends and promising practices in 
each municipality; (3) barriers and opportunities to enable the adoption of new policies, profitable business models 
and soc ial innovation activities; (4) how to adapt, develop and uptake new profitable business models; and (5) 
design-thinking workshops. Generated data during these workshops will feed the Stakeholder Platform and will be 
accessible to all represented actors, pr operly managed by the project members and coordinated by each manager 
depending of the related area (Impact, Engagement and RRI, IPR and Exploitation, Communication and 
Dissemination or Scientific area). All information about the do’s and don’ts regarding the full integration of the 
upgraded urban biowaste value chain into the existing local waste/wastewater management schemes, will be 
integrated into the stakeholder platform. This way we will provide transparency and make data available for waste 
generators, since they are key actors who provide the new waste fractions used during the innovative treatment 
processes here developed.  
Regulatory issues: All the tasks of the project will be designed and executed according to EU and national 
legislation, guideli nes and recommendations which prove often to be sketchy. The scientific and regulatory 
framework on by -products, waste and urban biowaste management will be taken into account throughout the 
project, as well as provisions and case law on the legal status o f sewage sludge and its use in agriculture. The EU 
Regulations on plant protection and any relevant provision that could help in understanding the legal status of 
biopesticides will be considered (lacking both a definition and a specific regulation on this  theme). The regulatory 
framework for bioplastics and materials intended to come in contact with food will also be taken into account. 
Provisions on food, feed, rearing and animal welfare will be considered too. 
2.2.1 COMMUNICATION ACTIVITIES 
SCALIBUR is a n interdisciplinary project which involves quadruple helix stakeholders. This fact is reflected in the 
communication activities in order to maximize visibility, support successful exploitation and impact generation and 
to establish continuity for the proje ct. According to Article 38 of the H2020 Grant Agreement, the beneficiaries 
“must promote the action and its results, by providing targeted information to multiple audiences (including the 
media and the public) in a strategic and effective manner”.  The communication activities of SCALIBUR will focus on 
ensuring a smooth information flow between the project partners and all relevant quadruple helix stakeholders 
and on raising awareness of the project activities and key results in a targeted and cost- efficient manner. The 
communication activities will be performed mainly via Stakeholder Platform (WP7), complemented with different 
media, forums and the consortium members’ extensive networks. These activities are defined in detail in WP9. 
The project will have a highly professional communication program running alongside the other work packages 
throughout the project, which will be defined in the Communication and Dissemination Plan. Core tools such as 
website, internal web portal, guidelines and generated susta inable business plans will be created by the 
consortium’s expert partners and will be used to build up platform for all consortium members to collaborate, 
share and transmit impactful communications. This platform (Stakeholder Platform) will serve as a tool to maximize 
the impact of communication actions. Therefore, this tool will generate and grant access to all relevant data (which 
will be open data), new sustainable business models for the project’s further replication, training and educational 
information, and project’s events and conferences. In essence, the SCALIBUR’s Stakeholder Platform will thus be a 
key tool that will allow, on the one hand to increase transparency, provide data and perform co -creation actions 
and engagement, and on the other hand to maximize the successful dissemination of project results. This will 
guarantee both the necessary continuous engagement actions and the interaction of all stakeholders involved.  
The Communication & Dissemination Manager will pay special attention to avo id common mistakes in 
communication (communicate without identifying the target audience, focus on the medium and not message, 
etc.). For each target audience, a distinct communication strategy using targeted messages, appropriate means and 
language will be set up with the aim of creating an innovative and replicable urban biowaste management scheme 
among quadruple helix stakeholders at local, national and European level; promoting the uptake of RRI actions and 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
40 
   
contributing to increase sustainability. The s pecific communication and dissemination objectives for each 
stakeholder group are: 
 Citizens and consumers: increase understanding & changing behaviour regarding collection and use of urban 
biowaste, increase acceptance of urban biowaste-derived products, reduce non-recycled biowaste rates  
 Municipalities: support the adoption of new policies (incl. logistic models), new profitable business models and 
social innovation initiatives. Identify areas of improvement in urban biowaste selective collection schemes.  
 Business and local service providers (water, energy, waste): support in developing, testing & replicating new 
profitable business models along the entire urban biowaste value chain 
 Policy makers: Pro-actively engage national and European policy representatives in the Urban Biowaste Clubs, 
participation in relevant conferences, fairs and policy dialogues, present the policy brief “recommendations 
for urban biowaste management” at the European Parliament. From the beginning of the project, SCALIBUR 
will foster the dialogue on the European level and involve policy representatives in order to create momentum 
for further uptake (and investment) of the urban biowaste initiatives. 
To reach our target audiences and communicate SCALIBUR key messages, our communication tools will be: 
 SCALIBUR Stakeholder Platform  – an interactive, tailored and user -friendly platform to compile all the 
information gathered and co -created related to the implementation of the innovative urban biowaste value 
chains (including new business models, results from the co-creation workshops, relevant news, partial and final 
open access results, media, regulatory aspects, action manuals (national/international replicability step-by-step 
manuals), and other relevant content generated as a consequence of SCALIBUR). The Stakeholder Platform will 
be accessible to all internal (project members, advisory board) and external (advocacy and policy groups, 
citizens, waste managers, waste generators, sectorial associations, etc.) stakeholders. 
 SCALIBUR dedicated social campaign : Social media, including short videos of SCALIBUR’s results (YouTube, 
Twitter, Facebook and LinkedIn) will be actively used to engage society at large and network with other EU 
related projects. E-mail campaigns based on the website registrations and RSS service will be performed.  
 SCALIBUR branding: project image, leaflets and other communication materials. 
 SCALIBUR newsletter: main news and results published in a 6 -monthly newsletter (plus press releases): waste 
management and valori sation related news, news on Urban Biowasteclubs, news from related waste 
management, biomaterials and circular economy projects, and other dissemination announcements. To be 
distributed in electronic version through mailing lists. 
 Events: presentation of project’s results in key sectorial events, as shown in Table 3.2.1.b. 
 Guided visits to DSs and the Best Performing Territory : The project will include scheduled visits for the 
Biowasteclubs representatives to demo plants where the SCALIBUR results will be validated: Las Dehesas 
(Madrid, ES) and the demo plant in Ostrava, CZ, as well as visits to Lund. The guided visits will have an 
educational purpose and will serve as an important communication channel for the citizenship, supporting the 
awareness raising and acceptance of biobased products obtained. 
 European Commission Communication channels: We will also use EC services to communicate largely on our 
project, its results and events: CORDIS News, CORDIS Wire, European Commission’s newsletters, EC’s event 
pages, the Europa website, the EU interactive platform for dialogue and discussion. This will be done in close 
coordination with our project officer and allow to reach a Europe-wide “qualified” audience. 
A set of success indicators will be put in place thus setting the basis for verifying whether the communication 
objectives have been met. For the online communication and dissemination data, a Google Analytics account will 
be set up linked to the proje ct Stakeholder Platform/project website whilst for all other social media, the available 
free analytics tool will be used (Facebook Insights, Twitter Analytics, etc.)

SECTION 3: IMPLEMENTATION
3.1 WORK PLAN —  WORK PACKAGES, DELIVERABLES  
 
OVERALL STRUCTURE OF THE WORK PLAN 
A competitive work p lan has been created in order to deliver on the objectives of the SCALIBUR project, which is 
divided into 10 WPs, subsequently divided further into working tasks. This project is coordinated by ITENE; 
however, each WP and task has a leader that is responsible for progress and communication of results. The work to 
be carried out in SCALIBUR is structured considering three different types of activities: 
Implementation (WP2-WP7; to develop and integrate urban biowaste valorisation approaches on a city level ), 
Validation (WP8; to check SCALIBUR approach from a technical, environmental, economic and social point of view), 
and Market Launch (WP9-10; to boost the introduction of SCALIBUR approach in Europe). Considering this 
approach, the project has been structured in ten WPs briefly explained. 
WP1 Management, to lead the project towards the desired objectives. WP2 Stakeholder engagement, to increase 
quantity and improve quality of organic fraction collected. WP3 collection and pretreatment, to adapt quality of 
organic fraction to the subsequent valorization processes. WP4 biochemical conversion of OFMSW , to obtain 
biopolyesters and biopesticides ; WP5 biological transformation biowaste from HORECA, to obtain proteins, lipids 
and chitin. WP6 biochemical and bioelectrochemical transformation of USS, to obtain chemicals (alcohols and acids) 
and bioplastics (PHBV). WP7 Scalibur Biowaste platform , to obtain a cloud architecture tool to connect all 
stakeholders in the value chain. WP8 Sustainability and safety analysis; to evaluate economic, social, environmental, 
regulatory aspects as well as the risks associated to substances obtained in the project. WP9 Dissemination, 
communication and training; to transmit the results of the project within related stakeholders. WP10 Exploitation 
and IPR management, to manage the exploitation of SCALIBUR results transferring the R&D performers to industrial 
and public sector end-users. 
Interconnectivity of the work packages is displayed in the Pert diagram followed by the Gantt chart. Sub sequently, 
each working package and working task is described in detail.

Objectives 
 To ensure smooth collaboration and apply personalised tools for efficient implementation of activities, decision making and steering 
 To anticipate, monitor and assess project progress vs. work plan and initiating if necessary prompt corrective actions  
 To assure timely reporting and communication with the project officer and the EC

Description of work (underlined partner = Task Leader) 
Task 1.1: Administrative, Financial, Contractual, Legal Management (Partners Involved: ITENE) – M01-M48 
The Project Coordinator ITENE will lead the global project coordination and will be responsible for its tasks listed in the Grant Agreement  and 
the Consortium Agreement, both among the partners and with respect to the EC. The Coordinator will be mainly in charge of: 
 Establishing a Consortium Agreement prior to the project official starting date based on the DESCA H2020 model.76    
 Requesting and reviewing any reports, documents or information required by the EC and verifying their quality, completeness a nd 
correctness before passing them on to the EC. 
 Appropriate and timely allocating of EC grant to partners upon Grant Agreement and General Assembly (GA) decisions. Keeping t he 
records of the distribution of grant and informing the EC in due time. 
 Follow-up of management actions, project correspondence and day-to-day demands from partners. 
 Designing and maintaining partner specific templates (financial, technical, IPR, dissemination, exploitation, innovation, impact...)  
 Based on GA decisions, implementing changes in grant agreement for contractual amendment request. 
 Financial reporting: The Coordinator will consolidate and analyse financial data (evert 6M) to compare the actual costs vs. budget figures 
and anticipate any deviations (over or under consumption).  Coordinator will notify the due dates and provide support for the 
completion of the Periodic financial reports (and certificates on financial statements if relevant). Coordinator will: [1] pay attention that 
EC rules are respected for cost reporting on the basi s of the information provided by the partners; [2] check the quality (completeness, 
correctness, format...) of information from all partners and review all individual financial statements to ensure consistency  with the 
planned and real technical tasks and to verify each partners’ engagement; [3] take care of the reporting related to EC grant allocation. 
 Progress reporting: The Coordinator will ensure an efficient organization of Periodic activity reporting. In addition to the official Periodic 
reports, 6-monthly interim WP reports will be produced with contribution from the WP leaders. 
Task 1.2: Data Management Plan (Partners Involved: ITENE, All) – M01 – M48 
To analyse the main elements of the data management policy with regard to the datasets generated by the project. The DMP will be 
generated at the start of SCALIBUR and then evolve during the lifespan of the project. Data management will be a fixed agenda  item at all 
management meetings. The DMP will consider all the data the project will generate and use  and will detail whether and how it will be used, 
exploited or made accessible for verification and re-use; how and under what conditions it will be curated, preserved and shared; and how it 
will be interoperable with regard to specific quality standards. 
Task 1.3: Internal Communication (Partners Involved: ITENE, G!E, CSCP) – M06 – M48 
 The Coordinator will promote efficient communication flows within the consortium. 
 Ensure that each partner is well informed of the project progress, understands its role and  contractual obligations in the project, and is 
aware of the requests and information from the EC.  Documents will be shared on a secured collaborative internet platform provided 
and updated by coordinator for knowledge management, on-line reporting and information exchange, as well as email lists. 
 Prepare, execute and post-process all official project meetings (tasks: agendas, invitations, logistics together with the host, preparation, 
distribution and archiving of materials, minutes and action lists). 
 Chair both the Executive Board meetings and General Assembly, every six months. 
 Have a strategic role on both meetings preparation. In addition, regular technical meetings will be organized by the WP Leaders on WP 
level on project and inter-WP levels. 
Task 1.4: Quality and Risk Management (Partners Involved: ITENE, All) -  M1 – M48 
The Coordinator will set  a quality management policy validated by the GA covering all aspects related to practical management (document 
exchanges & internal workflows) of the project and adressing: project SWOT, technical and non -technical risk management incl. critical path 
of t he project and associated contingency plans, communication and quality control activities, gender, societal and ethical issue s. For 
instance, it will clearly state internal processes related to standards of documents, proof - reading, validation workflow fo r the approval of 
deliverables, reports, dissemination, exploitation and IPR items, etc. Key indicators will also be proposed to evaluate the p erformance of the 
project and its impact. 
Deliverables

D1.2: Data Management Plan (ITENE; M6).  
D1.3: Quality and Risk management plan (M9, ITENE).

Objectives 
 Identify and engage key European quadruple helix stakeholders (at the local, national and EU level; objective: at least 100 
stakeholders), covering the whole value chain of  organic waste, and involve them in participatory and co -creation actions, to support 
the integration of urban biowaste valorisation approaches on a city level within each of the demo regions, allowing for social innovation 
and increased consumer awareness and acceptance of urban biowaste-derived products  
 Analyse the current value chain of urban biowaste in the best performing territory (identification of best practices and road map 
definition for replicability) and in the pilot cities (Madrid, Albano (LAZIO), Kozani (CLUBE)) 
 Identify the main barriers (political, economic, social, environmental and legal) for the implementation of urban biowaste va lorisation 
in an integrated way on city level 
 Generate the knowledge to be implemented in technological develop ment in WP3 on collection, transport, sorting and pretreatment 
with a view to improve quantity and quality of OMSW: Madrid (quantity 85%, quality 95% after the pilot), Albano (quantity 90%, quality 
97% after the pilot), Kozani (quantity 50%, quality 95% after the pilot), Europe in general (quantity 85%, quality 95% in 2030) 
Task 2.1 Stakeholder Identification, Data analysis and Engagement Plan (M1 -M48). Partners Involved: CSCP, FCC, VISUM, ITENE, UNIMORE, 
ZITIES, LAZIO, CLUBE 
The first task aims at developing a detailed Stakeholder Engagement Plan, building upon the following elements:   
Subtask 2.1.1 Tailored stakeholder analysis (CSCP, CLUBE, LAZIO, FCC): Based on the already existing work and networks in the 3 pilot cities, 
CSCP and the local partners wi ll be able to identify and map all relevant actors operating in the demonstrators’ regions, including 
local&regional authorities, waste generators (including HORECA, supermarkets and citizens), waste collection companies, waste /wastewater 
management utilities, energy providers, (biobased) industries, the scientific community, local SMEs, and local communities. The outcome will 
be a list of central actors combined with a detailed analysis of their operational settings, relationships, interests and mot ivations for each 
demo region. Additional information will be collected through direct exchange with the municipalities in each pilot, as well as key 
stakeholders in the local communities, who will help in the development of the engagement plan at local level.  
Subtask 2.1.2. Baseline analysis (ITENE, CLUBE, LAZIO, CSCP, Madrid, Lund): A baseline analysis of existing urban biowaste management for  
each pilot city participating (Madrid [ES], Albano [IT] and Kozani [GR]) with barriers and opportunities areas will be carried out to find out 
data on consumption behaviour and urban waste manangement. Data such as recycling rates, urban biowaste fractions separated, 
management routes, citizen engagement, etc., will help to identify gaps and inconveniences in their current  collection systems. Lund 
municipality (SE) will be the benchmark territory because of its high level of collection ( 98% for the whole city). B est practices in the 
selective collection of OFMSW and HORECA biowaste will be identified to be implemented in th e city pilots in WP2&3.  Visits to the four 
cities (Lund, Madrid, Albano and Kozani) will be requested to collect all the information ( CLUBE, LAZIO and Madrid will travel to the best 
performing territory as well), and projects from other regions across Europe and successful urban waste management plan will be also studied. 
A comparison and matching of the current data across the 3 pilot municipalities and the best performing territory is foreseen to assess 
initiatives that could be taken up where and inform necessary actions. This will provide the baseline for future analysis of the project actions 
results. 
As a result of the above activities, an Engagement Plan tailored for each municipality participating in the pilots, will be p roduced as well as 
an identification of best practises to be implemented in the pilot cities in WP3. 
Task 2.2: Local Stakeholder Engagement, Co -Creation and Participatory Actions (M7 -M44). Partners Involved: CSCP, ITENE, Madrid, LAZIO, 
CLUBE 
Subtask 2.2.1 Co-creation & local engagement process: Urban Biowasteclubs will be set-up for each of the demonstration areas, as the main 
tool for active engagement, which will comprise circa 16 to 20 pre -identified quadruple helix stakeholders at a local level. All Biowasteclub 
activities will be shaped according to a participatory approach, enabling actors to actively and efficiently work together, share information, 
and co-create knowledge. Meetings will happen regularly (at least 2 meetings per year per club) in physical spaces (e.g. public bui ldings, 
waste treatment facilities or alike) provided by the municipalities or involved stakeholders in the neighbourhoods participating in the pilots. 
To ensure that the citizens’ perspectives are well represented, the project will invite and/or nominate “local champions” to participate in the 
Biowasteclubs. “Local champions” are citizens known in the local communities already very active locally on the topics of sus tainability, 
neighbourhood improvement, social innovation, etc. These champions will act as  local ambassadors that facilitate the uptake of the project 
activities by further citizens. The project will support them both in motivating and engaging their personal local networks ( e.g. in their 
schools/ at work, friends+family+neighbourhood, etc.), but also in reaching a wider local audience (e.g. through social media, short footages 
in local news, and means such as meeting rooms and communication materials, actions in close collaboration with WP9). 
With a particular focus on the local context of each of the participating municipalities, the Urban Biowasteclubs meetings will aim to: 
 discuss how to increase and motivate understanding & changing behaviour regarding collection and use, acceptance of urban biowaste-
derived products (relevant for group Consumers / citizens) 
 discuss how to adapt, develop and uptake the new profitable business models tested in WP4 -6 along the entire urban biowaste value 
chain (relevant for business stakeholders), to define how they could be fully integrated into the existing l ocal waste/ wastewater 
management schemes of each municipality involved in the pilots (WP4-WP6) and to start taking the relevant steps.   
 discuss the role and need to adopt new policies (including logistic models), and to implement social innovation initia tives, in order to 
overcome specific barriers and benefit from opportunity areas for the implementation of an integrated system innovation approach  
(relevant for group Municipalities and consumers / citizens)

 identify milestones and define a roadmap for country wide-local uptake as basis for National action manuals (see T2.3).  
Further engagement activities, involving wider groups of stakeholders  and informing the collaborative activities include: i) discussing in 
interactive citizens’ workshops their expectations/needs/questions about waste collection and use of biowaste products. The events will take 
place back-to-back with other local activities in public spaces (at least 1/yr·pilot). ii) conduct interactive online questionnaires among citizens 
of the respective municipality, made available thorugh the SCALIBUR stakeholder platform. iii) Engaging representatives of successful urban 
initiatives and promising practises from other municipalities, regions or countries as external speakers or advisors in the Biowasteclubs 
The results of these activities will be captured both in short outcome-reports and handbooks, as well as translated into different online formats 
(i.e. news items, interactive infographics), in order to support their uptake, in collaboration with WP9 actions and the partnering municipalities. 
Guidelines for replicability of the co-created business models in other municipalities at national and European level will be generated. 
Subtask 2.2.2 Participatory actions: To lift the stakeholder engagement on the next level, SCALIBUR aims to also take participatory actions to 
test and demonstrate pathways to support the integration of the urban biowaste valorisation approaches on a city level: 
 Start taking first steps to fully integrate the business models (=of the upgraded urban biowaste value chain) tested in WP4 -6 into the 
existing local waste/wastewater management schemes of each municipality involved in the pilots (WP4-WP6)  
 To support the above, and  based on the results of T2.1 and T2.2.1, the member s of the Biowasteclubs and the “local champions” will 
select the social innovation and enhancing active participation of citizens in urban biowaste collection ideas that fit most to their local 
contexts and take next steps to adapt / develop / scale-up them in their specific context. 
 Informed by the baseline analysis (2.1.2) on lifestyle trends and behaviour change, corresponding "See, Touch, Taste" experiences will 
be offered in framework of a neighbourhood activities (e.g. as cooperation with supermarkets , an engaging presentation back -to-back 
at existing citizen -events, or walking tours through the city exploring innovative start -ups, restaurants etc.) in order to increase 
consumers / citizens awareness and acceptance of urban biowaste-derived products. 
Task 2.3:  National & European Stakeholder Engagement (M24-M44). Partners Involved: CSCP, Madrid, ITENE, LAZIO, CLUBE 
Several national and European stakeholder engagement activities are foreseen to facilitate project replicability in other reg ions and 
countries, in close relationship with engagement actions described in WP9:  
 Biowasteclubs champions will be encouraged to act as national biowaste -ambassadors. Supported by CSCP and G!E, they will share 
their experiences with and engage their respective network s outside the pilot cities (e.g. representatives from pilot municipalities will 
engage neighbouring cities, service providers (waste, wastewater, energy) to implement the pilots in different cities, civil society 
representatives will engage their national organisations, citizens can share their experiences through the SCALIBUR stakeholder 
platform, etc.). 
 National action manuals for local uptake: experiences of the Biowasteclubs will be collected in a step -by-step manual that will allow an 
easy uptake in other cities and regions. CSCP, FCC, LAZIO and CLUBE will encourage national policy to foster the uptake in other regions 
and cities. The Scalibur -Biowasteclubs could then act in an advisory role as “helpdesks” for similar nationally funded initiatives beyon d 
the official project duration.  
Task 2.4: Evaluation of SCALIBUR multi -level engagement plan and activities, including gender (M20 -M48). Partners Involved: CSCP, VISUM, 
ITENE, Madrid, LAZIO, CLUBE 
The objective of the impact assessment and evaluation wil l be to assess, firstly, whether the perception of citizens on urban biowaste as a 
local resource has improved and citizens’ participation in its separate collection has increased thanks to social innovation initiatives and 
secondly, to assess whether the  consumer acceptance of urban biowaste-derived products, including food and feed ingredients, has indeed 
improved. These objectives shall be reached:  
 data collected in WP2 and WP3 (available through the SCALIBUR stakeholder platform) will allow to compare the baseline of citizens’ 
behaviour regarding waste in the 3 participating municipalities before, during and after the Scalibur engagement activities.  
 ex-ante & ex-post surveys of engaged citizens on collection & separation behaviour (combined with qualitative interviews of local champions).  
 all implementing activities (T2.2) will include both direct feedback mechanism (e.g. a short interactive poll after the “see,  touch, taste” 
experiences), as well as a comparative analysis of the participation and enga gement across time (e.g. how many people participate in 
the “experiences”, how many of those participants engage further afterwards (e.g. in the online platform, in setting up local  networks 
or similar), which (online) activities trigger larger discussions and follow-up, etc. 
 All the SCALIBUR engagement activities and the stakeholder platform will be designed to be gender inclusive, and gender balan ce will 
be sought through all project actions. A gender analysis with regard to engagement and participation i n each municipality will be made 
in M24&M48, allowing for introducing corrective measures in case that gender inclusiveness is not being achieved by M24. 
 Other impact indicators for quadruple helix stakeholders, including policy impacts, will be defined and analysed also in M24 and M48 to 
allow for corrective actions and maximization of project impact. The Public Engement MORRI indicators will be used ( D3.2 Metrics and 
indicators of Responsible Research and Innovation, H2020 MORRI project, December 2015).
