Objectives 
 Improving the qual ity and increasing the quantity of urban biowaste (OFMSW and HORECA) selectively collected in the pilots by 
implementing best practices to ensure a constant feedstock of biowaste materials with uniform quality  
 Physical and chemical characterisation and pr e-treatment of the OFMSW fractions, HORECA waste and sewage sludge UWWTP for 
subsequent treatment, optimization of the homogenization processes and for producing optimal mixtures for production of high -value 
products with the new processing technologies (WP4-WP6) 
 Definition of the pre-treatment criteria for each urban biowaste (sorting, stabilization, drying, etc.) 
 Stablishing the thresholds of composition of this waste streams for a feasible and successful valorisation 
Task 3.1: Improved methods for selective collection of urban biowaste (M6 – M44). Partners Involved: ITENE, CSCP, FCC, LAZIO, Madrid, CLUBE, 
Lund 
Sewage sludge is excluded from this task because it is automatically collected at UWWTP. 
Subtask 3.1.1. Improved selective collection of OFMSW (ITENE, FCC, CSCP, Madrid, LAZIO, CLUBE): ITENE, CSCP and FCC will seek for high-level 
technical best practices aimed to reach best quality and quantity of selective collected OFMSW. 
 Containerisation and deposit of the OFMSW (ITENE): Depot systems like bring -banks and door-to-door systems, as well as the different 
container systems will be analysed. 
 Communication and awareness of the citizens about OFMSW (CSCP): In cooperation with WP2, the main barriers to the collection and 
deposit of the biowaste will be checked, and technical solutions will be proposed. 
 Incentives to increase OFMSW collection (FCC): economic incentives like pay- as-you-throw (PAYT) methods, reduced taxation systems 
and the like will be analysed, which will allow for social innovation. 
Subtask 3.1.2. Improved selective collection of HORECA waste  (ITENE, FCC, CSCP, Madrid, LAZIO, CLUBE): Containerisation, communication, 
and incentives will be tackled with special focus on HORECA and the technical needs to separate high added value fractions be cause of their 
lower degree of contamination as compared to households. Together with WP2, where baseline values will be collected, technical barriers for 
best selective collection of HORECA waste will be analysed for the municipalities of LAZIO (IT), Madrid (ES) and CLUBE (EL). 
Task 3.2. Enhanced methods for transport & logistics of urban biowaste (M6– M44). Partners Involved: ITENE, LAZIO, CLUBE, Madrid, FCC 
Following T3.1, enhanced methods for transport & logistics of urban biowaste will be analysed for OFMSW & HORECA (excluding sewage sludge). 
Subtask 3.2.1. Improved logistics of OFMSW  (ITENE, FCC, Madrid, LAZIO, CLUBE): The best logistic methods to reduce collection times, 
avoiding transport steps and optimising the time to reach the treatment plants, will be analysed. Metaheuristic algorithms will feed from current 
statistical data about composition and quantities in selected areas of the municipalities. Tracking the vehicles used for col lection and the 
amounts of selectivelly collected OFMSW will give a  map of routes that will serve as basis for the heuristic calculation (FCC). Specific 
measurements of combined CH4, H2S and temperature sensors will be developed and integrated in the bins to reduce the degradation levels 
of the OFMSW.  
The information abo ut the logistic routes will be used to model the objective function and feed the heuristic logistic optimization method. 
Main boundary conditions will be established by the theoretical equations of degradation of waste as function of the time, te mperature and 
levels of H 2S and CH 4. Algorithms will be developed based on stablished ones, such as Clarke & Wright algorithm and using a GRASP 
methodology for improvements. The heuristic algorithm will then be implemented in pilot experiences afterwards with the di fferent 
municipalities to test the performance results (Task 3.5). 
Subtask 3.2.2. Improved selective collection of HORECA waste (ITENE, FCC, Madrid, LAZIO, CLUBE): The heuristic algorithm for OFMSW will be 
further refined for the specific case of the HOREC A waste, by adding new variable: location point, distance between them, and the schedule 
for collection vs. time of generation (i.e.: lunch, dinner, etc.). 
Task 3.3: Sorting & pre-treatment (M1 – M42). Partners Involved: FCC, Aqualia, ITENE, SMVAK, CENER, VISUM, LAZIO 
This task will tackle the main processes for the sorting & pre- treatment of the collected urban biowaste prior to entering the new processing 
technologies in WPs4-6. Specific treatments will be developed for each one of the types of biowaste. The pre -treatment of sewage sludge is 
considered, since it has to be pre-treated prior the biogas production. 
Subtask 3.3.1. Sorting and pre -treatment of OFMSW, [DS 1] (FCC, CENER, ITENE, VISUM): The FCC plant of Las Dehesas (Madrid, ES) will be 
used as DS  in which the selective collected OFMSW coming from the Madrid municipality will be separated and optimised to reach the 
required conditions to be feed in WP4 (enzymatic hydrolysis of OFMSW). The process for optimising the desired conditions for WP4 will 
consist on: 1) A biowaste monitoring system  (VISUM) based on state of the art optic and spectroscopic methods for the detection of 
contaminants inside the organic waste granules in combination with chemometrics. This system will be installed in the conveyo r belt by FCC 
using commercial components for waste characterisation; 2) A manual separation (FCC); 3) Primary trituration (FCC); 4) Trammel for separation 
of high density materials (FCC); 5) Electromagnetic separator to remove metals (FCC); 6) Homogenisati on, aimed at giving a constant 
composition of organic waste (proteins, fats, carbohydrates, mineral content). For such purpose, different rich fractions wil l be stored and 
mixed giving the right balance in carbohydrates for hydrolysis (FCC, CENER); 7) Stab ilization and hygenisation, in which the biological activity 
of the waste will be inhibited in order to avoid further decomposition. Sterilization will be made at 121ºC for 1h. The sorted and pre -treated 
OFMSW will be supplied in insulated containers at a particle size of 10 mm to fulfil the requirements of the subsequent enzymatic attack for 
the hydrolysis (FCC); 8) Drying of the stabilised OFMSW in an oven dryer (CENER) to minimize the water contents necessary for the high-solid 
hydrolysis. FCC will be re sponsible of supplying 20 tons of stabilized OFMSW obtained in this WP to CENER  in different batches along the 
course of this subtask. Based on the conclusions obtained and the identified critical points, existing technological alternat ives will be 
explored (FCC). A test plan will be established as well as an economic viability study for the selection of the optimal solutions (F CC, CENER, 
ITENE). 
Subtask 3.3.2. Sorting and pre -treatment of HORECA  (LAZIO, UNIMORE, ITENE): The most suitable blends of HORECA w aste capable of 
meeting the requirements for insect rearing (right balance of nutrient-enriched waste for optimum larvae growth) will be sought.  
Subtask 3.3.3. Sorting and pre -treatment of sewage sludge [ DS 6] (SMVAK, Aqualia, ITENE, WETSUS, WBD): Sewage sludge collected from 
SMVAK UWWTP (CZ), from primary settlement and biological treatment, will be pre- treated through homogenisation, based on giving the 
right balance between the necessary nutrients and feed to keep the bioelectrochemical process develope d in WP6, aimed at the production 
of commodity chemicals, running. Optimised mixing of fractions from the primary and secondary treatments will be studied to r each such 
objective. In addition, the homogenised sewage sludge will be hydrolysed, and fats and oils will be removed.

In the specific case of WETSUS UWWTP ( NL), the sludge will be collected from secondary treatment (activated sludge), so that it will be 
explored how to keep a feedstock culture with constant activity for PHBV production. The option o f mixing secondary activated sludge from 
UWWTP with regionally sourced residual organic waste materials will also be explored. 
ITENE will visit the two participating UWWTP in Czech Republic (SMVAK) and The Netherlands (WETSUS, WBD). 
Task 3.4: Characterisation and monitoring of urban biowaste ( M1 – M44) [DS 1]. Partners Involved: ITENE, FCC, CENER, UNIMORE, VISUM, 
Madrid, CLUBE, LAZIO, Aqualia, SMVAK 
In this task all the biowaste fractions will be physically and chemically characterised for the optimisation of the compositions to be fed in 
WP4-6. A specific characterisation protocol will be developed, which will include two different types of characterisation methods: 
Subtask 3.4.1. Streamlined characterisations  (ITENE, FCC, Madrid, CLUBE, LAZIO): Streamlined characterisations made at collection points 
(households, HORECA establishments,  retailers etc.) consisting in a calculation of the biodegradable content and the type of contaminants 
and inert materials (plastics, glass, metal, etc.) contained, including t he effect of seasonal changes per month. This will serve as the basis to 
compare the improvement levels reached by the implementation of best practices in the municipalities participating in the pil ots. Such 
characterisations will exclusively apply to OFMSW and HORECA waste. 
Subtask 3.4.2. Detailed characterisations (FCC, CENER, UNIMORE, Aqualia, SMVAK): Detailed physical and chemical biowaste characterisations 
will be made at the reception point of the sorting & pre -treatment sites prior to their treatment  in WP6-8. The detailed characterisations 
apply to all the urban biowaste fractions, including OFMSW, HORECA/ROW and USS from UWWTP. In the specific case of HORECA/ROW used 
for insect rearing, the detailed characterization will be useful to understand the variability of different biomasses on insect growth rate and 
influences of insect diet on their yield. The physical and chemical parameters to be analysed for OFMSW and HORECA biowaste are:

Task 3.5: Pilot implementation of improvements on selective collection, transport, sorting and pre-treatment (M13 – M44). Partners Involved: 
ITENE, CSCP, FCC, Madrid, LAZIO, CLUBE 
Best practices already identified within WP2 and technical improvements developed in WP3, related to the selective collection  of the 
OFMSW from households and HORE CA, will be implemented in this task during 24 months in specific neighbourhoods/areas of the pilot 
municipalities (Madrid, LAZIO, and CLUBE ) in order to improve their selective collection (ITENE, CSCP).  After those 24 months, the main 
outcome will be a factsheet for each best practice already implemented, which will include a clear description, the success case and the main 
results after the implementation in terms of quality, citizen engagement and relation with final products (bioplastics, biope sticides, food and 
feed animal). The monitoring of the implementation of those best practices will be also carried out to avoid deviations and g et the expected 
quality and quantity of biowaste targeted by WP3-6 through KPIs based on the characterisation parameters defined in Task 3.4.  
The pilots will include 2 -week visit periods  ITENE to the participating municipalities for the testing of the improvements proposed in the 
above-mentioned fields, and more specifically on: 
 City of Madrid (ES): Implementation of social  awareness best practices on collection of OFMSW (with Madrid and FCC), as well as 
sorting, pre -treatment and characterisation of OFMSW (with FCC). ITENE will seek also for the opportunities to meet the best 
requirements for the production of biopolyesters and biopesticides. 
 LAZIO (Albano, IT): Implementation of best practices for collection, transport & characterisation of OFMSW and HORECA waste 
 CLUBE (Kozani, EL): Implementation of best practices for collection, transport and characterisation of OFMSW and HORECA waste

Objectives: To demonstrate the biochemi cal conversion of the OFMSW in biobased and biodegradable polyesters and biopesticides  by 
enzymatic hydrolysis and fermentation processes. Validation from pilot to demo scale in an operational environment.  
 Demonstrate the production of fermentable sugars from the OFMSW in an operational environment. 
 Validate the robustness and performance of specific enzymatic cocktails prepared for OFMSW. 
 Verify an improvement of subsequent fermentation yields.  
 Validate and demonstrate the production of biobased and biodegradable polyesters from OFMSW. 
 Validate and demonstrate the production of bacterial biopesticides from the OFMSW by SSF. 
Task 4.1: Production and design of enzyme preparations (M1 – M24, Initial TRL 5/6). Partners Involved: ASA, CENER, FCC 
Subtask 4.1.1: Design and selection of enzyme cocktails for the disintegration and saccharification of OFMSW : Single enzyme cocktails as 
cellulases, hemicellulases, pectinases, amylases, proteases and lipases will be produced by ASA  at pilot scale and tested for the de gradation 
of OFMSW. Then, different combinations of the selected enzyme cocktails will be developed in order to optimize the release of  sugars from 
particular fractions of OFMSW.  
Subtask 4.1.2: Validation of selected enzyme mixtures for the treatment of OFMSW: OFMSW supplied from WP3 will be treated with enzyme 
cocktails under varied conditions. Resulting mono-, di- and oligosaccharides will be detected by HPLC.  
Subtask 4.1.3: Production of the most efficient enzyme preparations for runs and demonstration at CENER’s plant: The best enzyme cocktails 
will be produced and provided to CENER to test their efficiency at pilot scale (200 L). 
Subtask 4.1.4: Characterization of the enzyme mixtures  in terms of enzyme activity spectrum, pH and temperature activity an d stability, 
storage stability, substrate specificity, protein composition and further biochemical properties. 
Task 4.2: Enzymatic hydrolysis of the OFMSW for the production of sugars (M6 – M36, Initial TRL 6, [DS 2]). Partners Involved: CENER, AERIS, 
ASA, FCC, NOVAMONT 
The enzymatic hydrolysis process will be carried out at high solid loads (20 -25%) and demonstrated in a 3,000 L bioreactor. A liquid sugar 
enriched fraction will be separated through a series of unit processes (T4.2.3) and the recovered unhy drolysed solid fraction and other 
organic components will be split in two batches: a) processed with the urban sewage sludge (USS) in WP6 and b) used in T4.4 for SSF to produce 
biopesticides. The sugars available in the liquid fraction will be concentrated  to get a more enriched media suitable for the submerged 
fermentation processes (T4.4&ST4.4.1). 
Subtask 4.2.1. Validation of enzymatic hydrolysis at pilot scale  (CENER): Temperature, pH, agitation, residence time, enzymes and enzyme 
dosage will be validate d either at lab and bench scale. Key parameters such as soluble sugars, proteins -aminoacids, lipid-fatty acids will be 
monitored for calculating overall yields. A validation stage will be carried out at a scale of nearly 200 L.  
Subtask 4.2.2. Validation of enzymatic hydrolysis at demo scale (CENER): A complete operating process will be carried out at demo scale (up to 
3000L) using the best enzymatic cocktail supplied by T4.1. Analysis and quantification of the main parameters (described in 4 .2.1) will be 
monitored. 
Subtask 4.2.3. Downstream and upgrading of the hydrolysate (CENER, AERIS, NOVAMONT): The hydrolysate produced in the former subtasks 
will be subjected to flocculation, coagulation and concentration. Concentration of the sugars in the hydrolysate is done to obtain an enriched 
syrup guaranting significant sugar levels in the media for the further fermentation processes for biopolyesters and biopestic ides production. 
Additionally, the solid fraction will be used as feedstock for: a) SSF  to produce biopesticides (ST4.4.2), b) anaerobic co-digestion with sewage 
sludge in WP6. 
Subtask 4.2.4. Demonstration of enzymatic hydrolysis, downstream and purification and production of hydrolysate  (CENER): Operating 
conditions for these runs will be previously sele cted in ST4.2.1 and the scaling up of the process in ST4.2.2 will provide with more accurate 
information about biocatalyst behaviour at higher scales. Subtask 4.2.3 results will help to demonstrate the whole performanc e of the 
conversion process.  
Task 4.3: Fermentation into building blocks for formulation of biodegradable polyesters (M24 –48, Initial TRL 6, [DS 4]), Partners Involved: 
NOVAMONT, ITENE, CENER, ASA 
Sub-task 4.3.1. Validation of OFMSW into 1,4 bio -BDO production (NOVAMONT, CENER, M6-M24): Experimental tests will be done at pilot 
scale to validate the production of biobased 1,4 BDO by direct fermentation of sugars produced by CENER (T4.2). Fermenter volumes (from 
1L up to 100 L) will be done for validation. Feedback on potential contaminants and  inhibitors of fermentation will be provided to CENER in 
order to effectively adjust the sugars purification protocol.  
As a benchmark, commercial sugars (1st generation sugars) will be used for fermentation tests in order to compare productivit y, titter and 
yield obtained from 1st to OFMSW derived sugars. This phase will allow monitoring and analysing at pilot scale the main opera tional 
parameters and KPI before the demonstration at larger scale. Separation and purification steps of broth containing BDO ob tained from 2nd 
generation sugars will be verified and compared to that of the benchmark. Micro and nanofiltration, ion exchange will be appl ied. Type and 
concentration of (relevant) impurities in biobased monomers will be determined and compared to indust ry-references in order to identify 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
49 
  
possible deviations. Process strategies for the optimization of 2nd generation sugars preparation, fermentation and/or purifi cation and 
separation processes will be identified in order to meet demand side requirements and to guarantee high purity biobased monomers. 
Sub-task 4.3.2. Polymerization of 1,4 biobased BDO into biobased polyesters and their compounding for the targeted applications (NOVAMONT, 
M6-M30): The initial target will be focused on the optimization of the s ynthesis of biobased polyesters, starting from the bio- BDO produced 
in ST4.3.1. Hence, the evaluation will be started using a two -stage polymerization method based on transesterification and polycondensation 
comparing several catalytic systems (organometal lic compound of metals such as titanium, tin…). Di -carboxylic acids will be used in 
polycondensation reaction to synthesize polyesters and co- polyesters. Chemical-physical properties, mechanical and rheological properties, 
performances in aging, permeabili ty, biodegradability and their environmental impact will be determined. The characteristics of the bio - 
polymers obtained from the different biobased monomers will be compared to the benchmark, i.e. petrochemical based polymer. 
Polymerization conditions will be optimised (temperature, catalyst, molecular weight regulator, etc). Products will be fully characterized and 
tested. The most promising biobased polyesters will be compounded with other biobased materials to improve mechanical and thermal 
properties.  
Sub-task 4.3.3. Demonstration (NOVAMONT, M24-M48) of bio-BDO production (at 1 m3 scale) in batch mode, to demonstrate the robustness 
of the fermentation and of the downstream process at demo scale. Combination with 1st generation sugars will be also evaluated in order to define 
a proper mix based on techno -economic evaluations. The obtained bio -BDO will be then used to demonstrate the production of biobased 
polyesters and compounded polyesters. The biopolyester will be subjected to reactive extrusion with  organic and/or inorganic additives, bio- 
based polymers (e.g. starch) to obtain the right quantity and quality of biobased polymers to be validated into the targeted final applications. 
Subtask 4.3.4. Production and validation of the new biopolyesters obtained (ITENE, NOVAMONT) (M36-48): An evaluation of the processability 
of these new biopolymers and a complete characterisation of the materials will be carried out keeping in mind the requirement s of a future 
industrial scale. To validate their processabil ity, ITENE will produce films and sheets of the different formulations produced by NOVAMONT . 
One application will concern the development of biobased and biodegradable films for organic waste collection bags as well as  food 
packaging materials in view of f urther enhancing the market uptake of the new biobased and biodegradable polyesters applications. Final 
properties of the films and sheets prototypes, such as mechanical performance (tensile strength, compression strength, and pu ncture 
resistance tests), b arrier properties (Grease, OTR and WVTR), thermal resistivity and profiles by using a thermogravimetric, differential 
scanning and melt flow index equipment’s, will be evaluated. NOVAMONT  will carry out biodegradability and compostability tests of the 
developed applications according to EN13432 standard. 
Subtask 4.3.5. Food contact validation/certification (ITENE, NOVAMONT) (M36-48): The compliance with the Framework Regulation (EC) No. 
1935/2004 on materials and articles to come into contact with food will  be demonstrated. In this regard, the new polyesters will be 
evaluated according to the European Regulation (EU) No. 10/2011 on plastic materials to be in contact with foodstuff. To demo nstrate the 
inertia of the material, overall migration test of the fin al material will be performed in food simulants and selected conditions according to 
EN 1186-1:2002. The specific migration tests will be performed according to the European standard EN 13130-1:2005 and Regulation (EU) 
No. 10/2011.  
Task 4.4: Bacterial biopesticides production through fermentation (M36-M48, Initial TRL 5, [DS 2&3]) Partners involved: CENER, AERIS 
Production of bacterial biopesticide from sugar hydrolysate and part of the unhydrolysed solids through 2 different fermentat ion 
technologies (submerged & solid state) from pilot to demo plant. The activity of the biopesticide will be tested by standard toxicity bioassays on 
insects’ larvae. 
Subtask 4.4.1. Demonstration of bacterial biopesticide production through submerged fermentation (CENER): The sugar enriched hydrolysate 
produced in ST4.2.4. will be used as a carbon source to grow Bacillus thuringiensis sp. To validate the process at pilot scal e (100 L), an 
exhaustive control of the process conditions and nutrients available in the media will be done. Samples will be collected and toxicity against 
target pest analysed. After the validation at pilot scale the process will be reproduced in a 1,000 L bioreactor. Process conditions and nutrients in the 
media will be monitored. Once validated, a series of biopesticides production runs will be carried out in 1,000 L bioreactor. The biopesticide 
will be extracted from the liquid phase in the form of crystal proteins by centrifugation, separating the Bacillus thuringiensis sp spores & cells. 
Subtask 4.4.2. Demonstration of bacterial biopesticide production through solid-state fermentation (AERIS): Part of the solid fraction obtained 
after the enzymatic hydrolysis will be subjected to a SSF process. The solid organic material will be submitted to SSF in a p ilot plant that will 
be designed and developed specifically for this project. Optimal conditions of the process in terms of temperature, rate of a eration, mixing, 
etc. and best inoculation method will also be studied. A maximum rate of biopesticide producti on will be established to extract the 
biopesticide from the solid matrix by means of successive washings with Ringer solution.

from the OFMSW by enzymatic hydrolysis (CENER, M24&36)  
D4.2. Report on optimized protocol for bio-BDO and polyester production from OFMSW sugars (NOVAMONT; M24&M30)

D4.4. Report on optimized protocol for the production of bacterial biopesticide production from OFMSW) (CENER and AERIS; M48)

Objectives: The main objective is to obtain high-value products from Black Soldier Fly (BSF) reared on retail organic materials and OFMSW. In 
more specific terms the ways to address the above-mentioned challenge are:  
 to mass rearing insects on organic waste by optimization of pilot plant and integration of the INPUT stage for substrate preparation 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
50 
  
and the OUTPUT stage for insect treatment and stabilization.  
 to extract proteins and lipids from insects reared on organic waste by a chemical/physical approach. The extraction process will be 
developed in small scale and then will be scale up by realization of a prototype. 
 to characterize the insect substrate composition. Monitoring the quality of the substrate as source of energy and body mass. 
 to characterize the litter/compost to verify the quality of the substrate in terms of fertility elements. 
Description of work 
Task 5.1. Integration of new parts in the pilot plant (M3-M23, Initial TRL 6, [DS 5]). Partners involved: UNIMORE, Kour Energy 
The prototype of pilot plant of UNIMORE must be optimized to run with HORECA waste by adding new components : one part for automatic  
substrate preparation (INPUT stage) another for automatic treatment and stabilization of the insects at the end of process (OUTPUT stage).  
Subtask 5.1.1. Automatic preparation of substrate for rearing insect starting from organic waste  (INPUT stage) (UNIMORE, KOUR): Substrate 
preparation is crucial for insect rearing: the physical and chemical properties of substrate (density, composition, water con tent) should be 
uniform to guarantee the perfect function of the pilot plant. To ensure the optimum substrat e, a multi-step system will be developed with 
the following stages: milling, water excess removal, homogenization, automatic transportation inside the rearing pilot plant. 
 Technical specifications of the part for substrate preparation will be defined. A si mple model will be developed for calculating the 
technical parameter of the plant (actuators, sensors, electrical power, mechanical power) on the basis of the input parameters.  
 The mechanical projects of defined parts will be collected and the 3D model (d esign software Autocad Inventor) will be done. 3D 
models of the single parts will be “virtually” assembled in a single 3D project of the system. Electrical schematic will be d esigned and 
verified by using Elpan software. From these schemes the list of components will be compiled.  
 Realization of the single components and assembly and test of the components. The single components will be tested singularly . Some 
functional tests will be done on the whole assembled system and the INPUT stage part will be integrated in the pilot plant.  
Subtask 5.1.2.  Automatic system for  insect treatment and stabilization at the end of the process  (OUTPUT stage) (UNIMORE, KOUR): The 
OUTPUT stage is important to ensure the stabilization of insects. A pre- treatment is required i n order to physically separate the larvae from 
the substrate, to kill the insects and to clean the larvae from any residual of substrate (hot and cold water). These treatme nts could affect 
the fractionation process. For this reason, the general treatment and stabilization process has to be defined in collaboration with UNIMORE. 
 Definition of the technical specifications of the system on the basis of the details provided by UNIMORE.   
 Technical project of the components (mechanical and automation project) of  the insect treatment and stabilization part. The 
mechanical project and electric schematic will be done in the same way of the INPUT stage Task 5.1.1.  
 Realization of the single components and assembly and test of the components  
Task 5.2. Insect rearing on the pilot plant (M6-M42, Initial TRL 6, [DS 5]). Partners involved: Kour, UNIMORE 
Subtask 5.2.1. Insect rearing (UNIMORE, KOUR): The activity will start by using the original pilot plant of UNIMORE. Once the new integrated 
pilot plant is ready (M23), th e rearing of insects will continue in the final pilot plant. The rearing of insect will be done in an operational 
environment (UNIMORE) and the rearing conditions (humidity, temperature, feeding rate, density of larvae/cm2, mean larvae weight) will be 
optimized during the project. The larvae density (number of larvae / cm2) has to be maximise to increase the production capacity of the pilot 
plant, which depends directly on the rearing condition, the feed rate (substrate/day) and feed quantity per larva. The se two parameters will 
be optimized and compared with those reported in literature for substrates with the same composition.   
Subtask 5.2.2. Optimization of the pilot plant for rearing insect (KOUR, UNIMORE): The original pilot plant of UNIMORE for rearin g insect will 
be optimized for the conversion of organic waste material. For increasing the TRL from 6 to 7 some small components will be m odified 
during the validation in the operational environment.  
 Analysis of the pilot plant and functional tests. KOUR M6-M23  
 Optimization of the pilot plant and modification of components. KOUR M6-M42 
Task 5.3. Insect fractionation (M1-M42, Initial TRL 4, [DS 5]). Partners involved: UNIMORE, Kour, Zetadec 
Subtask. 5.3.1 Protein, lipid and chitin extraction and purificat ion (UNIMORE, Zetadec) Biomasses consisting of insect larvae will first be 
characterized. The protein content (by Kjeldahl analysis) and amino acid composition (by HPLC analysis), 77 in order to define the nutritional 
value of the protein fraction will be do ne. Based on this chemical composition, a preliminary evaluation of the properties of the biomass will 
be carried out. 
Various purification techniques will be tested on laboratory scale (max 1Kg) to identify the best procedure to apply to the n ew pilot plant. 
Lipids will be separated with organic solvents and subsequently characterized (see Task 5.3.2). A solventless approach will b e also tested. 
The residue of lipid extraction will be treated with aqueous systems (acids, bases, saline solutions, hydroalcoh olic solutions) or with enzymes 
to extract and purify the protein fraction. The insoluble residue will then be demineralized to obtain the purified chitin fraction. 
The composition of the protein fraction will be evaluated to understand its nutritional val ue in terms of essential amino acids, in order to be 
used as a high protein content supplement with high nutritional value in feed. The chitin fraction will be quantified as it r epresents an 
additional source of useful substances in several fields (e.g. fo od technologies and packaging applications). The lipids that will inevitably be a 
by-product deriving from the purification of proteins will be characterized for lipid composition by GC analysis of fatty acid m ethyl esters. 78 
We will have an evaluation of the quality of the lipids obtained, helping to define their possible use: food, feed and energy. 
Subtask 5.3.2.  Design and development of a prototype for automatic insect fractionation  (KOUR, UNIMORE) : The fractionation process 
developed by UNIMORE (Task 5.3.1) for the separation of proteins and lipids will be implemented in a prototype for automatic fractionation 
by Kour Energy. The prototype for fractionation will be designed to be industrial scalable and cost-effective.  
 Identification of the best technologies for fractionating that are both industrial scalable and comparable of those used in the lab.  
 The mechanical projects of defined parts will be done as described in tast 5.1. From the electrical schematic and the list of  components 
required the I/O list will be done and a proper controller (PLC) will be identified. The software for the automation will be developed on 
the basis of the fractionating process (reactions time, reaction steps). 
 Realization of the single components on the basis of the technical project and assembly and test of the components. 
Subtask 5.3.3. Validation of the prototype for fractionation (UNIMORE, KOUR): The prototype for fractionation will be validate by Kour Energy 
                                                                                                               
77 Food Chemistry, 121, 69-77, (2010) 
78 Food Chemistry, 121, 809-814, (2010)

and UNIMORE, the output proteins and lipids of the prototype w ill be compared with those isolated in lab. On the basis of the analysis the 
prototype will be optimized during the validation and some components or some part of the automation software code will be modified. 
Task 5.4. Validation and characterization of the chitin fraction (M6-M46, Initial TRL 5, [DS 5]). Partners involved: ITENE, UNIMORE 
Subtask 5.4.1. Production and validation of chitin nanofibers/nanowhiskers as material reinforcement  (ITENE, UNIMORE): Chitin samples 
produced as byproduct in T5.3 will b e treated by chemical, enzymatic and mechanical procedures to obtain chitin nanowhiskers. Their 
chemical properties, average size (by atomic and transmission force microscopy), thermal resistance and rheology will be dete rmined as well 
as yield. The chitin nanowhiskers will be evaluated as a reinforcement material. ITENE will use developed chitin nanowhiskers to produce two 
different materials and test to define future prototypes: a) Coating materials : A polymer coated with the chitin nanofiber gel. For the  
evaluation of the processability of the coating applications different trials, will be performed with a pilot scale coater; b ) Composites 
materials: Biocomposites will be produced by extrusion cast technologies, and their main formulations will be used to  produce different 
probes by injection moulding. 
Coated materials will be studied in terms of adhesion to substrate (ISO 2409:2013 cross cut test), optical properties and oth ers, like the 
coefficient of friction (ISO 8295:1995). Injected materials main properties will be evaluated and compared with non -reinforced polyesters 
produced in WP4. Characterization will include: thermal analysis (DSC, TGA), mechanical (tensile strength, delamination, roughness…), and 
barrier properties (Grease, OTR and WVTR) of the composite films and coated materials will also be evaluated.  
Subtask 5.4.2. Production, characterization and validation of chitosan as raw material for plastic packaging (ITENE, UNIMORE): Production of 
chitin will be performed in order to obtain varying degrees of chitosan. It will be subjected to an exhaustive analysis of physicochemical (FTIR 
and SEM analyses), mechanical (tensile and dynamomechanical analyses), thermal (TGA) and barrier (grease, oxygen and water va pour 
transmission rate) properties to evaluate its quality. Different blends of chitosan with various polymers, such as PHB or PLA will be prepared. 
The biopolymers will be processed by means of pilot extrusion and/or injection equipment in function of their properties to o btain flexible 
films and/or rigid packages such as pots. The properties of the new materials will be evaluated and compared with the conventional ones. 
Evaluation of the processability of these new biopolymers and a complete characterisation of the materials including mechani cal, thermal, 
optical, antimicrobial and barrier properties will be carried out keeping in mind the requirements of a future industrial scale.

Objectives: This WP proposes a “s tart to end” valorisation process where feeds are majorly pre -conditioned in WP3 to obtain ready -to-use 
products. Two prototypes will be built to demonstrate the feasibility to obtain high -value products from raw biowastes (OFMSW and USS). 
This process wil l be validated in prototypes operated in three demonstration sites: MSW ( DS 1, ES) and USS ( DS 6 (CZ) and 7 (NL)). Special 
attention will be given to the key operation parameters and system design for the production of target valuable end -products to be adapted 
at DSs. Specific objectives of WP6 are: 
 Scale up from pilot plants to demo level of units based on BES and biochemical treatment of USS 
 Design, construction and integration of the demo plants 
 Overall process operation, optimization and validation at DSs 1, 6 and 7 
Task 6.1: Pre-treatment techniques evaluation (M01 – M12). Partners Involved: SMVAK 
Pre-treatment of sewage sludge is necessary to break- down complex molecules into simple monomers, to increase solubilization of organic 
material and improve  the efficiency of the following anaerobic step. The selected homogenization and pre- treatment procedures in WP3, 
will be evaluated in Task 6.1. Proposed pre-treatment will be tested with raw materials and mixtures defined in WP3, whose feasibility will be 
evaluated and optimized at prototype scale. Biodegradability tests of single and mix substrates will be also performed as a b asic tool to 
determine possible undesirable inhibitory or toxic effects and establish appropriate load, feed mixtures ratios and o peration conditions to be 
used at prototype scale at DS  1 (ES), 6 (CZ), and 7 (NL). Additional pre -conditioning actions will be carried out with USS, which will be 
partitioned to improve its valorisation in SCALIBUR. Fats, oil and grease waste present in w astewater (currently disposed in landfill) will be 
separated in this task to be valorised in Task 6.2 as cosubstrate in the advanced anaerobic bioconversion step.  
Task 6.2: Sewage sludge advanced anaerobic conversion (M07 – M24, Initial TRL 5, DS 1 & 6). Partners Involved: SMVAK, AERIS 
Subtask 6.2.1. Design and construction of prototypes  (M7 – M11, SMVAK, AQUA, Aeris) of the  SCALIBUR prototype for the anaerobic 
bioconversion of sewage sludge into high -value compounds. It will include the engineering of the  anaerobic reactor and the design of fluid 
flow system including flow meters, pumps, valves, pipe work feed and receipt vessel (if needed), as well as the implementatio n of the 
automation and control system. Optimized design of advanced anaerobic digestion  with pre -treatments/homogenization to maximize 
products yield and quality will be done. Mechanical stress and chemical resistance test will be performed for each component of the 
prototype to assure the optimal construction and performance. Several partne rs will participate ( SMVAK, AQUA, Aeris) to assure a properly 
functioning prototype, with an innovative process for the collection, conditioning and feed of the pre -treated materials to the advanced 
anaerobic step. Validation tests will be carried out with  USS collected from other sites, including the addition of other residual materials to 
enhance the process performance. Prototypes will be erected in DS s 1&6, where the whole process (homogenization, pretreatment, 
bioconversion and downstreams) will be ope rated. Feed and the resulting fractions (liquid, solid and gas) upon anaerobic step will be 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
52 
  
monitored and available to be subsequently treated in cascade downstream to fulfil the quality standard of the end-products targeted.  
Subtask 6.2.2. Installation and start-up of integral process (M12 – M14, SMVAK, AQUA, Aeris): The SCALIBUR prototype will be installed and 
operated in the facilities at DS  1 (FCC), to be completed and deployed at month 12, and 6 ( SMVAK). The reception of the integral system 
including all the elements of the prototype will be accordingly adapted. T he advanced anaerobic bioconversion prototype unit will also 
include instrumentation and other additional equipment, together with a dewatering unit that allows the solid -liquid fractions separation in 
order to fulfil the standards defined for the subsequent downstream, required to obtain target end-products.  
Subtask 6.2.3. Operation and optimization of pre -treatment and anaerobic bioconversion performance (M15 – M24, AERIS, AQUA, SMVAK): 
Long-term performance of the SCALIBUR prototype will be assessed under real conditions. On the other hand, actions to implement different 
methods for securing the long -term homogeneity (proposed in WP3) of the feed will be applied. Operation strategies will be explored in 
order to expand the flexibility of the system, and facilitate transformation of pre -treated sewage sludge into target end -products. Evaluation 
will be carried out by AQUA with the local support from SMVAK  at DS 6.  Initially, optimization of t he prototype will be performed in batch 
mode. After that, mixtures with greater potential will be continuously fed to optimize the physical and biological units in the integral process. 
During the bioconversion process, LCFA and VFA accumulation will be co ntrolled to assure a stable process performance. The remote 
monitoring and control functionalities will facilitate the process monitoring and resolution of possible problems. 
Additional actions will be carried out focused on fats, oil and grease separation  and used as co -substrate to enhance the efficiency of the 
SCALIBUR solution and the resulting products. The separation process (chemicals dose, reaction time, mixing rates, etc.) and mixtures ratios 
will be optimized. The advanced anaerobic bioconversion process will be adapted to assimilate new sources of biowastes. 
Both installations in Spain and Czech Republic will be characterized by in -depth analysis of energy consumption, chemicals consumption, 
bioconversion rate and extension, for the production of target end-products.  
T6.3. Bioconversion of steering CO2 fermentation with bioelectrochemical systems (BES) (M1 – M36, Initial TRL 5, demos sites 1 & 6). Partners 
involved: AQUA, FCC, Aeris, ITENE, SMVAK 
Subtask 6.3.1. BES prototypes design and construction for bioconversion of OFMSW (DS 1) and USS (DS 6) into high-value compounds (M01 – 
M09, AQUA, SMVAK, Aeris) will be done. Prototype design will include the engineering of the whole BES prototype with pre- treatment and 
the design of fluid flow system. Mec hanical stress and chemical resistance test will be performed for each component of the prototype to 
ensure the optimal construction and performance. All partners involved in this task will participate to ensure the design of a properly 
functioning prototy pe. AQUA will provide a BES unit including instrumentation for process monitoring. Aeris will collaborate in the 
adaptation of the current process for biogas collection and conditioning to be fed into the BES prototype. If necessary due t o impurities of 
the gas, AQUA, SMVAK and FCC will provide the required pre-treatment steps previous to the BES.  
Subtask 6.3.2. Development of microorganisms inoculum pre -culture (M10 – M33) AQUA: In order to accelerate the start -up of the BES 
prototype, AQUA will provide a n enriched and highly -active inoculum of bioelectrogenic consortium. AQUA will collaborate with the 
University of Girona as subcontractors, where existing bench scale facilities are available, and have demonstrated the feasib ility of the 
process proposed i n previous R&D joint actions. This ensures the source of ready -to-use inoculum in case of destabilization of the BES 
prototypes. In addition, this strategy will facilitate the selectivity towards the production of target compounds with the different feeds. 
Subtask 6.3.3. Installation and start -up of integral BES process  (M10 – M12, M22 – M24) AQUA: The BES prototype will be installed and 
operated in the facilities provided by FCC ( DS 1) and SMVAK (DS 6), which are responsible of the preparation of the DSs for the reception of 
the integral system including the BES prototype. The BES prototype will be completed and deployed at month 12 (DS 1) and 24 (DS 6). 
Subtask 6.3.4. Operation and optimization of BES prototypes performance (M13 – M21, M25 – M33) SMVAK: Long-term performance of the 
BES prototype will be assessed and stability of microorganisms’ biofilm will be also monitored. On the other hand, actions to  implement 
different methods for securing the long-term homogeneity of the transport properties of the e lectrodes will be applied. Operation strategies 
will be explored in order to avoid adverse clogging effects by the biofilm. Evaluation will be carried out by AQUA. FCC and SMVAK will provide 
local support at DS s. The main parameters that will be analyzed are pH, cathode potential, partial pressure of CO 2, and application of feast -
famine conditions. The partners involved will prepare technology transfer documents and safety assessment, in coordination with WP8. 
Subtask 6.3.5. Evaluation of prototype performa nce, products quality and suitability for bioplastics production  (M16 – M21, M28 – M33, 
SMVAK, FCC): DSs 1&6 will be characterized by in -depth analysis of carbon and electron balances, and the energy requirements for the 
production processes using CO 2 from the two selected sources. The CO 2 conversion rates, and the resulting product spectrum will be 
investigated to identify the process limiting factors, and improve the overall performance. Energy and chemical requirements will be 
determined. CAPex and OPex studies will be compared with state -of-the-art OFMSW valorization ways. Special attention will be given to the 
key parameters and system design for the production of valuable organics such as long chain fatty acids and alcohols. The con sortium will 
build a prototype to demonstrate the feasibility of BES to obtain high-value products. This study will be replicated in two demonstration sites 
for the sake of comparison and validation in different scenarios (CZ and ES), the quality of the resulting effluent fro m SCALIBUR will be fully 
assessed in order to guarantee that it accomplishes with the requirements of target compounds standards as end -product and raw material 
for further polishing. CAPex and OPex studies will be compared with state-of-the-art OFMSW and USS valorisation ways. 
Task 6.4. PHBV production from sewage sludge (M1–M48, Initial TRL 5, DS 7). Partners involved: WETSUS, WBD, ITENE 
Surplus full -scale activated sludge for biomass supply and regionally available liquid fraction of fermented OFMSW will  be used as the 
substrate. The biomass will be accumulated in bi -weekly batch production campaigns to yield PHA at 100 to 200 gPHA/batch in PHA -rich 
biomass. The batch-to-batch materials will be dried, assessed as a “semi-product”, assembled and master batched. The master batched PHA-
rich biomass will be purified to nominally 98 % pure polymers.  
Subtask 6.4.1. Production process design, construction and commissioning WETSUS, WBD (M1-12): Facility and infrastructure for processing 
raw materials (activated s ludge and regional organic biowaste from municipal will be realized and implemented. This facility will include 
process steps of acidogenic fermentation, PHA -accumulation, biomass drying, and polymer solvent extraction. The goal is to establish a 
production line and to manage and handle materials within a relevant up-scalable context. Especially, previous experience of PHARIO piloting 
polymer recovery will be applied and advanced to bring the polymer recovery methods from TRL 4 to 6. 
Subtask 6.4.2. Biopolymer Production Campaign I (Operation and Tuning) WETSUS, WBD (M12-24): The process will be brought into a mode or 
routine operation and polymer production. Variability of process and raw material quality will be monitored towards defining and tuning 
process with respect to influence on production efficiency and product quality, with a goal to produce between 8-16 kg of product. Materials will 
be supplied to the downstream T6.5  partners for preliminary evaluations and collaboration on questions of quality wit h respect to the 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
53 
  
product end use. 
Subtask 6.4.3. Biopolymer Production Campaign II (Products for Downstream Developments)  WETSUS, WBD (M24-30): Based on the results 
and experience of T6.4.2, the facility should now be operated as a production facility from  raw materials to semi-products to polymers. This 
period of operation should define the achieved TRL and the current state of the art for product and product quality control. It is the goal 
during this period that between 4 and 8 kg of PHA as product be produced for T6.5.3 critical downstream evaluations. 
Subtask 6.4.4. Production Optimisation and Value Engineering (Innovating for Scale up)  WETSUS, WBD (M30-36): Subsequent to anticipated 
critical goal -oriented evaluations of materials from T6.4.3, the proce ss will be evaluated with an eye for improving performance and 
economics with respect to questions of production efficiency and product quality. Since the recovery process is known to repr esent the 
greatest burden for investment, a principal objective will  be to evaluate innovative ways to reduce recovery costs and achive economy of 
scale. This will be done in a value engineering approach in cooperation through a subcontract with an engineering contractor with 
experience in designing solvent extraction plants. It is also the goal during this period that between 4 to 8 kg PHA will again be produced. 
Task 6.5. Evaluation of products quality for biopolymer production (M30 – M36). Partners involved: ITENE, WETSUS, AQUA, FCC 
Polyhydroxyalkanoates (PHAs) will be obtained from sewage sludge within the process performed at Wetsus facilities. Bioplastic composition 
and properties of both tasks will be assessed to validate its suitability for future uses.  
 Production and evaluation as raw materials for plastic: A full characterization of the new biobased polyesters will be performed to select 
best grades for producing the packaging product prototypes. To validate their processability, ITENE will process the biopolymers by 
means of pilot extrusion and/or injection equipm ent in function of their properties to obtain blow films and/or rigid packag es such as 
cups of the different formulations produced by Wetsus. 
 Food contact validation/certification of developed biomaterials: The compliance with the Framework Regulation (EC)  No. 1935/2004 on 
materials and articles to come into contact with food will be demonstrated for the new packaging materials, as decribed in Task 4.3.5.

Objectives: During this WP, we will leverage the SMAC Technology stack (Social, Mobile, Analytics and Cloud) to design and build an 
interactive Cloud Platfor m that will allow the integration of data streams and specific user -oriented modules that is readily accessible over 
the web and mobile devices, such as smartphones and tablets. The functionalities and information given, as well as a user -friendly interface, 
will be tailored to the different levels of internal and external stakeholders, such as citizens/consumers, waste generators and managers, 
users of bioproducts and policy makers. It will be used for facilitating quadruple helix stakeholder engagement, p romoting social innovation, 
showcasing project data from the pilots, creating and demonstrating new business models for high -value biobased products derived from 
urban biowaste, promoting the new technologies, increasing awareness, showing the project tech nical and social impacts, or providing best 
practices and policy recommendations for project replicability. 
To achieve this objective, a number of modules will be developed and integrated to allow quadruple helix stakeholders to have access to an 
“all-in-one” environment for the implementation of sustainable urban biowaste valorisation into new bio -based products. The work will be 
carried out according to “ SCRUM” and Test -Driven Development (TDD) Agile methodologies , which have been successfully exploited b y 
VISUM for developing other complex software platforms for waste management and circular economy, such as in the Sharebox proj ect 
(http://sharebox-project.eu/) or the Agrocycle project (http://www.agrocycle.eu/). As a programming methodology oriented to c ode 
“reliable-by-design” software, TDD is particularly necessary for efficiently developing “almost-bug-free” large software Cloud platforms.  
Task 7.1: Definition of the Cloud Architecture (M1 – M12). Partners Involved: VISUM, ITENE, CSCP, NS, MADRID, LAZIO, CLUBE, Lund, FCC 
During this task, we will define the User Requirements of the Platform. Scoping sessions will be organised with a focus group  that will be 
recruited from the relevant quadruple helix internal and external representatives. We will use a selection of methodologies to establish the 
user requirements, specifications and features, functionality and desired User Experience. The first meetings of the Urban Bi owaste Clubs 
will also allow for co-designing the main characteristics of the smart modules of the SCALIBUR stakeholder platform (T7.2). An in-depth analysis 
of existing technologies will be performed to find out which are the ones that best match the requirements for each functionalit y. Based on 
the results of the scoping sessions, the in -depth architecture (backend, middleware, intelligence, database, etc: layers structures) will be 
defined for the SCALIBUR Cloud Platform. The architecture has to be flexible in terms of single -tenant or multi -tenant deployment, 
guaranteeing that it is abl e to highly perform when running the intelligence layer. Therefore, it will be designed how to address the 
envisaged computational workload and established how all the modules will work and seamlessly interact. Particular importance will be given to 
establish software quality measures prior to commencing the platform development work. A Quality Analysis (QA) methodology will be in 
place (in keeping with software quality management: ISO 9126 -3 and the subsequent ISO 25000:2005 quality model) to ensure consis tent 
and standardised implementation. As such, a set of metrics and key performance indicators will be fixed to be used to validat e the quality of 
the software. According to sued agile methodologies, all the individual tasks defined will include Unit or Fu nctional Tests. The outcome of 
this task will fuel D7.1.  
Task 7.2: Development of the different smart modules of the SCALIBUR interactive stakeholder platform (M6 – M48) Partners Involved: VISUM,

ITENE, CSCP, NS, MADRID, LAZIO, CLUBE, Lund, FCC  
Information on the do's and dont's of the (full ) integration of the upgraded urban biowaste value chain into the existing local 
waste/wastewater management schemes , derived from actions in T2.2, will be integrated in the stakeholder platform to provide 
transparency and make data available for the waste generators, which are the key actors providing the new biowaste fractions for the 
innovative treatment processes. Like this, they will be able to check the results of their actions (new added value products from urban  
biowaste) thanks to the innovative waste management at the source. The different modules defined in the previous task for eg. tracking of 
data and action effects, communication, marketplace, mapping, etc., will be defined in terms of inputs and outputs an d processing 
requirements, involving a data scientist when necessary. In particular, but not limited to, the following modules will be inc luded in the 
SCALIBUR platform: 
 Quadruple-helix engagement modules at local level: Specific modules will be created to facilite engagement with the communities where 
the three pilots will take place, each one in the local languages, as well as for the best performing territory that will ser ve as model, 
informing about the performance of the local waste management. The mod ule will also contain interactive questionnaires/ 
experiments/games and tools for methodology evaluation (WP2). 
 New processing technologies modules: Data and news regarding the new technologies will be shared and visualised to promote their 
further uptake. Models from WP3 will also be integrated and accessible by the cities and other users to test further optimisation scenarios. 
 New high-value biobased products modules: The new business models created for each produced biobased product will be integrated 
and a market place will be made available for promoting the new products sales. 
 Social innovation module: Social innovations achieved at each of the communities will be shared and showcased as a way to promote 
the return of value to each community, in the spirit of the very definition of circular economy, and their replicability.  
 Awareness raising module: Product acceptability will be sought through this interactive module. The results obtained in WP8 in relation 
to the environmental impacts, economic benefi ts, social impacts, regulatory issues, etc., will be shared for increased transparency and 
awareness raising in the use of biobased products. 
 National and European engagement module: The results of the application of best practices in each of the pilots wi ll be shared in the 
form of interactive factsheets, as obtained in WP3 for each one of the pilots, to promote replicability.  
Task 7.3. Development of the Backend (M10 – M48). Partners involved: VISUM, ITENE, CSCP, NS, MADRID, LAZIO, CLUBE, Lund, FCC  
This task involves backend programming activities (coding) to implement the architecture defined in Task 7.1. The work will be bro ken down 
into backlogs that will be developed in Sprints of typically 2 to 3 weeks in duration. A data warehouse will be developed  to store, integrate, 
retain and process results for data gathered by the waste managers and other stakeholders along the value chain. The source i nformation 
will be analysed in terms of source data structure, connection methods and data gathering strategy  required (either access to existing 
databases, import or import and synchronisation). Validation documents with unit tests will be created to ensure that data ar e correctly 
accessed/imported/synchronised. Based on this analysis, data models will be designed to store new information. A cloud web server with the 
INPUT API will be running and ready to receive data and it will be verified that new stored data fits the validation document  and that unit 
tests are working successfully. After passing the INPUT API , the data gathered will flow between the different layers of the architecture 
before reaching the database, where it will be stored. 
Task 7.4. Development of the Front-end (M10 – M48). Partners involved: VISUM, ITENE, CSCP, NS, MADRID, LAZIO, CLUBE, Lund, FCC 
This task also involves programming activities (coding), as well as graphical design and User Experience, both for PC -based and Mobile based 
GUI for each level of users. Screenshots or ‘mock ups’ of User Interface concepts will be made available to the consortium for discussion and 
approval prior to front-end coding. The front-end will be designed to be gender inclusive. 
Task 7.5. Software integration (M15 – M48). Partners involved: VISUM, ITENE, CSCP, NS, MADRID, LAZIO, CLUBE, Lund, FCC 
This task will involve the integration of the different modules, front end and back end as will have been defined in the architecture 
established in Task 7.1. As such, our Scrum Teams of developers will discuss backlogs with the relevant partners so that codi ng work can be 
executed. Again, according to the Scrum Methodology, backlogs will be developed in iterative Sprints each ending with a demo to the parties 
concerned.  
Task 7.6. Testing and Optimisation work (M18 – M48). Partners involved: VISUM, ITENE, CSCP, NS, MADRID, LAZIO, CLUBE, Lund, FCC 
According to established QA, Functional Testing followed by Non -Functional Testing will be carried out. A test environment that virtually 
simulates will be built for debugging and validating the functionalities of the SCALIBUR C loud Platform. The Simulator will allow testing 
automatically the main modules as standalone units as well as the whole system in defined cases study. The Simulator is consi dered an 
internal development tool which will not be delivered but finished and use d according to the specific schedule for the programming work. 
Each platform release will be run through a series of regression tests (system, performance, etc.) to detect undiscovered or developer -
introduced defects, and will involve cloud assessment, moving of data, moving of applications, leveraging the cloud (improved security etc.) and 
optimization.  
An online User Manual will be delivered, along with online tutorials. Furthermore, during the last year, a training workshop will allow 
introducing in liv e the platform more in depth to different users especially in terms of its smart modules such as multi actor optimisation 
modelling tools whereby practical cases will be covered at the Urban Biowaste Clubs. 
Deliverables: 
D7.1 Architecture for the SCALIBUR Cloud Platform including planed quality measures (VISUM; M10)  
D7.2 SCALIBUR Platform Alpha release (VISUM; M22)  
D7.3 SCALIBUR Platform Online User Manual and result of quality testing (VISUM; M32)  
D7.4 SCALIBUR Platform Beta release (VISUM; M47)

Objectives: To assess environmental, techno -economic, social impacts and safety aspects of SCALIBUR processes . The approach used will 
follow the findings and methologies proposed by STAR-ProBio (Sustainability Transition Assessment and Research of Bio -based Products) 
funded under H2020 BBI-01-2016: Sustainability schemes for the bio-based economy. The overall sustainability assessment will integrate the 
synergies and trade-offs of the project, and will present the information complementing that produced in STAR- ProBio project, including the 
democases based on biowaste to bioproducts supply chains. Specific objectives are: 
 deliver an environmental and techno-economic evaluation of the whole SCALIBUR processes.  
 report on the potential contribution to renewable energy and GHG emission reduction targets derived from SCALIBUR implementation 
 report on social benefits (such as the creation of highly skilled jobs, social innovation, urban biowaste management in citie s, and the 
policy implications and recommendations) will be carried out. 
 Safety and regulatory assements for all products produced. 
 Demonstrate sustainability of the developed processes. 
Task 8.1: Definitions, settings and system description (M1-M16). Partners Involved: ITENE, All 
T8.1 will provide the goal and scope of the assessment as well as all initial settings, including technological parameters, for inputing T8.2 to 8.8. 
 Information on current collection, transport and final disposal  of the OFMSW, USS and HORECA and ROW in the pilot municipalities, as 
compiled in WP2. LCA of the selective collection for these fractions will be done with information from all partners.  
 A LCA of SCALIBUR supply chains  requires data of the full lifecycle of biobased products production, which will include all the necessary 
steps, from cradle-to-grave, for the production and final use of the biobased products in corresponding applications. The lifecycle may 
consist, depending on the specific scenario, of the following steps: feedstock generation, transportation modes, conversion p rocess to 
intermediate feedstocks, transportation to plant, processing, bio -based product transportation & distribution / use. When specific data 
gaps have been identified, suitable proxies will be selected and used. 
 ITENE and CENER will prepare and send to all partners guidelines and templates for data collection. They will carry out the collection of 
the main information related to the LCA of the processes developed within WP4 -6. Afterwards, they will produce qualitative process 
flow diagrams (PFDs) of SCALIBUR supply chains. 
 After that, ITENE and CENER will build the life cycle of current and new management systems. Results obtained from the life cycle analysis in 
terms of GHG emissions for the current disposal of the organic solid waste, will be used to compar e the current situation with the 
valorisation processes developed during SCALIBUR, which will define the baseline for sustainability assessment on environmental, economic & 
social issues.  
Task 8.2: Modelling and integration of the SCALIBUR process (M1 – M48). Partners Involved: EXERGY, all 
T8.2 will integrate the three processes developed in WPs4 -6 into one process. The overall concept will be demonstrated through simulations 
by using commercial software (AspenOne \  SuperPro). The objective of this task is  also to prove the technical, and later economic feasibility 
of the SCALIBUR concept in order to progress towards future commercialization of the process. A detailed flowsheet will be pr epared which 
will be used as the basis of process simulation once proc ess data has been collected from the previous work packages. Each individual 
module from Wps4-6 will be simulated separately first. Integration of all three modules (where possible) into one process will be followed. 
The process parameters in the integrated model will be optimized and the heat & mass balance will be carried out. The simulation results will 
allow the comparison between theoretical and empirical data (from the pilot / demo plants), which will provide an insight int o process 
equipment design, and will be beneficial for future development such as pilot / demo plants trouble shooting and sensitivity studies. A 
potential scale -up case study, an industrial scale simulation model and basic engineering for the main equipment and streams will be 
described. The outcome of this task will be used to evaluate the environmental and economic impacts of the project in terms of ene rgy and 
mass streams.  
Task 8.3: Techno-economic assessment of the processes (M1 – M48). Partners Involved: EXERGY, all 
This task will analyze and optimize, where possible, the economic feasibility of the proposed process and the different biobased product s on 
the outputs from previous WPs and the process simulation results from T8.2. The results of the techno -economic assessment will  be 
assessed through a sensitivity analysis as well as a risk analysis (which will identify favorable and non -favorable scenarios, such as price 
variations in the market) in order to determine potential hot spots in the process which can affect the feasibi lity of the technology and to 
determine if it is better to commercialize the process as a whole or in modules. The TEA will also provide sufficient informa tion to compare 
the proposed process with current solutions from an economic perspective by using met hods such as cost -benefit analysis and discounted 
cash flow, and by determining information such as cost of production and minimum sell price.  
Task 8.4: Environmental Life Cycle Assessment (M4 – M48). Partners Involved: CENER, ITENE, NOVAMONT 
Environmental impacts associated with the value chains identified in T8.1 in comparison to their reference systems will be evaluated and 
periodically updated along the project. The environmental sustainability assessment will follow the next approach: 
 Identification of environmental impacts to be considered. According to processes/technologies studied in this project, highly relevant 
environmental impacts that will be evaluated in detail are: fossil energy consumption and GHG emissions.  
 Definition of indicators and methodologies to evaluate environmental sustainability criteria of the environmental impacts.  
 References for the definition of sustainability methodologies include Guidelines of ISO 14040/14044 on product life cycle assessment, 
RED Directive (including subsequent ILUC Directive, and future RED II Directive); Standards and criteria established by Working Group 4 
“Sustainability criteria, life cycle analysis and related issues” of CEN/TC 411 “Bio-based products”. 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
56 
  
 Evaluation of environmental sustainability  of t he supply chains developed in the project by LCA methodology. The LCAs will be 
performed using dedicated software (SIMAPRO) and the Ecoinvent database. 
 Sensitivity analysis, to identify key points & assess sustainability results changes by modifying proces ses/products parameters and/or 
methodologies.  
 Updates of sustainability assessments, according to future modifications on processes/products considered in the project. 
 The LCAs will be performed using dedicated software  (e.g. SIMAPRO software) and the Eco invent database for a selected set of raw 
material (urban biowaste)/production process/product, taking into account use and disposal or re-use, i.e. ‘from cradle-to-grave’. 
Results will be interpreted and presented to the partners, who will work in the def inition of strategies to minimize the environmental 
impacts of the developed processes. CENER will conduct the LCAs for WP4, while ITENE will carry out the LCAs related to WPs5&6. 
Task 8.5: Social evaluation (M4 – M48). Partners Involved: ITENE, all 
The social analysis of the final products assesses the social and socio -economic aspects of materials or processes and their potential positive 
and negative impacts along their life cycle. These aspects assessed in are those that may directly or indirectly affec t stakeholders, including 
workers, local community, consumers, value chain actors and society. SLCA also follows a life cycle approach, but the impacts  in this case are 
related to socio-economic processes and comprise human rights, working conditions, heal th and safety, socio-economic repercusion, and so 
forth. This task is intimately related with T2.4, where the project impact will be analysed. 
Therefore, social analysis will be focused on the acceptance of SCALIBUR concept by users and citizens. Initially  ITENE and CENER with the 
collaboration of the partners will develop the list of indicators, based on the UNEP -SETAC guidelines on SLCA, to be taken into account in the 
social analysis. Based on these indicators, questionnaires will be prepared and sent to  the partners as well as citizens of municipalities 
involved in the SCALIBUR project. The questionnaires will also be available at the interactive SCALIBUR stakeholder platform (WP7) and 
promoted through the project communication actions (WP9) so as to rea ch wider audiences. Information will be compiled, analysed and 
modelled with a view to obtain the SLCA models, which will be periodically updated. Finally, results will be interpreted and presented to the 
partners, and definition and discussion of strategies to improve the social viability and consumer/social acceptance will be done. 
Task 8.6: Safety assessment (M4 – M48). Partners Involved: NS, all 
The presence of mycotoxins and pesticides in project outcomes will be measured by chromatographic methods. LC /MS methods will be 
applied for the detection of common mycotoxins and GC -MS multi-residue method will be applied for determination of the main classes of 
pesticides found in the resulting products in WPs4 -6. The presence of antibiotics will also be measur ed by LC/MS and GC/MS. The presence 
of Salmonella and Enterobacteriaceae, E. coli and Enterococcus and heavy metals (As, Pb, Hg) will be determined as well. 
Task 8.7: Regulatory assessment (M1 – M48). Partners Involved: UNIMORE, NS, all 
T8.7.1 Legal support in authorisation procedures and in any other task of the project  (M1-M48). The legal unit will  overview the applicable 
provisions, in order to offer support to the technical units in obtaining or extending the required administrative authorisat ion for re search 
on byproducts and waste. Legal advice will be provided in any issue that will arise during the whole project performance. 
T8.7.2 Waste and byproducts: legal aspects  (M1-M5). Desk research on the EU provisions on waste and byproducts will be carried out, 
through the study of binding acts, soft law, case law and literature, in order to understand how the EU provisions cope with the international 
framework and how EU Member States have implemented supranational law (Antonini -Andreozzi, 2012; Benozzo, 20 13; Alabrese, 2014;). 
Differences among legislations that could hinder the implementation of the research results will be pointed out. The results will help to 
evaluate the opportunity to submit a proposal for an EU Regulation on waste. 
T8.7.3 Insect rearing: legal aspects (M6-M10). Through a desk research the unit will collect all the EU useful provisions that could apply to 
insect farming but that were adopted for other animals, in order to evaluate their suitability for this new type of farming. Aims of the task 
are identifying the weak points of the existing provisions and suggesting some improvements in a regulatory draft. 
T8.7.4 Products from biowaste: legal aspects (M21- M42).  
For all the bio -based products obtained in SCALIBUR value chains: bioplast ics, biopesticides, compounds for food and feed, and other 
compounds from insects, an overview of the EU and national legislation will be analysed. Amending proposals will be suggested , with the 
aim of improving EU and national laws, taking into account the development of new technologies. 
T.8.7.5 Use of compounds originated from insects in food  (M16-M20). The novel food Regulation and the subsequent implementing 
Regulations of December 2017, as well as literature and possible case law, will be analysed in order to understand the legal status of 
compounds originated from insects. Notification and authorisation procedures will be monitored.  
T.8.7.6 Use of compounds originated from insects in feed (M21-M23). According to the technical research that will be ca rried out, the legal 
units will offer support in investigating the applicable provisions on the use of insects in feed and submitting a possible a pplication for 
amending the EU feed catalogue. Case law and academic contributions will be taken into account. 
T.8.7.7 Other uses of compounds originated from insects  (M27-M32). The last part of the investigation will focus on other possible uses of 
compounds originated from insects and on applicable provisions. Amending proposals will be suggested, with the aim o f improving EU and 
national laws, taking into account the development of new technologies.  
T.8.7.8 Bioplastics (M33-M39). An overview of the applicabile provisions on bioplastics will be carried out in order to obtain a complete 
framework on the topic. This will allow to support any involved units in carrying out their activities. 
T.8.7.9 Biopesticides (M40-M44). A deep investigation on the provisions applicable to pesticides will be performed, in order to evaluate the 
suitability of the products obtained to be placed on the market.  
T.8.7.10 Enzymes (M45-48). The regulatory framework on the use of enzymes in industrial processing other than the food ones will be 
investigated in order to understand if it limits in any way the project outcomes. 
Task 8.8: Sustainability assessment (M1 – M48). Partners Involved: ITENE, all 
This task is focused on an integrated analysis of the results obtained in the environmental, economic and social study, to bu ild a complete 
sustainability assessment. Comparative analysis will be done between the initial disposal of urban biowaste and the final valorisation processes. 
Deliverables

D8.2. First sustainability report: Environmental, Economic and Social LCA (ITENE; M24) 
D8.3. Techno-economic analysis of the SCALIBUR value chains (EXERGY; M48)
