Objectives: The main objective of this work package is to conduct focused dissemination and replication actions towards key quadruple hel ix 
stakeholders in the urban biowaste value chain, specially in relation to cities, waste generators and managers. Specific objectives are: 
 To ensure effective branding of SCALIBUR and disseminate key results to a large community of users, including municipalities,  
waste managers, investors, current and future entrepreneurs, as well as citizens and local communities. 
 To raise awareness on biowaste collection and recycling solutions and foster the replication of good practices at all levels 
Task 9.1. Communication strategy and tools (M1 – M48). Partners involved: G!E, VISUM, All 
Subtask 9.1.1 – Communication and Dissemination plan: A detailed awareness and communication plan at the beginning of the project (M6) 
outlining the target audiences, key messages and communication channels for the project w ill be produced. Based on the stakeholder 
mapping carried out in WP2, the plan will include a first mapping of the project’s expected results and the identification of  relevant 
audiences and communication channels. The consortium will be regularly consulted to adapt the planned activities to actual results’ delivery. 
This plan will outline WHO (target audiences) will receive WHAT (key messages), HOW (communication channels) and WHEN 
(implementation and time planner) with updates in M24 and M48. G!E will dev elop a professional communication package at the beginning 
of the project, a final logo, a tagline, a visual identity, document templates, definition of key messages and project written identity. As the 
main landing page for the project, the website –  to b e developed by IRIS/VISUM, in close coordination with G!E  –   will present: project 
objectives, expected results, project’s progress, reports and recommendations, relevant events, and a dedicated media space. It will be 
directly linked to social media (Twi tter, Facebook, LinkedIn and YouTube), where SCALIBUR will actively promote the project’s outcomes to 
both professional and public networks. The project website will integrate the Stakeholder Platform. Website content will be m anaged and 
updated by G!E on a regular basis and the structure will be adapted throughout the project to reflect project’s achievements. 
Subtask 9.1.2 – Communication material: A comprehensive set of communication material, comprising a project leaflet, to be produced in 
English, for use at EU -level activities and international conferences, as well as a poster template, that can be used and adapted by project 
partners for targeted events. Five roll -up banners, including one in English and one in each of the local languages of the Pilot  Cities will be 
integrated in this package for local and international dissemination events. To foster dissemination within the Pilot Cities,  a flyer template, 
will also be produced. Sustainable printing options, such as the use of recyclable or compostable paper, and bio-based ink will be selected.  
Additionally, a set of 3 one-minute animated videos will be produced to raise awareness on the 3 main valorisation lines. Videos will be used 
for wider promotion on social media and other online platforms. As t he main landing page for the project, the website (to be developed by 
IRIS/VISUM, in close coordination with G!E) will present: project objectives, expected results, project’s progress, reports a nd 
recommendations, relevant events, and a dedicated media sp ace. It will be directly linked to social media (Twitter, Facebook, LinkedIn and 
YouTube), where SCALIBUR will actively promote the project’s outcomes to both professional and public networks. The project w ebsite will 
integrate the Stakeholder Platform and  will be designed to be gender inclusive. Website content will be managed and updated by G!E on a 
regular basis and the structure will be adapted throughout the project to reflect project’s achievements. 
Task 9.2. Communication activities (M1 – M48). Partners involved: G!E, All 
Subtask 9.2.1 – Media relations will be key to raise awareness of the general public. The project will engage in a local and international media 
relation strategy. At the beginning of the project, a database of European and national media contacts will be established with the 
cooperation of all partners. This database will be updated on a regular basis, and throughout the whole duration of the proje ct, journalists 
identified will be engaged via social media content, news and press rel eases. Targeted communication tools, (media space on the project 
website) and the distribution of a designed media pack containing pictures, captions, data visuals and infographics, as well as key quotes and 
figures, will facilitate journalists’ access to information about the project and its major outcomes.  
Subtask 9.2.2 – Online communication: As SCALIBUR results are being published, a series of interviews and feature articles will be published 
on the project website, distributed on EC communication chan nels and to selected media, and translated in national languages, whenever 
relevant. From M18, G!E will circulate a project newsletter to interested stakeholders on a regular basis.  
Social media are a strategic communication channel to reach out to a wide  number of stakeholders. To tap their full potential, G!E will 
integrate a dedicated social media strategy to the project’s communication and awareness plan. This will include recommendati ons to 
ensure the correct usage of social media platforms by project  partners, and a detailed content plan. Infographics, data visuals, key quotes as 
well as short video interviews with SCALIBUR local champions will be used to maximise audience and interaction on social networks.  
Subtask 9.2.3 – Pan-European awareness raising campaign: To maximise communication impact towards the end of the project, G!E will also 
coordinate the organisation of a pan-European awareness raising campaign on urban biowaste sorting and recycling between M42 and M44. 
During the campaign, which c omplements actions in WP2, each Pilot City will organise happening events in public spaces such as markets 
and supermarkets, to raise awareness on biowaste collection and new products developed from biowaste recycling. Live intervie ws with 
famous “ambassadors” for waste collection and sorting, as well as with local champions and citizens, will be organised and retransmitted on 
social media via live streaming during the events. These events will be the opportunity to assess and test citizens’ awareness throu gh mini-
questionnaires.

Throughout this campaign, citizens will be invited to participate in a competition to select the most innovative social innovation idea for waste

their city. Users will be invited to interact and to campaign for their favourite idea on social networks via a dedicated has htag. Each 
participating citizen will be offered to take part in a raffle to win prom otional gifts. The most popular social innovation idea/business model 
selected through this competition in each city will be presented at the occasion of the final event in Brussels. 
Subtask 9.2.4 – Conferences and networking: SCALIBUR will engage dialogue with policy representatives by face to face meetings with representatives 
from European institutions and relevant sectoral associations to discuss potential regulatory barriers at European level and promote the 
biowaste initiatives developed. Furthermore, project partners will participate in relevant conferences, events and fairs to promote SCALIBUR 
to various stakeholders, including business owners, investors and researchers, throughout the whole duration of the project.  
Task 9.3. Dissemination activities (M6 – M48). Partners involved: G!E, All 
Subtask 9.3.1 – Local dissemination will ensure successful implementation of SCALIBUR project’s solutions in the Pilot Cities and wider 
replication throughout EU. In each Pilot City, dissemination workshops targeti ng schools and municipal staff, complementing co -creation 
workshops in WP2, will be organised to foster the replication of best practices with at least 1 intervention in a school and 1 workshop / Pilot.  
Subtask 9.3.2 – Scientific dissemination: The project will also produce 10 plus articles and scientific presentations. Open access articles will be 
published in peer -reviewed and/or technical publications (national and international) journals to share the results with the scientific 
community. Scientific presentations will be delivered on the occasion of relevant sectorial events, which list will be collectively established in 
the first 6 months of the project and updated annually as part of the awareness and communication Plan (see initial list in Section 2.2).  
Subtask 9.3.3 – Final multi-stakeholder event: In M46-M48, G!E will organise a Final EU-level multi-stakeholder event in Brussels (approx. 100 
participants) dedicated to lessons learned and policy recommendations towards wider replication. The event,  to be organised in cooperation 
with a relevant sectoral association (such as Municipal Waste Europe, or ACR+) at the Committee of the Regions or the Europea n Economic 
and Social Committee, will bring together high -profile experts, local, national and European decision -makers, investors, as well as members 
from all Regional Urban Biowaste clubs and representatives from Early Adopter Cities. This event will allow sharing results on integrated models 
for urban biowaste valorisation, and discuss regulatory and  market barriers, while launching the project’s policy recommendations. Relevant 
international & national media contacts will be invited to take part in a press conference focusing on the project’s results and recommendations.

Objectives: To define a durable exploitation strategy for each result and develop replicable business plans to ensure successful market 
uptake of the technologies and products to be created within the project. Specific objectives of this work package are: 
 To produce a detailed exploitation plan and develop adapted business models for each project result to secure their market uptake; 
 To explore and report o n further research opportunities and develop policy recommendations to facilitate market uptake and unlock 
potential barriers to commercialisation beyond the project’s end; 
 To conduct targeted capacity-building activities to ensure Europe-wide deployment of urban biowaste management strategies; 
Task 10.1. Exploitation strategy and tools (M1 – M48). Partners involved: G!E/VMT, all 
Subtask 10.1.1 – Exploitation plan: This plan will define joint exploitation and marketing activities by the consortium aiming to  leverage 
impact by streamlining individual market exploitation efforts towards concerted activities (first version by M12 and a consol idated version by 
M46):  
 Definition of the exploitable results and their routes to market. 
 Development of joint business models by using the business model canvas.  
 Market appraisal: existing and currently emerging markets, competitors and competing solutions. Inclusion of new applications & markets. 
 IPR analysis and agreement of (joint) exploitation interests of partners and on IP ownership in compliance with freedom to operate. 
 Market deployment strategies for SCALIBUR products including branding, lobbying, advertising, and other promotion activities. 
 Standardisation and development of specifications for SCALIBUR products and intermediates. 
 Most suitable site locations/integration options for operation plants. 
 Realisation of single processes of the process chain versus a series of processes with mutual integration. 
 Economic competition between different applications of SCALIBUR products and intermediates. 
 Funding and financing models and opportunities for first installations. 
 Exploitation risks analysis. 
 Key market and regulatory barriers and recommendations to overcome these barriers. 
 Further research opportunities beyond the end of the project. 
Subtask 10.1.2 – Validation and refining of exploitation strategies : VMT will act as coach and coordinator for all exploitation tasks. Annual 
Exploitation Workshops involving all partners will be organized with project meetings to reduce costs and ensure maximum involvement: 
 Initial Exploitation Workshop (M6): Introduction to exploitation challenges, methodologies and identification of exploitable results. 
 Mid-term Exploitation Workshop (M24): Clarification of exploitable results, dev elopment of exploitation options and identification of 
uncertainties (risks and opportunities). Pre-assessment of the market potential of key results and of exploitation options. 
 Final Exploitation Workshop (M42): Risk Response Plan and consolidation of draft business models and plans for each key exploitable result. 
Subtask 10.1.3 (Lead G!E) – Research and policy uptake : In close cooperation with the Urban Biowaste Clubs and WP2 actions, policy

recommendations will be developed (see D2.3) and integrated in  the Final Exploitation plan at the end of the project, and presented at the 
European Parliament. The report will also include further research opportunities for project sustainability.  
Task 10.2. Business case definition (M1 – M48). Partners involved: G!E/VMT, All 
Subtask 10.2.1 – Market analysis : To define what new innovative applications for SCALIBUR products, intermediates, services and 
technologies would be the most attractive beyond the project’s end. The Exploitation leader will follow up emerging d evelopments and 
markets, including both novel applications and markets emerging from scientific and technological progress. If relevant, iden tified 
opportunities will be integrated in the exploitation strategy. Additionally, concrete business cases will be  developed and integrated into the 
final Exploitation Plan.  
Subtask 10.2.2 – Value proposition will be implemented to assess the value for money for each function offered by SCALIBUR products and 
services, by looking at what constitutes the real value of such products/services for their potential end -users, asking three main questions: (i) 
What users’ problems could be solved with SCALIBUR new products and services? (ii) What functionalities would need to be added or modified 
to meet users’ needs? and (iii) What functionalities can be reduced or eliminated, as they do not add any value for users? 
This will increase SCALIBUR products’ and services’ suitability for market exploitation and allow developers to better allocate the investment 
where its market potential is the highest. Secondly, a value analysis will be performed to quantify the value of the new products, followed by 
an assessment of users’ willingness to pay based on estimate costs for each of the different functions. Finally, the prices i dentified will be 
compared with development, industrialisation and marketing costs to assess financial sustainability and potential profit margins. 
Subtask 10.2.2 – IPR protection and agreements: The IPR management strategy will help avoid future conflicts among t he partners regarding 
(Joint) Ownership, Access Rights and Freedom to Operate, issues related to the dissemination of research Results versus secre cy for 
commercial/competition purposes, and standardisation issues. G!E/VMT will discuss what protection stra tegy fits the best for each 
Exploitable Result. The project will include an IP directory, chaired by G!E/VMT as Exploitation Leader, listing all relevant  IP brought in and 
developed by project partners, which will allo for a proactive and regular dialogue on IP related issues to facilitate the development of 
agreements on Use and Access Rights and to develop the market uptake strategy as soon as possible. The findings and recommendations will 
be included in the exploitation plan.  
Task 10.3. Business modeling and business plans (M24 – M48). Partners involved: G!E/VMT, All 
Subtask 10.3.1 – Development of business models and plans for each key result: Based on the functional analysis in T10.2, a market appraisal 
will be performed by G!E/VMT with input from pro ject partners to further define the market conditions for each exploitable result, and 
provide an overview of future market trends and competing products and technologies. Building on the findings, the consortium  will develop 
business models and business plans for each KER after the mid-term exploitation workshop, to be integrated in the final Exploitation Plan. 
Subtask 10.3.2 – Testing and validation of the business models with end-users: This task focuses on early interactions with future customers to 
otain early feedback by testing and validating the business model options in a three-step approach: 
 Clarifying the “specifications” of the targeted end-users (via phone and email contact) 
 “Recruitment” of the potential end -users capable of becoming realistic early adopters, including request for feedback (through 
questionnaires), and invitation to participate in replication and training activities. 
 Capture and strategic analysis of feedback, leading to a review and update of the value proposition and business models. 
The Advisory Board will also be periodically invited to provide feedback on the Exploitation Plan, in particular to help to v alidate the 
characterisation of exploitable results and the draft business models. 
Task 10.4. Standardisation (M1 – M48). Partners involved: ITENE, All 
To safeguard the potential of the products developed within the project for commercialisation, functional requirements for th eir 
standardisation will be established, based on results from LCA. Novel laboratory and field test me thods developed by SCALIBUR will reported 
in the form of feedback to the CEN standardisation process. Results will be integrated into the final Exploitation Plan.  
Task 10.5. Replicability actions (M1 – M48). Partners involved: G!E, All 
Subtask 10.5.1 – Early Adopter Cities (Leader: G!E; Participants: All)  To foster large- scale replication of the solutions developed within the 
SCALIBUR project, a small group of Early Adopter Cities will be constituted in the first half of the project. Interested cities will  be invited to 
join the club of Early Adopter Cities. 
Subtask 10.5.2 – Training kit for municipalities, communities and entrepreneurs (Leader: G!E/GEO; Participants: All), including sets of slides with 
speaking notes, detailed documentation about the techn ologies developed within the project and associated business models, citizen 
engagement strategies, as well as information on regulatory compliance and performances, will be developed by M30, and will b e the basis 
for the development of a e-learning platform. To be developed in a Responsive Web Design (RWD) and maintained by G!E/GEO, the e -
Learning platform will have an easy-to-follow structure with clear, gender-inclusive graphics, focusing on presenting the value of the content 
with interactive exercises.  
The e-Learning platform will include a set of online courses divided into two training modules that will be made available beyond t he end of 
the project: one oriented towards potential replicating municipalities and local communities, while the other wil l target future and current 
entrepreneurs. The platform will also include downloadable reference documents and useful links, an “Ask the Tutor” function,  and a Forum 
area to allow users to interact, ask questions and leave comments. A registration procedur e will be set up in order to monitor the feedback 
based on the type of users and evaluate eLearning effectiveness, to complement the engagement analysis in WP2.  
Task 10.6. Capacity building (M1 – M48). Partners involved: G!E, All 
To secure replication of the business models identified within the project, G!E/VMT will develop a common concept for the organisation of 
replication and capacity building activities with potential end-users, both for the social innovation business models for municipalities, and for 
business models related to the innovative technologies developed within the project.  
Subtask 10.6.1 – Training workshops (Leader: G!E; Participants: All): For the municipalities, G!E will organise training workshops in Early 
Adopter Cities, with repres entatives from the project’s Pilot Cities, as well as members from the club of Early Adopter Cities and regional 
Urban Biowaste Clubs, to present the social innovation business models and advice cities on how to replicate these business m odels and 
integrate them in their local framework, using the results from WP2. Using the material developed for the training kit, G!E/VMT/GEO w ill 
give a dedicated and personalised training to up to five Early adopter Cities.  
Subtask 10.6.2 – Coaching programme (Leader: G!E/VMT; Participants: All): G!E/VMT will develop a coaching programme for 10 entrepeneurs 
from different countries wishing to create or upscale a business in the urban biowaste valorisation sector. The entrepreneurs  will be

3.2 MANAGEMENT STRUCTURE AND PROCEDURES  
ORGANISATIONAL STRUCTURE AND PROCEDURES 
The management structure of SCALIBUR is pr esented below, considering the development of this project to 
produce bio-based products from biowaste. ITENE will play a central role as project coordinator. SCALIBUR involves 
5 management bodies consisting of General Assembly (GA), an Executive Board (EB ), Innovation Committee (IC), 
The Advisory Board (AB), and the project coordinator. 
 
Figure 11. SCALIBUR Management structure 
The responsibilities and decision -making structures will be defined in more detail in the Consortium Agr eement, 
covering different aspects of the project (such as. management issues, intellectual property aspects, licensing rights 
of the project, including ownership of knowledge, protection of that knowledge and access rights).  
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.
CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
62 
  
The General Assembly (GA) is chaired by the Coordinator (ITENE) with a representative of each partner, as a 
decision-making and conflict resolution body. The GA will be responsible for the overall strategic orientation 
and policy of the project, as well as ensuring that the adopted strategy is respected to reach excellence. The 
General Assembly will meet physically at least every 6 months, exceptional sessions (telephone or web 
conference) may be called upon and organized when needed or requested. Before making any decision, 
quorum of at least 50% of the GA members will be necessary and simple majority will do ruling. The 
coordinator will have casting vote. 
An Executive Board (EB) is in charged of monitoring the effective and efficient implementation of the project. It 
will be chaired by the Coordinator and completed by the WP leaders. EB will also benefit from the support of a 
management team (MST) to ensure day to day operational project management and will meet face-to-face at 
least every 6 months. Regular meetings by teleconference/Skype will be organized once per month, or when 
needed/requested. Quorum of at least 50% of the EB members will be necessary before taking any decision 
and simple majority will apply. The coordinator will have casting vote. The members of the EB will be validated 
by the members of the GA. 
The Innovation Committee (IC) will deal with the innovation activities, namely Impact management, RRI & 
engagement, IPR & exploitation, Communication & Dissemination, Data Management and Scientific 
management. Appointed managers will constitute the Management Support Team (MST). The IC will meet 
face-to-face at least twice a year, and additional meetings by teleconference/Skype will be organized when 
needed or requested. Quorum of at least 2/3 of the IC members will be necessary before taking any decision, 
and decisions will be taken by 2/3 majority. The following Innovation Managers are appointed: 
 The Impact Management will be Antonio Dobon (ITENE), as leader of WP 1 and 8, in charge of maximising 
the impact, monitoring of success project indicators at all levels, and promote maximum policy influence 
through advocacy actions, policy-society dialogues and other actions 
 The RRI and Engagement Management will be Nora Brueggemann (CSCP), as leader of WP2, in charge 
of maximising the multi-level engagement of key stakeholders and communities, monitoring the success 
project indicators at community level, and maximising the outreach of all RRI dimensions in relation to 
project execution.  
 The IPR and Exploitation managers will be Gosse Hiemstra, Van der Meer & Van Tilburg  (G!E), managing 
IPR and project exploitation (plan and implementation) beyond the project lifetime. 
 The Communication and Dissemination Manager will be Valeria Mazzagatti  (G!E), leader of WP9 and 10, 
who will be totally aligned with the project multi-level engagement plan for increased outreach. 
 The Scientific Manager will be Ines del Campo (CENER), leader of WP4, in charge of scientific validation, 
guaranteeing scientific excellence when addressing socio-environmental biowaste issues and scientific 
dissemination from the project results. She will guarantee objectivity and scientific soundness in the 
standardisation of the valorization methodologies. Moreover, she will define the impact criteria to be used 
as a base of future regulations. 
The Advisory Board (AB). By involving quadruple helix stakeholders, including policy makers and environmental 
authorities at different levels, odour emitting activities, research and academia, European Working Groups in 
biowaste management, NGOs and CSOs, influencing the policies is intended. An external Advisory Board will be 
formed from representatives of these categories and independent experts. The AB will be constituted in the 
first 6 months of the project by the project Coordinator. In Section 4, # letters of support from different 
stakeholders expressing their interest in joining SCALIBUR Advisory Board can be found, including national and 
regional governments, environmental authorities, academia, industry, municipalities associations, 
environmental journalist networks, city networks, research centres and civil organisations. 
The Project Coordinator will serve as an intermediary between the partners and the EC. It will ensure daily 
communication between partners and compliance with the internal quality processes. All tasks assigned to it 
will be described in the Grant Agreement Model, including the monitoring the compliance by the partners with 
proper project implementation, submitting the deliverables and reports to the EC, and ensuring that all 
payments are made without unjustified delay. 
SCALIBUR coordinator is Dr. Susana Aucejo. She has large experience in the development of innovative packaging 
materials and nanotechnology. She is an expert for the development of bio-based polymers, with more than 15 
years of experience working at ITENE. Currently, she is the R&D director at ITENE and has more than 10 years’ 
experience working with European projects. She has participated in over 50 research projects (national and 
European). Till date she has been responsible for 27 of these projects related to the development of innovative 
This proposal version was submitted by Susana AUCEJO on 13/02/2018 16:37:31 Brussels Local Time. Issued by the Participant Portal Submission Service.

solutions from bio-based products (e.g. OPTINANOPRO where new materials are validated for diverse applications 
in nanotechnology). She is co-author of more than 30 peer-reviewed scientific articles and is regularly involved in 
dissemination activities, being active in organizing national and international scientific conferences and symposium. 
She has also participated in several experts committee at both national and European level. 
MILESTONES AND PROCEDURES FOR MONITORING PROGRESS STATUS  
Technical and financial assessments of the whole project will be performed by the corresponding manager, and the 
final reports will be dis cussed in the GA meetings. During these meetings, the GA will assess the status of the 
project. Frequently monitoring of the operational the WP leaders will do a progress reports. Project achievements 
will be reviewed during GA meetings, as well as possibl e technical, financial and executive problems that may arise 
from the evolution of SCALIBUR. Periodic reviews will be also implemented as it is stated in the Grant Agreement. 
These reviews will be organized by the GA involving all participants and the EC when necessary. 
A more detailed list of rules for this consortium will be described in the Consortium Agreement to be evaluated and 
concluded prior its signature of the Grant Agreement. SCALIBUR Consortium Agreement will be based on the 
DESCA-2020
 model for large projects to balance and reflect the interests of all participants.  
A list of important milestones has been identified for SCALIBUR implementation (Table 3.2a) a nd will be monitored 
by the corresponding WP leaders and project coordinator. Milestones assessment will be reviewed upon the date 
of its achievement, and a report will be issued. In the case that a milestone has not been achieved on the expected 
date, the impact of this milestone in the WP and the course of SCALIBUR will be assessed. All these issues will be 
reviewed by the EB and, subsequently, they will report to the GA.

Knowledge management and communication (3.2.3): Project documentation will be stored and exchanged through 
the use of a private, password protected secure and confidential platform administrated by the Project 
Coordinator. All project members will be registered. Draft documents will be edited and stored following the 
project proposed templates. This platform will allow data and information exchanges between project members 
without unnecessary risk of external disclosure. SCALIBUR project will contribute to the Open Research Data aiming 
at improve and maximise access to and re-use of research data generated by projects. The consortium will make an 
inventory and review options for sharing of research data in a Data Management P lan (WP1). G!E will organize the 
dissemination of SCALIBUR results that will be reported and published in numerous ways (WP9).  
Intellectual Property Management: For optimum exploitation of the results, procedures addressed to the protection 
of IP will be considered for all significant new findings. All material published externally will be released by the EB 
and the quality will be assessed prior to publication. Moreover, all relevant information will be published (internally 
and externally) on the project website.

3.3 CONSORTIUM AS A WHOLE 
SCALIBUR consortium is a balanced combination of 6 SMEs (AERIS, ASA, EXERGY, KOUR, NS  and ZETACED), 3 large 
companies (FCC, NOVAMONT, SMVAK), 2 research organizations ( ITENE, CSCP, WETSUS), 2 non -profit associations 
(ITENE, CLUBE), 1 association (G!E), 3 companies (NS, VISUM, ZETADEC), 1 municipality (Lund), 2 public bodies 
(Madrid, LAZIO), 1 water authority (WBD), and  university (UNIMORE). Partners come from 9 different EU member 
countries: Spain, Italy, Germany, Ireland, The Netherlands, Greece, Sweden, Belgium and Czech Republic, 
SCALIBUR consortium covers the whole value chain, from biowaste recovery to valorization and characterization of 
the final bio -based products (proteins, lipids, chemical commodities, bioplastics, and biopestecides). The strategy 
followed in this project is focus on the exchange of knowledge, where all participants are involved through the 
whole value chain and life cycle of the project. Knowledge and know ‐how of the consortium covers all relevant

aspects of SCALIBUR vision. Large experience on EU -projects by most of the partners is beneficial to reach

the European level to obtain all the n ecessary resources to achieve SCALIBUR objectives. Co -creation of new 
strategies and business models involving citizens, 3 municipalities and relevant stakeholders will complete the 
circle, aiming also at new waste management policies.  
3.4. RESOURCES TO BE COMMITTED 
The financial resources mobilized by the 21 partners of the SCALIBUR project represent a total budget of 
12,005,922 €. The requested grant to carry out the proposed activities is 9,999,390 €. This relatively high budget is 
related to the ambition of the project and the large product portfolio to be obtained. 
Figures below show the budget distribution per cost category and per and per type of partner. 
 
  
 
Personnel costs [55% of total budget] 
A total of 1,32 3 person-month are foreseen, which gives an average of 28 people (or 1.3 persons per partner ) 
working full time for the project during its 4 years of duration. The average cost of the person -month is 5,021 
€/month, a very reasonable amount despite large differences exist among the personnel costs of partners (due to 
different costs per countries and different degree of specialisation of the work force required).

Organisation description 
 
INSTITUTO TECNOLOGICO DEL EMBALAJE, TRANSPORTE Y LOGISTICA ( ITENE) is a non -profit 
research centre specialized in packaging technologies, transport, logistics and circular economy. Our 
main activities are Research and development, Innovati on, Tests and advanced services, Market 
research and R&D Management. We are unique as we provide business solutions from a holistic 
vision along supply chain.  
ITENE has participated in 39 projects from FP6 and FP7 (some of the are currently in execution) and 
is currently involved in 10 H2020 projects. We will provide knowledge and expertise as a 
coordinator and will also make a robust contribution as a technical partner and key stakeholder for 
dissemination and communication purposes.    
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
ITENE uses 7,000 m2 of its installations as laboratories and experimentation facilities, equipped with 
the latest technology for research and testing, and product and services development. R&D 
activities are carried out in the following la boratories: Nano Additives and Nano Clay Pilot Plant, 
New Material Processing Pilot Plant, Nano Safety Laboratory, Chemical Laboratory, Physical 
Laboratory, Packaging Manufacturing Pilot Plant, Packaging Pilot Plant, Microbiology Laboratory, 
Packaging Eval uation Laboratory, Transport Simulation Centre, RFID Pilot Plant, and Packaging 
Waste Pilot Plant. 
Software: SimaPro software and access to the Ecoinvent database, two -well recognized sources for 
Life Cycle Assessment. 
The main areas ITENE is involved in the Scalibur project are: 
Overall coordination. ITENE will act as project coordinator, having been selected for its great 
experience. 
Sustainability: this department will lead the management WP and hence the project. Within the 
WP2 ITENE will participate in  social engagement activities, especially in those that affect the 
municipalities and the waste managers. ITENE will directly work with the municipalities to define 
the real situation regarding the collection of organic waste and its quality. We will suppo rt WP7 by 
designing together with the municipalities and the External Support committee the acceptance 
campaigns of the waste -based products and the selective collection awareness actions. ITENE will 
also lead the WP8 developing the LCA LCC and SLCA.  
Transport & Sustainability: Support in WP3 to define the waste requirements for treatment in the 
four technological lines of the project (drying, stabilization of waste). Development of actions to 
improve the collection logistics, the waste quality and its use  in the treatment processes to obtain 
products with high added value.  
New advanced Materials: This department will participate in WP4 and WP6 with the production and 
validation for packaging applications of the biopolymers obtained in the processes develo p within 
these WP, biopolyesters and PHA, respectively. A full characterization, the evaluation of the 
processability and Food contact certification of these new biobased polymers will be performed. 
Regarding WP5, ITENE will produce chitosan and chitin nan owiskers for the reinforcement of 
biocomposites for packaging applications. 
Technology Transfer / Business development :  Support in dissemination activities and product / 
technology exploitation plans within the WP10

2. AERIS

Organisation 
description 
 
AERIS is a spin-off of the Autonomous University of Barcelona comprising experts from the GENOCOV 
research group (U AB) aimed at helping industries and public entities to improve the environmental 
quality of their emissions. AERIS has a large experience designing and building highly automated pilot 
plants for research purposes. These are always developed according to th e specific customer needs. 
This includes fermenters, air -lift reactors, sequencing batch reactors (SBR), photobioreactors, etc. 
Also, other of AERIS main business areas is the optimization of the biological and/or physico -chemical 
depuration of natural and  industrial liquid streams containing nutrients, COD and/or recalcitrant 
compounds. In this field, numerous R+D and technological implementation projects have been 
carried out in the last years, mostly in paper-producing, tannery and food industries. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
Despite being a company with less than 10 years of life, Aeris has great experience in participating in 
publicly funded projects. Aeris currently participates in 5 projects financed by the EU (three RISE, one 
CIRC and one SMART), integrated in different aspects of the environmental field. Aeris has the ability 
to develop tailor-made pilot plants, with a high level of sensorization and autonomy, valid for 
research in the environmental field.  
Within the the SCALIBUR project Aeris will execute the tasks of obtaining high added value products 
from the solid fraction obtained from the hydrolysis of the OFMSW. 
Key personnel curriculum

Engineering, with PhD Extraordinary Quality Prize. His areas of expertise include the design and 
operation of biological reactors for biomass production and related products and for degradation of 
pollutants. He has published more than 30 references in  these fields and has wide experience in 
management and development of both national and European projects.

origin. He has more than 140 publications in international scientific journals and has participated as

Organisation 
 description 
 
The business activities of ASA Spezialenzyme GmbH are the development and production of 
enzymes, microbial mixed cultures and other biotechnological products. 
The product range covers the fields of application food and feed processing, bioenergy 
(bioethanol, biogas), organic synthesis, analytics, biosensors, textile industry and paper industry.  
Since the foundation in the year 1991 several research projects were carried out in the area of 
enzymatic degradation of renewable raw materials resulting in new cellulase and hemicellulase 
products for the utilization in the production of biodiesel, bioethanol and biogas. Furthermore 
ASA was engaged in several r&d -projects dealing with the conversion of organic waste materials 
(e.g. lignocellulytic material as grain stillage), whereby ASA developed several new cellulases, 
hemicellulases, pectinases etc.  Moreover  within the scope of a r&d -project AS A developed 
hydrolases for the degradation of organic compounds of municipal wastes, which might be useful 
for the SCALIBUR project.
  
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
Fermentation: incubation chambers for flask shake cultures, pilot to industrial scale a utomated 
stainless steel bioreactors (10 L, 20 L, 100 L, 300 L, 1.000 L) 
Downstream processing: ultrasonic cell disruptor, glas bead mill, ultrafiltration systems from 
laboratory to technical scale, chromatography columns up to pilot scale, freeze dryer  
Gene technoology: PCR, electrophoresis systems, electroporator  
QC and analytics: electrophoresis systems, UV/Vis scanning spectrophotometers, 2 analytical 
HPLCs, 1 preparative HPLC

4. CENER 
 
Fundación CENER-CIEMAT 
CENER-CIEMAT Foundation  
http://www.cener.com/ Country Spain Type: SME 
Short 
Name: CENER Participant No.:  4 
Organisation description 
 
The National Renewable Energy Centre (CENER) is a technology centre specialized in applied 
research, and the development and promotion of renewable energies. It is highly rated and has 
acknowledged national and international prestige. CENER, as a foundation, is an organization 
destined to support renewable energies sector competitiveness in order to help companies to 
reach their R&D needs. It offers high added value services and activities and transferring 
technology by means of a cutting -edge technological infrastructure, with t he most modern 
laboratories and facilities in Europe. Staff is approx. 200 people, where around 80% are 
technical organized in 6 Technical Departments: Wind Energy, Photovoltaic, Solar Thermal, 
Energy Building, Grid Energy Integration and Biomass Energy.  
CENER´s Biomass Energy Department  is composed of a multidisciplinary staff, over 19 people, 
some of them with more than ten years’ experience in biomass and bio -based products, with 
specific knowledge in biology, chemistry, agronomy and chemical engineerin g. Biomass 
Department has been working since 2002 in the conversion of lignocellulosic biomass into 
biofuels and bioproducts and since 2012 it owns and operates the “Second Generation Biofuel 
Centre”.  This is a semi -industrial pilot scale test facility, a ble to develop advanced biofuel and 
bio-based products production processes based on raw materials that are not competitive with 
the food industry (specially lignocellulosic materials and municipal solid waste), through the 
implementation of different conv ersion routes (thermochemical, biochemical and/or 
enzymatic) and also the application of biorefinery concepts.  
In CENER laboratories and pilot plant premises a wide kind of bioconversion processes  
(feedstock preparation, pretreatment, enzymatic hydrolysis , fermentation, etc) are carried out 
and optimized. These are focused on bio-based products production  such as bio -pesticides, 
building blocks based on furfural compounds, and fractionation & separation of lignocellulosic 
biomass in order to get more valuable bio -products.Besides, CENER is specialized on 
LCA 
assessment (at least GHG and energy balances) of the processes/products developed in its 
premises. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
CENER, as WP4 leader, will be focused in:  
 Set the optimum condition s for the OFMSW to be used as feedstock in the enzymatic 
hydrolysis process. 
 Demonstrate at TRL 7 the production on fermentable sugars from OFMSW.  
 Generate a solid fraction to be valorized together with sewage sludge in WP6. 
 Demostraste biopesticides production at TRL7 from the fermentable sugar 
liquid fraction of OFMSW. 
Also, CENER will be in charge of environmental sustainability evaluation of WP4 value chains by 
means of Life Cycle Assessment in WP7.

Germany. As researcher of the Biomass Department since 2002, Irantzu Alegría works on the 
development and coordination of R&D projects related to biochemical conversion of biomass 
into biofuels and/or bio -based product. Her main research lines are associated with biomass 
fractionation, enzymatic hydrolysis, fermentation and compositional analysis.  
 
Ms Inés del Campo (F, Msc in Chemical Engineer). From October 2002 she has been working

advanced biofuels technologies (biochemical & thermochemical), advanced biofuels plant

issues, policy and regulations about biofuels, biomass characterisation, biomass 
pretreatment, enzymatic hydrolysis, fermentation, biofuel characterisation and use. She also 
actively participates in the EERA Joint Program on Bioenergy.

5. CLUBE 
 
Cluster of Bioenergy & Environment of Western Macedonia (CLUBE) 
http://www.clube.gr/ 
 Country: Greece Type: Non profit 
Short 
Name: CLUBE Participant 
No.:  5 
Organisation description 
 
The Cluster of Bioenergy and Environment of Western Macedonia  (CLUBE) is a non -profit company 
established under the Greek Law among local actors and stakeholders of the Region of Western 
Macedonia.  
CLUBE is developing R&D and business activities in the fi elds of bioenergy and environment, in 
order to reinforce bio, green and circular economy in the region and the neighboring area, namely 
through: 
 Energetic exploitation of woody and other biomass for household and industrial use and 
especially for district heating systems for small, medium or large towns 
 Increasing the share of biofuels in the energy mix of transportation fuels 
 Co-firing with lignite in existing power stations and/or future heating plants  
 Optimization of heating systems 
 Improvement of energy efficiency for households, public and private buildings 
After being legally established in February 2014 as a non for profit association, the cluster currently 
includes 34 triple helix members covering the public sector, academia and business sector, 
including wood companies, forest and agricultural cooperatives, etc. Regarding urban wastes CLUBE  
has a strong collaboration with two of its members, the Waste Management Company of Western 
Macedonia (DIADYMA SA) and the Municipalities of the region through th e Regional Association of 
Municipalities of Western Macedonia. In the Region of Western Macedonia there is an integrated 
system for urban wastes with separate selection of recyclable material in 4 different bins. 
Furthermore, in pilot scale, there are two more projects. A separate collection of bio -wastes in 
small areas of two Municipalities, Kozani and Voio (in 2018 it will expanded to another 5 
Municipalities of the Region). 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
The members of CLUBE and its staff have a vast  experience in the fields of biomass, bioenergy and 
environment. They manage and successfully completed several European and Transnational 
Projects in the field of research and dissemination of knowledge and have assist the regional 
business sector promoting and fostering entrepreneurship in Western Macedonia. 
Key personnel curriculum

He holds a PhD in Clusters in Traditional Sectors of the Economy from the Aristotle University of

coordinator of the Regional Innovation Pole and the Regional Innovation Office of Western 
Macedonia, national Coordinator of the Strategic Med project “PROFORBIOMED”, external expert 
on innovation issues of FOROPA South East Europe project, etc. He coordinated several foresight 
exercises and has cooperated with a large number of SMEs (feasibility studies, project proposals 
and implementation, etc ). He is currently the national member of the European Bioeconomy Panel 
of the European Commission (DG RTD)

6. CSCP 
 
Collaborating Centre on Sustainable Consumption and Pr oduction 
gGmbH                                                                         
https://www.scp-

Organisation 
Short 
Name: CSCP Participant

Organisation  
description 
 
The Collaborating Centre on Su stainable Consumption and Production (CSCP) gGmbH is a Think and 
Do tank that works with businesses, policy makers, partner organizations and civil society toward a 
sustainable planet. The United Nations Environment Program (UNEP) and the Wuppertal Institu te for 
Climate, Energy and Environment jointly founded us in 2005. As a non -for profit and focuses, we 
focus on the promotion of sustainable patters of consumption and production (SCP). The CSCP 
adopts a holistic approach to foster SCP involving all actor groups and stakeholders. It has expertise 
in the areas of Products and Services, Cities & Infrastructure, Policy, Lifestyles & Behavior and 
Business & Entrepreneurship. Within these areas, it provides both ‘think’ and ‘do’ services in 
collaboration with it s partner organizations across the globe. The CSCP specializes in discovering, 
developing and replicating sustainable practices in the above topic areas in order to achieve a 
resilient and sustainable future for all. The CSCP has successfully acquired and implemented a range 
of EU funded projects including the projects funded under EU’s 7th Framework of Programme (FP 7) 
and Horizon 2020. In these, it has provided expertise on stakeholder mapping, outreach, dialogue, 
policy advice, sector sustainability road map development and translating sustainability in areas such 
as food and agriculture, Information and Communication Technologies (ICT), housing, mobility and 
health. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
The CSCP will support and ensure the efficient and succ essful implementation of the Urban 
Biowasteclubs in Spain, Italy, Sweden and the Czech Republic of the regional SCALIBUR partners by 
involving CSCP colleagues with respective language skills if needed. Thanks to its multidisciplinary 
and multinational team experienced Italian, Spanish, Swedish native-speakers can be involved.

European Topic Centre on Waste and Materials in a Green Economy, co -manages the German

projects in the fields of environmental politics and sustainable food production and c onsumption. 
Furthermore, she is interested in corporate social responsibility and the influence of civil society in 
shaping and promoting sustainable lifestyles.  
 
Janpeter Beckmann (male). Janpeter is an economist and specialized in resource economics. At CSCP 
he focusses on economic and sustainability -related analyses and modelling. Prior to joining the CSCP 
in 2015, he worked as a project manager and scientific employee dealing in particular with techno -
economic evaluations in regard to the material us e of renewable resources. In this context he 
focused on value chain analyses and market entry strategies as well as on market framework 
analyses and Green Premium.

Relevant projects  
and patents 
 REFRESH – Resource Efficient Food and dRink for the Entire Supply cHain (H2020, 2015 -2019) is 
an EU research project with 26 partners taking action to reduce avoidable waste and improve 
valorisation of food resources in line with SDG 12.3. The CSCP is responsible for the 
implementation of REFRESH in Germany including research on consumer behaviour regarding 
food waste (incl. moderation of focus groups) and the development of a German roadmap t o 
reduce and avoid food waste. A group of 15 organisations from business, civil society, science, 
and politics, moderated by CSCP, is working collaboratively together to create and negotiate 
this document as well as to implement innovative projects resulting from the discussions.  
 R2π (H2020, 2016-2019) – Transition from Linear to Circular focusses on enabling organisations 
and their value chains the transition towards a more viable, sustainable and competitive 
economic model. R2π examines the shift from th e broad concept of a Circular Economy (CE) to 
one of Circular Economy Business Models (CEBM) by tackling market opportunities and failures 
as well as policy opportunities and failures. Its innovation lies in having a strong business- model 
focus as well as in the role of policy development. R2π unfolds in diverse contexts with a strong 
emphasis on stakeholder involvement and exchange. The CSCP coordinates this project. CSCP 
supports the project on the selection of Circular Economy Business Models case studie s in 
sectors as e.g. food waste, Biomass/bio-based, circular raw material. 
 
 SPREAD – Sustainable Lifestyles 2050 (FP7, 2011 -2012) was a European social platform project 
addressing the challenge of improving quality of life with the help of social innovatio n. The 
project, coordinated by CSCP, examined the key lifestyle impact areas of consuming, living, 
moving, health and society. The consolidation of existing knowledge on sustainable lifestyles 
enabled SPREAD to prepare a roadmap for strategic action for po licy makers and to deliver 
innovative ideas for business, research and society on how to enable sustainable lifestyles in 
European society. 
 INHERIT – Intersectoral Health and Environment Research for Innovation (H2020, 2016 -2019)  
examines effective inter -sectoral policies, interventions and social as well as technological 
innovations that encourage individuals and communities across Europe to lead healthier and 
more environmentally sustainable lifestyles.   The CSCP contributes with its expertise in impact 
areas of and promising practices for sustainable lifestyles and will lead a foresight process on 
ideal futures for sustainable and healthy lifestyles in 2030.  
 ETC/WMGE- European Topic Centre on Waste and Materials in a Green Economy (2014 – 2018, 
EEA) is a consortium contracted by the European Environment Agency (EEA) to supply thematic 
expertise, and facilitate efficient communication and interaction among policy makers, 
administrative agencies and the scientific community to drive the transition towards a low -
carbon and circular economy in Europe. To ensure an interactive cooperation among member 
countries, the CSCP organizes annual EEA workshops, webinars and conferences and high -level 
meetings on SCP, waste management, and the circular economy.

EXERGY is a leading engineering and technology company that inspires innovative solu tions across 
the globe that contribute to its goal of a low carbon, sustainable future in two main areas: Green 
Building and Cities and Sustainable Processes.  
For over 5 years, EXERGY has been in the sustainable industry playing a major role in the 
development of sustainable and energy efficient engineering systems, including more than 20 
projects in UK and Europe, in collaboration with partner organisations and expanding to other 
countries around the world. Actually, the head company of EXERGY is based in  Coventry (UK) and 
apart from that, there are 3 branches in Netherlands, Colombia, and USA.  
EXERGY’s approach is based on a collaborative and innovative model where citizens, businesses and 
governments are a fundamental piece of its sustainable value chain . The technologies are developed 
through R&D efforts, that once proved, are incorporated in the products and services maintaining a 
dynamic and always cutting-edge value. 
Operating across a range of innovative low -carbon sustainable technologies, EXERGY’s capabilities 
cover everything from project planning to construction and from operation to reuse throughout the 
project life cycle to achieve target sustainability ratings and benchmarks. EXERGY is also member of 
SPIRE and BIC. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR

description 
 
FCC was founded in 1992 following the merger of two companies: Construcciones y Contratas 
(1944) and Fomento de Obras y Construcciones (1900). Since then, we have worked to become a 
company that provides high -quality services for citizens on a daily basi s. FCC is a publicly traded 
company on the Spanish stock exchange and one of the biggest and oldest waste management 
companies in the world, starting with its first contract for environmental services for 
municipalities in the city of Barcelona in 1901.

FCC is the parent company of one of Europe's leading citizen services groups, operating in sectors 
such as environmental services, water, and infrastructure. FCC is one of the world’s largest waste 
management and recycling companies with a presence in 55 countries. FCC obtained $7.906,75 
Billion in revenues in 2014, of which 44% came from international markets, mainly Europe and 
America. FCC's more than 63,000 employees worldwide. Over 100 million people in more than 
5,000 municipalities around the world b enefit from the services we provide. By employing the 
most advanced technologies we continuously improve our ability to manage the thousands of 
tons of solid waste collected every day in some of the world’s most important cities. More than 
25 million tons of refuse are collected per year. 
Our policies on corporate responsibility and continuous innovation in environmentally -friendly 
techniques have given rise to cleaner and more sustainable cities. And this is not all we have 
achieved. By diversifying our se rvices, we have helped to increase public satisfaction and made 
people's lives easier. We employ a variety of collection systems according to each city’s needs, 
using a combination of vehicles and containers designed to maximize efficiency and minimize the  
environmental footprint in terms of noise and emissions.  
FCC has over 200 centres that handle 24 million tonnes solid waste per year. This waste is treated 
through thermal, composting, biomethanisation, recycling or incineration processes, and the use 
of sanitary landfills. 
FCC’s Waste Treatment Department 
Our waste management activities include collection, treatment and elimination of solid urban 
waste, sewer system maintenance, treatment and elimination of industrial waste, Biomass or 
Waste to Energy re newable energy generation, street cleaning, park and garden maintenance, 
and full -service water management. We provide the whole range of environmental activities: 
collection, cleaning, and grounds maintenance, all types of waste treatment, recycling, ener gy 
from waste and final disposal. In Spain, we provide services to over 27.8 million inhabitants in 
3,456 municipalities. We collect 7 million tons of waste per year and over 8 million tons of waste 
is either treated and/or disposed. This waste is treated using processes such as heat, composting, 
biomethanisation, recycling, incineration, and use of controlled landfills and tips. To this end we 
have 60 treatment and disposal facilities run by over 31,000 employees.  
At FCC we treat waste as a resource, reus ing and recycling everything possible and making use of 
the energy value of the remaining fraction when feasible. 
In many locations, multiple technologies are combined to ensure the most complete waste 
recovery possible. 
More than 130 sanitary landfills re ceive the fraction of waste left after recycling and energy 
recovery. Biogas is captured from the landfills to produce energy and the company is installing 
wind turbines at landfill sites to further increase energy production. 
 Waste Treatment, Recycling, Energy Recovery and Disposal services in numbers:  
 24 million tonnes waste per year 
 Delivering services to 59 million people 
 More than 200 treatment, recycling and disposal facilities 
 10 existing Waste -to-Energy projects, with 2.6 million tonnes annual proc ess capacity 
and more than 300 MWe power output.

CE-SFS-25-2018  
 
86 
  
 
Las Dehesas facility 
The contract for the MBT includ ed Design, Building, Financing and Operation for 4 years (then 
extended 14 years more until 2026) Las Dehesas Biomethanation plant.   
The facility serves some of the boroughs of Madrid. FCC was awarded the contract in September 
2005 after winning the biddi ng process organised by Madrid City Council. The Project received 
funding from the European Union (cohesion funds). It was commissioned in December 2008 and 
operation end date is June 2026. Madrid City Council owns the plant site and obtained the 
planning permission for it. The JV made sure that the industrial equipment met international 
standards and complied with Spanish legislation. 
The plant receives 218 ktpa (kilo tons per annum) of mechanically pre -sorted organic fraction 
from municipal solid waste. I t has facilities to receive, bulk, condition and anaerobically digest 
waste, in order to treat it properly and extract valuable energy from it.  
Plant facilities are grouped into three treatment stages: 
 Pre-treatment area (two 33t/h lines), where waste cond itioning takes place (prior to 
digestion). 
 Biomethanation area, where the mesophilic (40ºC) anaerobic fermentation of the waste 
organic fraction takes place (biogas is produced). It can process up to 160ktpa. 
 Process water treatment area, where pre -treatment, aerobic digestion of active sludges, 
sludge treatment, ultrafiltration and reverse osmosis is undertaken.  
 Environmental aspects have been of paramount importance when designing the plant. A 
deodorization system has been implemented in the facilities t o avoid emissions to the 
atmosphere. 
Key parameters of the facility are: 
 Land area 19.900 m2  
 6,608 m2 industrial premises 
 Capacity of the reception and pre-treatment area can be extended 
 Five 3,600-m3 digesters, one 280-m2 biofilter which can process 48.210 Nm3/h,  
 Leachate biological treatment system which can process 192 m3/day.

Organisation  
description 
 
Greenovate! Europe (G!E) covers all parts of the innovation value chain, bringing together the 
expertise required for technology and service developers to successfully transfer research to 
market, and for policy -makers to create an environment in which eco -innovative business can 
thrive. To this end, G!E brings together over 500 experienced innovation ad visers and 2,000 
technical experts from 14 countries, providing all of the expertise needed to support the 
innovation process.  
G!E focuses on green innovation comprising all technologies and processes with a positive life -
cycle impact such as the bio -economy, bio -based construction materials, the integration of 
renewable energy sources and the circular economy (waste and waste water management). 
Particular emphasis has been on the bio -economy, where G!E has been developing tailor -
made communication and dis semination activities for several European projects in the fields 
of bioenergy, circular economy, bio-based construction materials and biofuels. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
Since its foundation in 2007, G!E has acquired extensive experience in the c oordination and 
management of EC-funded projects and has been Dissemination and Exploitation WP leader in 
over 20 European projects. During its participation in the projects EuroPruning (“Development 
and implementation of a new and non -existent logistic ch ain for biomass from pruning”) and 
BIOrescue (“Enhanced bioconversion of agricultural residues through cascading use”), 
Bio4Products (“Creating sustainable resources for process industries)” and Rubizmo 
(“Replicable Business Models For Modern Rural Economi es”), G!E has had the opportunity to 
work on the development of new bio -based value chains and business models. Through its 
involvement in 3 EU funded smart cities projects (EU -GUGLE, SINFONIA, STARDUST), G!E has 
also demonstrated its expertise organising and leading replication and knowledge exchange 
activities in and between cities , engaging with municipal, industry, R/D and civil society 
players.  
In SCALIBUR, G!E will lead two workpackages. WP9, on Dissemination and Communication, 
and WP10 on Exploitat ion and Replication. In WP9, in particular, G!E will be responsible for 
the development of the dissemination and communication strategy, for the organisation of 
the project’s dissemination events and knowledge sharing activities, the networking with 
related European projects. In WP10, G!E will coordinate the capacity building activities and 
develop recommendation for policy and scientific uptake as part of the Exploitation tasks.

Organisation description 
 
KOUR is a small Italian company founded in 2012 with the objective  of developing and managing 
Bio-gas plants for converting organic and livestock waste. During the past three years KOUR  has 
also focused his business on the industrial field, especially thanks to Marco Benassi's experience, 
it concentrated in revamping ind ustrial plants such Power plants, ceramics manufacturing and 
Agrifood Industries. 
KOUR is also involved in the export of Italian technology to West Africa and, since one year, 
KOUR can count on an operative office in Dakar (Senegal) in order to develop new  projects in 
Africa. 
Kour is always open to create new technologies and innovative solutions and, for this reason, 
Kour is one of the main partner of the project ValoriBio for developing new technologies for 
rearing insects in collaboration with BIOGEST SITEIA. 
Coming from one of the most industrialized Italian regions, Kour has consolidated expertise in 
industrial plant and automation. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
KOUR is a very dynamic engineering/project developing and consulting company, specializ ed in 
developing prototypes. Not only Kour can count on a wide and strong network of farms and 
associates, but also it has access to different labs regionwide.  
KOUR's headquarters has offices dedicated to the project development and management.  
As to the realization and production of prototypes (assembling and testing) KOUR  owns a large 
hall where forklift trucks, overhead travelling cranes as well as assembly systems are available.  
The realization and testing of the automation parts and electronic compon ents as well as the 
research and development take place in a prototyping laboratory. In this laboratory there are 3D 
printers, 3D cutters, machines for the realization and testing of electronic boards, mechanical 
design and programming software. In this ki nd of laboratory, it is possible to develop many 
innovative parts of the industrial prototypes designed by Kour.

12. LUND 
 
LUNDS KOMMUN   
CITY OF LUND                           
www.lund.se/ 
Country: SWEDEN Type: Municipality Short Name: LUND Participant No.:  12 
Organisation 
description 
 
Lunds kommun (a.k.a. City of Lund) is a municipality in the Scania region (Region Skåne) in southern 
Sweden. It covers approx. 443 km² and has more than 120,000 inhabitants. Lund is a centre of higher 
education in the southern parts of Sweden and the city is expanding in high speed with the transition into a 
smart sustainable city.  
Lund has long been an active local government with strong dedication to sustainable development. The city 
is the founder and host of the Swedish, nationwide, association Climate Municipalities with 37 members. 
Lund is currently invol ved in several projects with European funding, through Horizon 2020, FP7 and the 
Interreg programmes. The involvement in the collaborative and innovative Smart City projects presents an 
excellent experience and platform for the execution and dissemination of the SCALIBUR project.  
The decision to place the European Spallation Source (ESS) in Lund underlines the city’s ambitions in being 
at the forefront of innovative research and education. Around the ESS and Max IV (a Swedish national 
laboratory providing s cientists and industry with the world’s highest quality X -
rays for research and 
development), the Brunnshög area is being developed, with high sustainability targets.  
Capabilities and 
role in SCALIBUR 
The City of Lund is responsible for the administration  of the municipality and for the development of the 
city. The city is also responsible for the collection of household waste. The political leadership have set up 
six overarching goals for the city. One of them is: The impact on the climate and environment  from the City 
of Lund should be significantly reduced. This goal is then broken down into comprehensive targets and 
achievements in the environmental programme and in the waste management plan.  
The Cleansing Department in Lund has developed a system for sorted household waste collection called 
“the four compartment bins”. It is not only the bins that have been developed but also the collection 
vehicles that can automatically empty the bins in a single step. This system is now spreading in Sweden with 
more than 20% of the municipalities using it. Most households in Lund have two bins, which means that 
eight fractions of waste is collected at every house. One of the fractions is food waste and now we have 
achieved a purity of 97% of the waste (determined as correctly sorted waste). The food waste is then 
transported to a biogas plant where biogas and bio -fertilizer is produced and the biogas is upgraded to 
vehicle gas for the use in cars and busses. In 2017 Lund was awarded the price for the best recycling 
municipality in Sweden and in 2016 Lund was awarded “best waste management services by a Swedish 
municipality”. 
The main task in the project is to share our experiences in separated organics waste collection and to 
actively participate in the development of new solutions with a higher valorisation.  
Key personnel curriculum 
 
Dr. Markus Paulsson: (male) is an energy strategist and project manager at the Department of strategic 
development at the City Office (Kommunkontoret) at the City of Lund. He has a lon g experience of working 
with EU projects and with waste related issues. He has been leading projects concerning new methods of 
treating park and yard waste as well as new methods for waste water treatment and sludge management.  
 
 
Mr. Erik Rånlund : (male ) is the Managing Director of the Cleansing department in the City of Lund since 
2003. He has implemented the four compartment bin system in the entire city. He has also implemented 
the environmental and quality systems (ISO 14001 & 9001) in his organisation

13. MADRID 
 
Ayuntamiento de Madrid   
Madrid Council Town 
www.madrid.es/ 
portal/site/munimadrid/   Country: Spain Type: Public Body  Short Name: MADRID  Participant No.:  13 
Organisation description 
 
The municipality of Madrid is the public body in charge of the administration of the city  
of Madrid. MADRID has an integral system for solid urban waste treatment:  
 
Waste management of the municipal solid waste in Madrid is carried out at Valdemingómez 
Technology Park in the south of the city, at Vallecas district. It comprises the following 
installations: 
- 3 waste treatment plants (La Paloma, Las Lomas and Las Dehesas) with 2 b iometanation 
plants (La Paloma and Las Dehesas) 
- 1biogas upgrading plant 
- 2 waste -to-energy plants (one valorising the rejects of Las Lomas plants and the other 
valorizing the biogas from La Galiana landfill) 
In 2016,  1.248.180 tons of municipal solid waste  was treated at Valdemingómez Technology Park 
(with 67.060tons of material recovery, 78.756tons of selective collection of recyclables and 
4.449tons sold of stabilized material production) 
Waste-to-energy plants produced 245.314MWh of electricity (covering  5.62% of Madrid’s power 
consumption) and 74.958 thermal megawatts exported to the national grid. 
MADRID has also collaborated in an environmental education program with 9.729 visitors to 
Valdemingómez Technology Park from schools, business associations an d national and 
international public bodies

14. NOVAMONT 
 
NOVAMONT S.P.A.                                
www.NOVAMONT.com/ Country: Italy Type: Large Enterprise 
Short 
Name: NOVAMONT Participant 
No.:  14 
Organisation 
description 
 
NOVAMONT S.p.A is an Italian industrial company whose roots lie in the Montedison School of 
Materials Science and which was set up to implement the ambitious project of some researchers from 
the chemical corporation: to integrate chemistry, agriculture and the environment. Founded in 1989, 
it is now worldwide leader in the sector of bioplastics and involved in the development of bioproducts 
such as biolubricants, biochemicals and cosmetic ingredients from renewable sources.  
NOVAMONT’s mission is to develop materials and biochemicals through the integration of chemistry 
and agriculture, by starting up biorefineries in the local areas and providing application sol utions that 
ensure efficient use of resources throughout their entire life cycle, with advantages for the social, 
economic and environmental system. 
Its model of development aims at building bridges between different sectors and creating new value 
by colla borating with all the stakeholders in the value chain: from agriculture to research, from 
industry to waste management, from local institutions to civil society. 
Guided by these principles, NOVAMONT  promotes an approach to bioeconomy based on the efficient  
use of renewable resources and on the regeneration of local areas, building world -first plants based 
on proprietary technologies and revitalising industrial sites that are decommissioned or no longer 
competitive to create new industries, new products and new jobs. Examples are Mater -Biotech, the 
company born from the reconversion of a decommissioned industrial site in north -east Italy into the 
first dedicated industrial plant at world level to produce biobutanediol through fermentative 
processes and the Matrìca biorefinery, the 50:50 joint venture between NOVAMONT and Versalis (Eni) 
to reconvert a part of a preexisting petrochemical site in Sardinia. A further example is the subsidiary 
Mater-Biopolymer, in central Italy, producing biopolyesters in a plant r econverted using a 
NOVAMONT’s proprietary technology. 
Besides being an industrial company, NOVAMONT  is also a research centre which covers a wide range 
of expertise and specialisations, with equipment and facilities ranging from laboratory scale activities 
to innovative pilot plants. Over the years it has developed four proprietary and integrated 
technologies for the production of bioplastics and bioproducts, creating synergies between the 
different areas of study (Bioplastics, Biotechnology, Agronomics and Organic Chemistry). 
Moreover, NOVAMONT regularly implements training programmes for young and experienced 
researchers, in collaboration with partners from the public and the private sector (more than 300 
activities since 2000). 
MATER-BI is the innovative family of bioplastics developed by NOVAMONT  research. It is 
biodegradable and compostable according to the European standard EN 13432 and other 
international standards and has characteristics of use very similar to those of traditional plastics.  
MATER-BI provides solutions for specific environmental problems while combining product quality and 
performance with an efficient use of resources. In particular, MATER -BI has been conceived for 
applications in which biodegradability and compostability represent an added value, such as shopping 
bags that can be reused to collect organic waste or foodware products “contaminated” with leftovers, 
or serve a function, such as mulch films. The main fields of application are: separate waste collection, 
agriculture, large retail sector, disposable foodserviceware, packaging. 
With 600 people, NOVAMONT  group posted sales of €170 million in 2016 and made continuous 
investments in research and development activities: 7.4% of its  turnover, around 20% of people (2016 
consolidated financial statements). It has a portfolio of around 1,000 patents. The group has its 
headquarters in Novara, a production facility in Terni and research laboratories in Novara, Terni and 
Piana di Monte Verna (CE). NOVAMONT ’s subsidiaries are based in Porto Torres (SS), Adria (RO), Terni 
and Patrica (FR). It has a representative office in Brussels (Belgium), foreign seats in Germany, France 
and the United States and operates through own distributors in Benelux.

technologies, biodegradation, che mistry applied to vegetable oils, carbohydrates and 
lignocellulosic materials, biotechnology applied to chemicals, ecology of products and 
environmental footprint, engineering, agronomy), located in Novara;

three case studies so test and validate better system -wide economic and environmental outcomes 
by i) decoupling the chain from fossil feedstocks, (ii) reducing the negative environmental impact 
of plastic packaging; and (iii) creating an effective after-use plastics economy. (

Nutrition Sciences N.V. (NS) is a Belgian private company (26 collaborators) belonging  to the 
Nuscience-group (1125 collaborators) and is well known for its R&D activities in animal production 
and spends much attention to the introduction of new feed ingredients, concepts, services and 
technologies in animal livestock production for its cus tomers. Their innovation -driven attitude 
enables them to supply sustainable and economically viable solutions for the efficient production of 
animal feed and feed ingredients within the food value chain. Main focus today is developing 
concepts and services  for (1) reduction of raw material depletion and (2) lowering the dependency 
for antibiotics in livestock production.  
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
Nutrition Sciences N.V. has its own laboratory, in order to perform and validate novel feed 
technologies as well as novel and sustainable feed concepts. For evaluation of feed concepts, specific 
bioassays on feeds and samples can be performed. In this respect, demonstration and validation of 
production processes with novel feed ingredients can be performed . Finally, Nutrition Sciences N.V. 
has access to different trade fairs for demonstration of outcomes of the project and is (co)organising 
different workshops and trainings for different stakeholders in the food chain.
