16. SMVAK 
 
Severomoravské vodovody a kanalizace Ostrava a.s.    
Severomoravské water supply and sewrage system Ostrava                                 
www.SMVAK.cz  Country: CZ Type: Large Company  Short Name: SMVAK Participant No.:  16 
Organisation  
description 
 
Severomoravské vodovody a kanalizace Ostrava a.s. ( SMVAK) was founded in 1992 as a joint -stock 
company. The majority of shares were owned by the municipalities from the Moravian -Silesian 
Region. SMVAK Ostrava operates in the districts of Frýdek -Místek, Karviná, Nový Jičín and Opava, with 
water also being delivered as per contract to the cities of Ostrava, Hlučín, Studénka and other 
municipalities. The entity supplies the drinking water for more than 730,000 people in 76 
municipalities through 130,000 service pipes (total length: 771 km). It also supplies drinking water to a 
part of the Olomouc Region (Lipník nad Bečvou, Přerov, Hranice na Moravě) and to a border territory 
in Poland (Jastrzębie -Zdroj). It also operates 65 wastewater treatment plants (61 mechanical -
biological and 4 mec hanical WWTPs) with the total capacity of 279,682 m 3 per day (973,210 ep). The 
length of the sewage system is 1,774 km. More than 521,000 people are connected to the SMVAK  
Ostrava’s sewage system. In addition to the core business, SMVAK Ostrawa provides other services.  
The core business is production and supply of drinking water as well as discharge and treatment of 
wastewater. 95% of drinking water is produced from central resources managed by Povodí Odry (the 
river basin authority) in three main water tr eatment plants in the Ostrava Area Water Network The 
water treatment plants are located in Podhradí u Vítkova, Nová Ves u Frýdlantu nad Ostravicí and  
Vyšní Lhoty near Frýdek -Místek. Raw water is taken from the Kružberk Dam in the foothills of the 
Jeseníky Mountains and Šance Dam and Morávka Dam in the Beskydy Mountains. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
Infrastructures & facilities : Operation of 65 wastewater treatment plants with a total capacity of 
279,682 m3/d in 76 municipalities where SCALIBUR actions will be carried out. This as sures a constant 
supply of sewage sludge to be treated during the project execution. The strong background of SMVAK  
in drinking water production and supply,as well as treatment and discharge of wastewater will 
facilitate the successful execution of SCALIBU R SMVAK will participate actively in several WP, whose 
main role is: 
 To contribute in WP1, leading activities and WP towards the desired objectives. 
 To contribute in WP2 actively engage all relevant stakeholders and support the integration of the 
urban bio waste valorisation approaches, designing the roadmap for the implementation of the 
SCALIBUR vision at a regional scale, since. SMVAK operates in different districts in Czech Republic.  
 In WP3 SMVAK will participate in the logistical optimization of the rou tes aimed at the desired 
synergistic effects by treating different wastes. It will also provide detailed analysis of sewage 
sludge generated in WWTPs located in Czech Republic. 
 SMVAK will lead WP6 to verify the feasibility of SCALIBUR process as a cost -competitive 
alternative for sewage sludge and mixtures treatment to obtain high -value compounds. It will 
promote the collaboration between partners involved in WP6 for an effective implementation of 
the process as well as verification of performance and end-products quality.

UNIMORE (1176) is third oldest University in the world and has always been ranked among the first 
Italian universities for quality of teaching and research since 2007. UNIMORE is a networked campus 
located in the towns of Modena and Reggio Emilia. It counts about 20000 students, including 3500 
postgraduates, 900 f aculty members, 13 PhD schools. UNIMORE has over 300 international exchange 
agreements and cooperation programs to encourage students and researcher to actively interact in a 
globalized world. The University has a strategic commitment to promote research i n the following 
major areas: Mechanics and Mechatronics, Logistics, Molecular and Regenerative Medicine, 
Nanoscience and Nanotechnology, ICT and Neuroscience. 
UNIMORE has excellent international network being part of, among the other, Biobased industries, ETP 
Nanomedicine, EARPA -  Transport networks including academic and industrial players. The University 
project portfolio comprises 45 on -going Horizon 2020 projects, more than 50 running FP7 projects, 
ARTEMIS, Ecsel, and ENIAC Joint Technology Initiatives included, plus several projects financed by 
other international donors. UNIMORE is part of the High Technology Regional Cluster, involving all the 
Universities in the Emilia -Romagna Region, and offers cutting -edge facilities for technology transfer in 
the sectors of regenerative medicine, advanced materials, mechanical engineering, mechatronics, ICT 
in business applications. 
Research Office provides RTD advisory, project management services, training and capacity building in 
transferable skills supporting t he building of transnational collaborative projects and industry -
academia partnerships. A dedicated Industrial Liaison Office supports spin -off and provides IPR tech -
transfer advisory. 
In addition, UNIMORE have recently been accredited by the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA). 
At UNIMORE research is conducted both at the 14 Departments and research centres, the latter may 
involve multiple departments in the development of interdisciplinary research activities. The 
Department in charge of the implementat ion of the project is the D Department of Life Sciences and 
the Department of Law. 
The Department of Life Sciences  originated from the aggregation of three Faculties (Agriculture, 
Biosciences and Biotechnology and Pharmacy). Over the years it has achieved very important results in 
agricultural, food and environmental technologies. 
The Department of Law is hosted in a building that has recently been renovated. It has been equipped 
with the most up -to-date research tools. Researchers who obtained outstanding results in the field of 
environmental and agrifood law and the relevant systems of sanctions work within the department .

18. VISUM 
 
Visum Limited  
www.seeingnewdata.com Country: Ireland  Type: Company  
Short

Organisation description 
 
VISUM (www.seeingnewdata.com) is an optical engineering company from Dublin that 
specializes in the development and commercialization of Near Infrared Spectroscopy (NIRS) -
based portable and inline analyzers and measurement systems for process monitoring and 
quality control applications in the food, pharmaceutical and chemical applications. The 
company was established in 2014 and currently employs 9 staff from its facilities in Nexus 
UCD (technology park at the University College Dublin campus). In 2016, the company 
launched the VISUMPalm (a handheld NIR measurement instrument) and has secured first 
sales. An integration platform (VisumNIR) for the inline version is currently under 
development in coop eration with early adopter clients from the food processing industry 
(dairy, meat and olive oil) and pharmaceutical industries. VISUM Ltd. is an SME Champion -
awarded a Phase 1 and a subsequent Phase 2 Grant under H2020’s SME Instrument.  
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
VISUM will lead the WP 7 with support from its 3 rd party IRIS, they will also provide key 
monitoring technology for the biowaste treatment plant in WP3. 
VISUM will also contribute to the transversal tasks like IPR management, dissemination and 
exploitation planning.
  
The optical engineering and smart systems teams at VISUM Ltd. have specialized expertise in 
sensor integration, optical engineering, chemometrics, data analytics, cloud infrastructures 
and data management systems.
 
Key personnel curriculum 
 
DR. TIMOTHY KEHOE (Male) PhD in Engineering, University College Cork, Ireland- developed an

in Optoelectronics, Queens University Belfast. Designed a n Echelle spectrometer while based 
at Andor Technology Ltd.  Worked at Tyndall National Institute, Cork, and Catalan Institute of 
Nanotechnology, Barcelona, developing diffractive optical and acousto -optical metrology 
techniques for nanotechnology applicati ons, in particular for characterision of nanoscale 
structures fabricated by nanoimprint lithography and directed self -assembly. Other research 
activities: quantification of ordering in self -assembled structures by image analysis techniques 
and optical sensors using hydrogel materials. Tim is the VISUMPalm Product Manager, as well 
as the Technical Lead at VISUM Ltd.

19. WBD 
 
Waterschap Brabantse Delta                                  
Water Authority Brabantse Delta                                  
www.brabantsedelta.nl Country: NETHERLANDS Type: Water Authority 
Short 
Name: WBD Participant 
No.:  19 
Organisation description 
 
Waterschap Brabantse Delta (WBD) is  the regional water authority for the West Brabant 
region in the Netherlands. The Dutch regional water authorities are decentralised public 
authorities, responsible for flood protection, regional water management and treatment of 
urban wastewater in the Netherlands. Water authority Brabantse Delta maintains the water 
quality for 8,100 km of ditches, canals and rivers and maintains 568 km of dykes for flooding 
protection. There are in total 17 sewage treatment plants in  the region and these plants 
together treat the wastewater from 1.2 million people equivalents. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
BD has been consortium leader for the PHARIO project that involved 10 months of pilot testing 
at the WWTP Bath of Brabantse D elta and is also leading a consortium of Dutch water 
authorities (Fryslan, Scheldestromen, De Dommel and Hollandse Delta) that together have the 
ambition to demonstrate the PHARIO approach at a larger scale as proposed in the Scalibur 
proposal. Scalibur wi ll support these ambitions by making it possible to involve end -users in 
the larger scale by supply of materials and through optimization studies.  WBD will ensure that 
these other water authorities are kept updated on the outcomes of Scalibur and together  they 
intend to invest in further expansion and promotion of the PHA production as intended in 
Scalibur. 
WBD will make available the knowledge and contacts they have developed for PHA production 
from sewage sludge. The WWTP Bath has shown to have very good  capabilities to produce 
PHA in an efficient way and WBD will make this sludge available for PHA production in the 
Scalibur project. 
Key personnel curriculum 
 
Etteke Wypkema (female) is innovation manager for WBD. Etteke has initiated and coordinated 
various innovation projects within WBD. Examples of such projects are pilot testing of cold 
Anammox (UNAS system), thermophylic digestion and dynamic filtration of sewage sludge. 
Etteke has 25 years of experience in sewage treatment processes.

20. WETSUS 
 
Stichting Wetsus, European Centre Of Excellence For Sustainable 
Water Technology 
www. wetus.eu  
 Country: NETHERLANDS Type: Research 
institute 
Short 
Name: WETSUS Participant 
No.:  20 
Organisation 
description 
 
Stichting Wetsus, European Centre of Excellence For Sustainable Water Technology, is  a research 
institute dedicated to sustainable water technology. At WETSUS, a unique environment is created 
where over 100 companies and 16 European universities participate in creating innovative 
solutions to water-related problems. The institute carries out multidisciplinary research performed 
by 60 PhD students and postdoctoral researchers who are mostly located in the WETSUS 
laboratories in Leeuwarden, the Netherlands. WETSUS is part of WaterCampus Leeuwarden. The 
WaterCampus houses facilities and services to develop new water technologies and bring them to 
the market, including piloting and demonstration sites. 
WETSUS will be the main Scalibur partner to design, build and operate the demonstration scale 
facility for polyhydroxyalkanoate production from organic residuals (PHARIO)  
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
The work of WETSUS on polyhydroxyalkanoate production from organic  residuals in the SCALIBUR 
project will benefit from the more fundamental research in the WETSUS theme on Bioplastics. This 
work will be coordinated by Dr. Alan Werker, highly qualified for this work, as he drove the 
development of this process from fundamental laboratory scale to its current stage. Experiments to 
support the demonstration work can be done in the WETSUS laboratories. WETSUS has not only 
the personnel, expertise and facilities to carry out these tasks, as an organisation connecting 
universities and companies, it’s also ideally suited to support companies in the development and 
up-scaling of novel technologies. WETSUS is dedicated to transfer the generated IP to the 
participating companies and support them to reach the commercial phase. WETSUS ’ research 
facilities are very well equipped and adapted to multidisciplinary projects. The researchers have the 
support of very competent technicians and analysts. WETSUS is located at the water campus where 
it has access to facilities for piloting and demonstration of water treatment installations. 
   
Facilities at WaterCampus Leeuwarden to realise the PHARIO demonstration facility  
Key personnel curriculum 
 
Dr. Alan Werker  (male) is the leader of the recently initiated Bioplastics theme at WETSUS. This 
theme will, to start with, employ two PhD researchers with academic enrolment at Delft University 
of Technology. Plans are also to support the technology developments in the practical 
demonstration efforts of SCALIBUR. Alan is an environmental engineer  with 30 years of experience 
in both academic and industrial research and development efforts. For the past 14 years, he drove 
the devil in the detail from fundamental laboratory scale R&D all the way to bioprocess 
development in piloting proof of concept for producing biopolymers from residuals management 
services. Value added biopolymers (polyhydroxyalkanoates) can be produced as an integrated 
outcome to the treatment and management of industrial and municipal wastewater and sludge 
streams. In the most recently completed project, it was shown in a 10- month production campaign 
that municipal activated sludge can be a raw material to make commercial quality polymers for the 
bioplastics industry. Alan led a trans- disciplinary team that peaked at 12 research e ngineers and 
scientists. Through this work he engaged in national and international academic, corporate, and 
public/private collaborations in basic research, thesis supervision, EU Consortium Projects, and in 
practical business development challenges for r enewable resource value chains. As well as being 
the WETSUS Bioplastics theme leader, Alan is a co -owner and consultant with Promiko AB, a 
Swedish SME, and an Adjunct Professor, School of Chemical Engineering, at the University of 
Queensland.

Relevant projects and 
patents 
 The Wetsus research theme on Bioplastics was launched in 2017. The theme is sponsored by 
PAQUES (http://en.paques.nl), STOWA (www.stowa.nl), and Slibver werking Noord -Brabant 
(www.snb.nl). The theme was strongly motivated by the compelling and positive outcomes 
from the project PHARIO. 
 PHARIO was financially subsidised from the Topsector Energy program of the Dutch ministry 
of Economic Affairs (TKI Biobase d Economy). The project brought together a public -private 
sector co-development effort. It confirmed that surplus full -scale municipal activated sludge 
can be a robust raw material to make biopolymers of predictable and high quality for the 
bioplastics industry when combined with fermented regionally available organic residuals. The 
techno-economic feasibility for a regional bioplastics value chain was demonstrated and this 
progress continues with proposed next steps of increasing TRL in SCALIBUR.  
 EIT RawMaterials upscaling project coordinated by WETSUS on a novel magnetic route for 
phosphorus and iron recovery from sewage sludge (ViviMag). This project is being done in 
cooperation with TUDELFT (NL), Outotec (FI), ICL (IL) and Kemira (FI). 
 H2020 project coor dinated by WETSUS on Storage and recovery of renewable electrical 
energy by reversible salt water dissociation (BAoBaB), Grant number: 731187

Zetadec is a R&D and consultancy company in the field of feed raw materials  processing and 
design of new feed, food and biomass forms. As such, Zetadec assi sts in development of new 
products, product formulation and conceptualization of manufacturing lines. The main focus is on 
the interaction between raw materials and (feed) processing equipment. Zetadec has experience in a 
large number of unit -- operations e.g. grinding, mixing and forming operations like pelleting, 
extrusion or high --shear granulation. Zetadec has access to its own lab where "proof -of-principle" 
experiments are performed. Also, 2 cabinets are available within the Zetadec facilities for shel f life 
trials. In addition, Zetadec is one of the founding fathers of ‘the Insect Center’ a non -profit branch 
organization with respect to production of insect for food and feed applications. The customer base 
is globally oriented and includes large multin ational companies in the field of feed manufacturing, 
raw materials manufacture and commodity training. In addition, Zetadec provides services for SME 
companies who develop new innovative feeding methods and concepts. 
Capabilities and role in 
SCALIBUR 
The laboratory consists of two units; one unit is used for developing products andconsists in part of 
(traditional) wet- chemistry analytical tools and procedures (as particle size distribution analyses, 
DSC, spectrophotometer, …). The other unit is used to bu ild and install (prototypes of) lab -scale and 
pilot equipment used in milling, extruding, granulating and coating the various products Zetadec is 
working on. Also, equipment for distillation, extraction and spheronisation of ingredients are 
available.

Description: 
IRIS (Innovació i Recerca Industrial i Sostenible SL) is an advanced engineering company that specialises in process monitoring 
and control, and process optimisation. Its commercial division offers advanced monitoring and control solutions based on NIR 
and hyperspectral imaging solutions for fore ign body detection and chemical composition analysis; data management 
solutions for data processing, decision support, automation and data analysis (big production data).  
Besides, IRIS’ innovation division has 3 core lines: 
-New optical photonics-based technologies and PAT systems for production process optimisation  
-Data mining, IOT & cloud platforms 
-Circular and Bio-based Economy: digitalization and waste valorisation 
The company was established in 2007 and currently employs 56 staff with a turnover of €3.8 M. It is equipped with 
engineering workshops (3), food testing and wet chemistry laboratory, optics labs (2), and an electronics/telecommunications 
lab. IRIS is ISO 9001:2008 certified and also is certified under UNE-EN-ISO 166002: Management Systems R&D&i. 
With its team including telecom and electronics engineers, system engineering, application programming and web 
development etc. IRIS can carry out full system desi gn and engineering, including electronic design (PCB) and assembly, 
firmware and software development, electrical harnesses and interconnections. Moreover IRIS has mechanical and 
mechatronics engineers, specialised in process upscaling, integration work, a s well as installation, validation and 
industrialisation of prototypes and equipment in different industries. In addition to this broad cross -disciplinary engineering 
team, IRIS’ research team consisting among other of food and material scientists, biologi sts and physicists, have all the 
expertise to validate the technologies developed. Finally, IRIS has significant expertise in the use of QFD (quality function  
deployment) and uses a systems development management approach based on KANBAN agile methodologie s. 
Significant Infrastructure:  
Spectroscopic Laboratory equipped with several instruments, namely, a FTIR -ATR (Interspectrum), 2 UV -VIS (PerkinElmer and 
Ocean Optics), an Extended -SWIR (StellarNet) and a NIR (Mightex) spectrophotometers as well as a SWIR Hyperspectral 
imager (Specim -Xenics). The associated staff are properly trained and skilled in chemometrics modelling by using a 
commercial suite (SOLO+MIA from Eigenvector) as well as ad hoc non -commercial chemometric tools (Matlab and Python 
toolboxes). 
Electronics, mechanical and optical workshops and laboratories equipped with up -to-date hardware and tools: signal 
generators, wide band oscilloscopes, PCB design [Altium] and building tools, development kits for programming 
microcontrollers, CNC -milling m achines for electronic and mechanical prototyping, and CAD software [SolidWorks], among 
others.   
IRIS’ optical engineers work with ZEEMAX software for optimally designing of optical systems and to setup the designs by 
means of advanced optical components and facilities (optical tables, windows, lenses, lasers and light sources and related 
“opticalware”). 
Food and wet chemistry lab equipped with a DSC, a Surface Energy analyser, an HPLC, a Cobb tester, microbiological 
equipments, microspcope and microtome f or structural analysis, migration cells, colourimeter (for colour and opacity 
measurement), Ford cup viscometers, water vapour permeation cells, turbidimeter, climatic chambers, manual and automatic 
coaters, electrospray, different drying technologies, plasma surface activation, etc.

19. WBD 
Does the participant plan to subcontract certain tasks  YES 
Subcontractor:  To be selected on a best value for money basis 
Tasks: An EPC contractor (EPC: engineering, procurement, construction) with experience in design and construction of 
solvent extraction and recovery plants will be hired to perform a value engineering exercise in order to translate the costs of 
the pilot scale PHA extraction to a full scale design and asses cost optimization opportunities. In this way a direct insight  is 
obtained in main cost determining factors for a full scale design of the green solvent PHA extraction system and can then be 
validated in the pilot scale extraction facility, for instance to determine key design parameters or test alternative 
approaches that can lead to significant cost reductions in a full scale plant. The scope of the subcontract will consist of the 
following elements: 1. Basic engineering design and cost estimate based on the results of the first pilot extraction runs. 2.  
Value engineering exercise with EPC experts and experts from Wetsus and WBD to determine the cost determining factors 
and identify possible approaches for cost reduction that can be tested and implemented on pilot scale. 3. Make a new 
design and cost estimate based on optimized parameters obtained at the pilot scale.  
This approach will lead to a reduced cost for the solvent extraction process and will support and improve the business case.  
Maximum cost: 80,000 € 
 
20. WETSUS 
Does the participant plan to subcontract certain tasks  YES 
Subcontractor:  To be selected on a best value for money basis 
Tasks: The solvent extraction pilot to be realized within the project will use green solvents to extract the PHA from the 
biomass. Since solvents are flammable and potential explosive t he pilot needs to be designed in a way that makes it safe 
and easy to operate. The design will need to comply with the EU ATEX 95 and 137 regulations for handling will need to be 
performed on the design and way to operate the pilot plant. For this reason t he construction of this part of the pilot will be 
subcontracted to an company that has experience in designing pilot equipment handling flammable and explosive 
chemicals. The subcontractor will design the pilot based on a process design supplied by Scalibu r partners Wetsus and WBD 
and also give instructions for safe operation of the system. 
Maximum cost: 120,000 € 
 
21. ZETADEC 
 
Does the participant plan to subcontract certain tasks  YES 
Subcontractor:  To be selected on a best value for money basis 
Tasks: Minor physic-chemical analysis   
Maximum cost: 9,000 €

SECTION 5. ETHICS AND SECURITY
5.1 ETHICS 
 We confirm that this proposal complies with ethical principles (including the highest standards of research 
integrity- as set out, for instance, in the European Code of Conduct for Research Integrity - and including, in 
particular, avoiding fabrication, falsification, plagiarism or other research misconduct. 
Concerning the Ethics issues table of Part A of the proposal, SCALIBUR does not raise any ethical issue cause 
although it involves the use of insects and microorganisms, when referring to animal welfare,  we shall consider 
Council Directive 98/58/EC and Directive 2010/63/EC.  
 Council Directive 98/58/EC of 20 July 1998 concerning the protection of animals kept for farming purposes does not 
apply to invertebrate animals (so insects are outside its scope); 
 Directive 2010/63/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council of 22 September 2010 on the protection of 
animals used for scientific purposes applies only to live non -human vertebrate animals and live cephalopods, so again, 
insects are not included. 
According to EU law, therefore, up till now, ethic issues are not involved.  
Therefore, the table in the administrative online form has been filled in accordingly, answering NO to all the 
questions included in the following sections: 
1. HUMAN EMBRYOS/FOETOUSES 
2.  HUMANS 
3. HUMAN CELLS/TISSUES 
4.  PROTECTION OF PERSONAL DATA 
5. ANIMALS 
6. NON-EU COUNTRIES 
7. ENVIRONMENTAL PROTECTION 
8. DUAL USE 
9. MISUSE 
10. OTHER ETHIC ISSUES 
As a result, the proposal does not require submitting an ethics and self-assessment document.
5.2 SECURITY 
This proposal does not raise any security issues.

SCALIBUR: SCALable technologIes for Bio-Urban waste Recovery. TOPIC: Integrated 
system innovation in valorising urban biowaste. Topic identifier: CE-SFS-25-2018. 
 
LETTER OF SUPPORT 
Mr. dal Prete Andrea, on behalf of Municipality of Polpenazze d/G. which is informed 
about the project proposal SCALIBUR”: SCALable technologIes for Bio-Urban Waste 
Recovery, submitted by ITENE, Packaging, Transport & Logistics Research Centre, under 
the European Union Horizon 2020 Programme, within the topic Integrated system 
innovation in valorising urban biowaste. (Topic identifier: CE-SFS-25-2018), states that:  
The innovative results to be launched in the SCALIBUR project to optimise the selective 
organic collection for obtaining high-added value products such as bioplastics, biofertilizers, 
biopesticides and proteins for feed and food, represents a real opportunity and deed for our 
municipality. We commit to implement the project actions and participate actively as 
stakeholders. This support doesn’t mean, in any case, any financial or legal commitment 
from our side.  
Hereby, we are committed to assume the role of Pilot municipality. The main tasks to carry 
out as Pilot are:  
1. To participate actively in the co-design meetings to develop SCALIBURs’ waste 
management improvements. 
2. To implement the best practices identified regarding to the bio-waste collection in the 
municipality.  
3. To provide information and data about bio-waste managements and the tools from the 
Platform. 
4. To involve relevant stakeholders of the organic waste chain in the co-design of the 
waste management plans. 
5. To be involved in the workshops and awareness campaigns of the municipality. 
6. To promote and disseminate SCALIBUR’s results to other interested actors. 
 
Yours sincerely,  
Dal Prete Andrea,  
Mayor of the Municipality of Polpenazze d/G
